# CHUNK 1: Definiciones Fundacionales + Modelo de Usuario
## Growth Operating System — Bit2Me

**Version:** 1.0 — Chunk 1 of 4
**Date:** 2026-02-19
**Author:** Head of Growth (Daniel)
**Status:** Draft for validation by Daniel + Pablo

---

# PHASE 1: FOUNDATIONAL DEFINITIONS (The Language)

Every term below has one definition. No ambiguity. Every definition is SQL-translatable.

---

## 1.1 Primera Monetización (First Monetization) — The Decision

### Context

Pablo's exact questions (verbatim):
1. "¿Cómo se calcula?"
2. "¿Por qué se calcula así?"
3. "¿Se calcula igual en el agregado que en cada producto?"
4. "¿Se calcula igual según el canal de adquisición?"
5. "¿Hay fórmulas matemáticas para eso tb que pueden ayudar?"

S. Rut's reframe (correct): "No es primera compra lo que hay que definir, sino el momento de activación." Each product has its own activation moment and dormancy moment.

### Evaluation of 6 Candidates

#### Candidate 1: First Revenue Event (FRE)
- **Definition:** Timestamp of the first event where Bit2Me captures any revenue > €0 from a user across any product.
- **SQL:**
```sql
SELECT user_id, MIN(event_timestamp) AS fm_date
FROM revenue_events
WHERE revenue_amount > 0
GROUP BY user_id
```
- **Strengths:** Precise. Unambiguous. Directly tied to business value. Works across all products (Brokerage spread, Earn yield, Card interchange, Loan interest).
- **Weaknesses:** Treats €0.003 of Earn yield identically to a €500 Brokerage commission. Noise from dust transactions and micro-yields. A user who deposits €5 into Earn generates revenue on day 1 via yield accrual, but the amount is economically meaningless.
- **Verdict:** Too noisy without a threshold. Fails to distinguish signal from noise.

#### Candidate 2: First Completed Trade (FCT)
- **Definition:** Timestamp of first buy or sell execution on Brokerage or Pro.
- **SQL:**
```sql
SELECT user_id, MIN(trade_timestamp) AS fm_date
FROM trades
WHERE status = 'completed' AND product IN ('brokerage', 'pro')
GROUP BY user_id
```
- **Strengths:** Simple. Industry standard (Coinbase MTU uses this). Already tracked in Qlik Activation report.
- **Weaknesses:** Brokerage-only. Ignores Earn (user deposits €50K, never trades), Card (user activates and spends, never trades), Loan (user originates loan, never trades). As Bit2Me adds products, this definition becomes increasingly incomplete. It penalizes diversification.
- **Verdict:** Insufficient for a multi-product platform. Would have been correct in 2022. Not in 2026.

#### Candidate 3: First Deposit (FD)
- **Definition:** Timestamp of first fiat or crypto deposit into the Bit2Me wallet.
- **SQL:**
```sql
SELECT user_id, MIN(deposit_timestamp) AS fm_date
FROM deposits
WHERE status = 'completed' AND amount > 0
GROUP BY user_id
```
- **Strengths:** High-intent signal. Leading indicator of monetization. Simple to track.
- **Weaknesses:** Generates zero direct revenue. A user who deposits and never acts is not monetized. Conflates intent with action. Creates a misleading CAC calculation: you'd report "acquiring monetized users" who generated €0.
- **Verdict:** Excellent activation signal. Wrong FM definition. Use as funnel metric, not as FM.

#### Candidate 4: First Economically Meaningful Action (EMA) ★ RECOMMENDED
- **Definition:** First revenue-generating action by a user where the revenue exceeds a product-specific minimum threshold, across any Bit2Me product.
- **SQL:**
```sql
SELECT user_id, MIN(event_timestamp) AS fm_date, product AS fm_product
FROM (
    -- Brokerage/Pro: first trade with commission > €0.50
    SELECT user_id, trade_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'brokerage' AS product
    FROM trades
    WHERE status = 'completed'
      AND commission_eur > 0.50

    UNION ALL

    -- Earn/Staking: first deposit where projected_30d_yield > €0.50
    SELECT user_id, deposit_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'earn' AS product
    FROM earn_deposits
    WHERE status = 'completed'
      AND deposit_amount_eur * annual_yield_rate / 12 > 0.50

    UNION ALL

    -- Card: first interchange-generating transaction
    SELECT user_id, tx_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'card' AS product
    FROM card_transactions
    WHERE status = 'completed'
      AND interchange_eur > 0

    UNION ALL

    -- Loan: first loan origination
    SELECT user_id, origination_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'loan' AS product
    FROM loans
    WHERE status = 'originated'

    UNION ALL

    -- Launchpad: first participation
    SELECT user_id, participation_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'launchpad' AS product
    FROM launchpad_participations
    WHERE status = 'completed'
) all_fm_events
GROUP BY user_id
```
- **Strengths:** Cross-product. Filters noise. Revenue-aligned. Each product contributes. The threshold eliminates dust and micro-yield noise. Extensible: adding a new product means adding one UNION ALL.
- **Weaknesses:** Requires threshold calibration per product. Slightly more complex to implement than FCT. Thresholds need periodic review.
- **Verdict:** Best balance of precision, cross-product coverage, and noise filtering. This is the recommendation.

#### Candidate 5: First Value Exchange (FVE)
- **Definition:** First event where both (a) user receives tangible value AND (b) platform captures revenue.
- **SQL:** Same as EMA in practice, since any revenue-generating event also delivers user value (crypto acquired, yield earned, card used, loan received).
- **Strengths:** Philosophically elegant. Captures the bilateral nature of the exchange.
- **Weaknesses:** In practice, indistinguishable from EMA. The "user receives value" condition adds no filtering power because all revenue events inherently deliver user value. Adds conceptual complexity without operational benefit.
- **Verdict:** Collapses into EMA. Not worth the separate definition.

#### Candidate 6: First Qualified Monetization (FQM)
- **Definition:** First action with statistically significant correlation to 90-day retention, calibrated via cohort analysis.
- **SQL:** Requires ML model output. Not directly SQL-translatable without a scoring table.
- **Strengths:** Most predictive by definition. Data-driven thresholds. Self-calibrating.
- **Weaknesses:** Requires 12+ months of cohort data with sufficient volume per product. Cold start problem for new products and new geos. Black box for Pablo (he needs to explain it to the board). Circular risk: the definition changes as the data changes, making historical comparisons unreliable.
- **Verdict:** Aspirational. Target for Month 6+. Use EMA now, migrate to FQM when data supports it.

### RECOMMENDATION: EMA (First Economically Meaningful Action)

**Answer to Pablo's questions:**

**1. "¿Cómo se calcula?"**
FM = the timestamp of a user's first revenue-generating action above a product-specific minimum threshold, across ANY Bit2Me product. The system takes the earliest qualifying event across all products.

**2. "¿Por qué se calcula así?"**
Three reasons:
- It works across all products (not Brokerage-only). As Bit2Me grows its product suite, the definition grows with it.
- The threshold eliminates noise (dust trades, micro-yields, test transactions).
- It ties directly to revenue, which is what the Council cares about.

**3. "¿Se calcula igual en el agregado que en cada producto?"**

No. Two levels:

| Level | Definition | Use |
|-------|-----------|-----|
| **FM Global (usuario)** | MIN(fm_date) across all products. One per user. | CAC calculation, lifecycle stage classification, Council reporting |
| **FM por Producto** | First qualifying action within THAT specific product. One per product per user. | Product activation rates, product-specific funnels, cross-sell timing |

A user can have FM Global = Brokerage (2024-03-15) AND FM Earn = (2024-06-22). The global FM captures when they first became a monetized user. The product FM captures when they activated on each product.

**4. "¿Se calcula igual según el canal de adquisición?"**

Yes, the DEFINITION is the same regardless of channel. The THRESHOLD is the same. What changes is the ANALYSIS: you cut FM by channel to understand acquisition quality.

```sql
-- FM rate by acquisition channel
SELECT
    acquisition_channel,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN user_id END) AS fm_users,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS total_registered,
    ROUND(100.0 * COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN user_id END)
          / COUNT(DISTINCT user_id), 2) AS fm_rate_pct
FROM users u
LEFT JOIN user_fm f ON u.user_id = f.user_id
GROUP BY acquisition_channel
```

If Paid has 30% FM rate and Academy has 12% FM rate, the problem is the channel quality, not the FM definition.

**5. "¿Hay fórmulas matemáticas para eso?"**

Yes.

**Tasa de Primera Monetización (FM Rate):**
```
FM_Rate = FM_Users_period / Registered_Users_period
```

**Velocidad de Monetización (Monetization Velocity):**
```
Monetization_Velocity = MEDIAN(fm_date - registration_date) in days
```
Use median, not average. The distribution is heavily right-skewed (most FM happens in days 1-7; a long tail extends to 90+ days).

**FM Revenue Contribution:**
```
FM_Revenue = SUM(revenue) WHERE user's fm_date is within the reporting period
```

**FM Quality Score (per channel):**
```
FM_Quality = (D30_retention_of_FM_users_from_channel) × (ARPU_30d_of_FM_users_from_channel)
```
This separates channels that produce FM users who stick from channels that produce FM users who churn.

### Product-Level FM Definitions (Thresholds)

| Product | FM Event | Minimum Threshold | Rationale |
|---------|----------|-------------------|-----------|
| **Brokerage** | First completed buy or sell | Commission > €0.50 (trade ~€30+) | Filters dust trades and test buys |
| **Pro** | First completed trade (market or limit) | Fee > €0.50 | Same logic. Pro fees are lower, so volume threshold is higher |
| **Earn** | First deposit into yield product | Deposit > €50 (projected monthly yield > ~€0.50 at typical rates) | Filters €1-5 test deposits |
| **Staking** | First stake | Staked amount > €50 | Same as Earn |
| **Card** | First interchange-generating purchase | Any completed purchase | Card activation already requires intent; no minimum needed |
| **Loan** | First loan origination | Any originated loan | Loan origination requires significant collateral; self-filtering |
| **Launchpad** | First participation in token sale | Any completed participation | Participation requires B2M holding; self-filtering |
| **Referral** | First referred user reaches FM | Referred user's FM event | Per S. Rut: activation = first successful referral, not sharing a link |

### Threshold Calibration Methodology

The €0.50 revenue threshold is a starting point. Calibration process:

1. Pull distribution of first-transaction revenues for each product (histogram).
2. Identify the natural breakpoint between "noise" (test transactions, dust) and "signal" (intentional usage).
3. Validate: users above threshold should have D30 retention 2x+ higher than users below threshold.
4. Recalibrate quarterly, or when product economics change (e.g., Pro fee cut of Jan 2025 shifts the distribution).

```sql
-- Threshold validation: retention above vs below threshold
SELECT
    CASE WHEN first_trade_commission > 0.50 THEN 'above_threshold'
         ELSE 'below_threshold' END AS threshold_group,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS users,
    AVG(CASE WHEN has_activity_d30 = 1 THEN 1.0 ELSE 0.0 END) AS d30_retention
FROM user_first_trades
GROUP BY 1
```

If D30 retention is similar above and below threshold, the threshold is too low (not filtering noise). If the "below" group is tiny, the threshold might be too high (filtering real users). Target: the "below" group should be 5-15% of first-time users and have D30 retention under 10%.

### Edge Cases

| Edge Case | Resolution |
|-----------|-----------|
| **Dust transaction** (€0.10 buy from referral bonus) | Filtered by threshold. Not counted as FM. |
| **Free crypto from promotion** (sign-up bonus, airdrop) | Not counted as FM. User did not take an economically meaningful action. The promotion is a funnel step, not monetization. |
| **Card-before-trade user** | FM = Card first purchase date. Product FM Card is set. They may never have a Brokerage FM, and that's fine. |
| **Earn deposit but no trade** | FM = Earn deposit date (if above threshold). This user is monetized via yield spread even if they never touch Brokerage. |
| **User deposits fiat but never buys** | No FM. Deposit is a funnel step, not monetization. Track as "Deposited_Only" status. |
| **User receives crypto transfer (not a purchase)** | No FM. Receiving crypto generates no revenue. FM triggers only when the user takes an action that generates platform revenue. |
| **Pro fee cut to 0%** (Jan 2025 scenario) | If fee = 0, there is no revenue event. Pro trades at 0% fee do NOT count as FM. This is correct: if Bit2Me earns nothing, the user is not "monetized" from Pro. Track separately as "Pro_Active_Zero_Fee". |
| **Liquidation event on Loan** | Not counted as FM. Liquidation is a distressed event, not a user-initiated action. FM for Loans = origination only. |
| **User in multiple products simultaneously** | FM Global = earliest qualifying event across all products. Each product tracks its own FM independently. |
| **Referral bonus triggers a micro-trade** | If the trade is above threshold, it counts. If below, it doesn't. The referral bonus itself is not FM. |

### Anti-Gaming Safeguards

| Risk | Safeguard |
|------|-----------|
| Wash trading for FM attribution | Flag users with buy-then-immediate-sell within 60 seconds. Exclude from FM if spread < threshold. |
| Bot accounts | KYC requirement is the primary gate. Secondary: flag accounts with >10 trades in first 5 minutes. |
| Referral gaming (self-referral loops) | Flag referral chains where referred users share IP, device fingerprint, or complete FM within 2 minutes of registration. |
| Affiliate fraud | Cross-reference FM timestamp with affiliate click timestamp. Exclude if FM occurs within 60 seconds of registration (pre-loaded bot). |

### Cascade Effects

FM definition directly determines:

| Downstream Metric | How FM Affects It |
|-------------------|-------------------|
| **CAC** | CAC = Spend / FM_Users. Wrong FM definition = wrong CAC. |
| **LTV** | LTV calculation starts at FM date. Wrong FM = wrong lifetime measurement. |
| **Activation Rate** | Activation = FM_Users / Registered_Users. Denominator is fixed; numerator depends entirely on FM definition. |
| **FM vs LC Revenue Split** | Every user's revenue is classified as FM or LC based on their FM date. |
| **Lifecycle Stage** | FM event triggers transition from KYC_COMPLETE/DEPOSITED_ONLY to FIRST_MONETIZATION stage. |
| **Council reporting** | Pablo sees "X new monetized users this week." The number comes directly from FM definition. |

---

## 1.2 Definiciones de Estado de Usuario (User Status Definitions)

MECE: Mutually Exclusive, Collectively Exhaustive. Every user falls into exactly one status at any point in time.

### Status Definitions

```sql
-- Master user status classifier
-- Run daily. Produces one row per user with current status.
-- Statuses are evaluated in priority order (first match wins).

SELECT
    user_id,
    CASE
        -- CHURNED: gone. Zero balance, no activity 180d, no login 180d.
        WHEN days_since_last_activity > 180
             AND total_balance_eur = 0
             AND days_since_last_login > 180
        THEN 'CHURNED'

        -- DORMANT_ZERO: no balance, inactive 90d but < 180d or has logged in.
        WHEN days_since_last_activity > 90
             AND total_balance_eur = 0
             AND NOT (days_since_last_activity > 180
                      AND days_since_last_login > 180)
        THEN 'DORMANT_ZERO'

        -- DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE: inactive 90d but has money on platform.
        WHEN days_since_last_activity > 90
             AND total_balance_eur > 0
        THEN 'DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE'

        -- AT_RISK: was active, now declining rapidly.
        WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
             AND days_since_last_activity <= 90
             AND (
                 activity_decline_4w_pct >= 50
                 OR health_score < 30
                 OR (had_active_dca AND dca_cancelled_recently)
             )
        THEN 'AT_RISK'

        -- ACTIVE: monetized and engaged within product-appropriate window.
        -- See Section 1.3 for full definition.
        WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
             AND days_since_fm > 30
             AND is_economically_active = TRUE
        THEN 'ACTIVE'

        -- FIRST_MONETIZATION: recently had FM event, within 30-day window.
        WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
             AND days_since_fm <= 30
        THEN 'FIRST_MONETIZATION'

        -- DEPOSITED_ONLY: has deposited fiat or crypto but never reached FM.
        WHEN total_deposits > 0
             AND fm_date IS NULL
        THEN 'DEPOSITED_ONLY'

        -- KYC_COMPLETE: verified but no deposits, no trades.
        WHEN kyc_status = 'approved'
             AND total_deposits = 0
             AND fm_date IS NULL
        THEN 'KYC_COMPLETE'

        -- REGISTERED_ONLY: account exists, KYC not complete.
        WHEN has_account = TRUE
             AND kyc_status != 'approved'
        THEN 'REGISTERED_ONLY'

        ELSE 'UNCLASSIFIED'
    END AS user_status,

    -- Timestamp of status evaluation
    CURRENT_DATE() AS snapshot_date

FROM user_master_table
```

### Detailed Status Specifications

| Status | Nombre Español | SQL Conditions | Population Est. (Spain) | Revenue Contribution | Notes |
|--------|---------------|----------------|------------------------|---------------------|-------|
| REGISTERED_ONLY | Solo Registrado | has_account AND kyc != approved | ~213,863 (49.1%) | €0 | Largest bucket. 49% of base. KYC funnel optimization target. |
| KYC_COMPLETE | Verificado Sin Actividad | kyc = approved AND deposits = 0 AND fm IS NULL | ~29,010 (6.7%) | €0 | High-intent: completed KYC but stopped. Likely friction at deposit step. |
| DEPOSITED_ONLY | Depósito Sin Compra | deposits > 0 AND fm IS NULL | REQUIRES DATA | €0 (direct). Generates float revenue if holding EUR. | Critical drop-off. User deposited money and did nothing. Highest-ROI nudge target. Maps to P0 event "Deposit_No_Purchase". |
| FIRST_MONETIZATION | Primera Monetización | fm_date NOT NULL AND days_since_fm <= 30 | Part of L2 (~36,866) | FM Revenue | 30-day window. After 30 days, transitions to ACTIVE or AT_RISK based on behavior. |
| ACTIVE | Activo | See Section 1.3 | ~50,416 (11.6%) | Primary revenue engine (FM + LC transactional + recurring) | Multi-product definition. Solves passive revenue problem. |
| AT_RISK | En Riesgo | Was active + 50% activity decline 4w OR health_score < 30 OR DCA cancelled | REQUIRES DATA | Declining. Revenue trajectory negative. | Early warning. Trigger point for retention campaigns. DCA cancellation is a strong signal here. |
| DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE | Dormido Con Saldo | days_since_activity > 90 AND balance > 0 | ~4,414 (1.0%) | Recurring only (Earn yield, Staking rewards if applicable) | 5-10x higher reactivation probability vs zero-balance. These users still trust the platform (money is here). May be generating passive revenue. |
| DORMANT_ZERO | Dormido Sin Saldo | days_since_activity > 90 AND balance = 0 AND NOT churned | REQUIRES DATA | €0 | Harder to reactivate. No financial commitment remaining. |
| CHURNED | Perdido | days_since_activity > 180 AND balance = 0 AND days_since_login > 180 | ~101,029 (23.2%) | €0 | Write-off for operational purposes. Still reachable via email/push for reactivation campaigns at low cost. |

### Edge Cases in Status Classification

| Edge Case | Resolution |
|-----------|-----------|
| User registered yesterday, KYC pending | REGISTERED_ONLY. Status updates when KYC resolves. |
| User completed KYC 2 years ago, never deposited | KYC_COMPLETE. Not DORMANT (never was active). |
| User had FM 31 days ago but no second action | Depends on is_economically_active flag. If generating recurring revenue (Earn), → ACTIVE. If not, → AT_RISK. |
| User is ACTIVE on Earn (€50K deposited) but has not logged in for 60 days | ACTIVE. The passive revenue definition (Section 1.3) handles this. Login is NOT required for ACTIVE status. |
| User withdrew all balance yesterday after being active for 6 months | Still ACTIVE (days_since_last_activity = 1). Will transition to AT_RISK within 1-2 weeks as health_score drops. Then DORMANT_ZERO after 90 days. |
| B2B corporate account | Classified using same logic but flagged with segment = 'B2B'. B2B has different lifecycle model (Phase 3, Chunk 2). |
| User reactivates after 180 days of inactivity | Moves from CHURNED back to ACTIVE (or FIRST_MONETIZATION if the reactivation event is treated as a "new" FM for that product). Track as reactivated cohort separately. |

### Mapping to Existing L0-L5 System

| Current Label | New Status | Difference |
|---------------|-----------|------------|
| L0 (Unverified) | REGISTERED_ONLY | Identical |
| L1 (Verified, no monetization) | KYC_COMPLETE + DEPOSITED_ONLY | Split into two: with/without deposit. Deposit signals intent. |
| L2 (First monetization, no retention) | FIRST_MONETIZATION | Narrowed to 30-day window post-FM |
| L3 (Active with value) | ACTIVE | Expanded: multi-product definition, includes passive revenue |
| L4 (Dormant with value) | DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE | Identical in concept. Adds 90-day threshold. |
| L5 (Churned) | CHURNED + DORMANT_ZERO | Split into two: with zero balance (two different windows) |
| (new) | AT_RISK | Did not exist. Inserted between ACTIVE and DORMANT. |

**Sync with Salvia's segments:** The status classification above is the GLOBAL user status. Salvia's per-product clusters (Brokerage C0-C9, etc.) operate at the product level and overlay on top of this global status. A user can be globally ACTIVE but in Brokerage cluster C3 ("Descartados"). This is not a conflict; it means they're active on OTHER products. The unified cluster table (`user_id, brokerage_cluster, pro_cluster, earn_cluster...`) is the bridge.

---

## 1.3 Definición de "Activo" (The "Active" Definition)

### The Problem

In crypto, "active" ≠ "logged in" or "traded recently."

| User | Behavior | Monthly Revenue for Bit2Me | Traditional Classification | Correct Classification |
|------|----------|---------------------------|--------------------------|----------------------|
| User A | Trades €500/month on Brokerage | ~€7.50 (1.5% spread) | Active | Active (Behaviorally + Economically) |
| User B | €50K in Earn, never logs in | ~€200/month yield spread | Inactive (no login) | Active (Economically) |
| User C | Uses Card 20x/month, never trades | ~€4 interchange | Inactive (no trades) | Active (Behaviorally + Economically) |
| User D | Logs in 15x/month, checks prices, trades zero | €0 | Active (logins) | NOT Active (no revenue) |
| User E | DCA €50/week BTC, never logs in manually | ~€3/month commission | Inactive (no manual login) | Active (Economically, DCA-driven) |

User B generates 27x more revenue than User A. Classifying User B as "inactive" is a business-critical error.

### Solution: Two-Layer Active Definition

#### Layer 1: Económicamente Activo (Economically Active) — THE PRIMARY METRIC

```sql
-- Economically Active: user generates revenue for Bit2Me within the measurement window.
-- This is the number that goes to Council. This is MMU.

is_economically_active = (
    -- Transactional revenue in last 30 days
    brokerage_revenue_30d > 0
    OR pro_revenue_30d > 0
    OR otc_revenue_30d > 0

    -- Recurring revenue: active positions generating yield/interest
    OR earn_balance_eur > 0  -- Earn generates daily yield spread
    OR staking_balance_eur > 0  -- Staking generates protocol rewards
    OR active_loan_count > 0  -- Loans generate interest

    -- Card: interchange in last 30 days
    OR card_interchange_30d > 0

    -- DCA: has active recurring buy
    OR has_active_dca = TRUE

    -- Launchpad: participated in last 90 days (event-driven, longer window)
    OR days_since_last_launchpad <= 90
)
```

**Usuarios Monetizados Mensuales (MMU / Monthly Monetized Users):**
```
MMU = COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) WHERE is_economically_active = TRUE
      measured on the last day of the calendar month
```

This is the proposed North Star metric for Council. It counts every user generating revenue for Bit2Me, regardless of HOW they generate it.

**Comparison to Coinbase's MTU:** Coinbase reports Monthly Transacting Users (users who made at least one transaction). Bit2Me's MMU is broader: it includes transacting users AND users with passive revenue positions. MMU ≥ MTU by definition. This is intentional. Bit2Me has more revenue sources than pure trading; the metric should reflect that.

#### Layer 2: Conductualmente Activo (Behaviorally Active) — DIAGNOSTIC METRIC

```sql
-- Behaviorally Active: user engaged with the platform (regardless of revenue).
-- Used for engagement analysis, NOT for Council reporting.

is_behaviorally_active = (
    days_since_last_login <= 30
    OR days_since_last_app_open <= 30
    OR days_since_last_price_check <= 30
)
```

This metric captures users who interact with the platform but generate no revenue (User D above). It matters for:
- Engagement tracking (are users coming back to look?)
- Conversion potential (behaviorally active + not economically active = cross-sell opportunity)
- App health (if behavioral activity drops, something is broken in the product)

But it does NOT go to Council. Pablo cares about revenue, not logins.

#### The 2x2 Matrix

| | Economically Active | NOT Economically Active |
|---|---|---|
| **Behaviorally Active** | CORE ACTIVE. Trading, using products, logging in. Ideal state. | ENGAGED BUT UNCONVERTED. Browsers, price-checkers. Cross-sell targets. |
| **NOT Behaviorally Active** | SILENT REVENUE. Earn whales, stakers, DCA users. Do NOT disturb. | DORMANT or CHURNED. No revenue, no engagement. Reactivation or write-off. |

The "Silent Revenue" quadrant is the key insight. These users (Earn depositors, stakers with auto-compounding) are generating revenue but never trigger login events. Traditional lifecycle tools (CleverTap session-based) miss them entirely. They must be classified from the balance/position data, not from event streams.

**Operational rule:** NEVER send "we miss you" or reactivation messages to Silent Revenue users. They are active. They are generating revenue. Disturbing them risks triggering a withdrawal.

### MMU Estimation (Spain, Current)

| Component | Estimated Users | Revenue Type |
|-----------|----------------|--------------|
| Brokerage/Pro active traders (30d) | ~35,000-40,000 | Transactional |
| Earn depositors with balance > €0 | REQUIRES DATA (subset of 85K with balance) | Recurring |
| Active Card users (30d) | ~4,600 annual active / ~2,000-3,000 monthly | Recurring |
| Loan holders (active loans) | REQUIRES DATA | Recurring |
| Staking positions | REQUIRES DATA | Recurring |
| DCA users (active recurring buys) | REQUIRES DATA | Transactional (recurring cadence) |
| **Total MMU estimate** | **REQUIRES DATA for precise number. Expected: 50,000-65,000** | Mixed |

Note: MMU > L3 (50,416) because L3 may not fully capture passive revenue users. The delta between MMU and L3 is the "Silent Revenue" population. Quantifying this delta is a P0 data task.

---

## 1.4 Definiciones de Churn (Churn Definitions)

### Three Horizons

| Horizonte | Nombre Español | Definition | SQL Logic | Action |
|-----------|---------------|-----------|-----------|--------|
| **Soft Churn (30d)** | Churn Suave | No monetizable action in 30 days (no trade, no deposit into Earn, no Card use, no DCA execution, no login). Positions (Earn balance, Stakes) do NOT reset this clock. | `days_since_last_monetizable_action > 30 AND NOT is_economically_active_passive_only` | Trigger AT_RISK status. Start retention sequence. This is an EARLY WARNING, not a churn declaration. |
| **Hard Churn (90d)** | Churn Firme | No monetizable action in 90 days AND no login in 60 days. | `days_since_last_monetizable_action > 90 AND days_since_last_login > 60` | Primary churn metric for Council reporting. User is dormant. Separate into with-balance and zero-balance. |
| **Dead (180d)** | Perdido | No activity 180 days, zero balance, no login 180 days. | `days_since_last_activity > 180 AND total_balance_eur = 0 AND days_since_last_login > 180` | Write-off. Low-cost reactivation only (email batch). Do not spend push/SMS budget. |

### The "Monetizable Action" Clock

```sql
-- What resets the churn clock (counted as "activity"):
last_monetizable_action_date = GREATEST(
    last_trade_date,           -- Brokerage/Pro trade
    last_earn_deposit_date,    -- New Earn deposit (not yield accrual)
    last_card_transaction_date,-- Card purchase
    last_loan_origination_date,-- New loan
    last_stake_date,           -- New staking action
    last_dca_execution_date,   -- DCA auto-buy executed
    last_launchpad_date,       -- Launchpad participation
    last_deposit_date          -- Fiat/crypto deposit
)

-- What does NOT reset the clock:
-- Passive yield accrual (Earn interest, Staking rewards)
-- Login without action
-- Price checks
-- Portfolio views
-- Push notification opens without action
```

**Why passive yield does NOT reset the clock:** A user with €50K in Earn who never logs in is Economically Active (generating revenue) but may be drifting toward platform abandonment. The Earn balance alone keeps them in ACTIVE status (via MMU). But the CHURN clock should still tick, because we want to detect the TRANSITION from "active depositor who occasionally adds more" to "set-and-forget depositor who might withdraw when rates change." The distinction matters for intervention timing.

### Market-Cycle Adjustment

**The question:** Should churn windows adjust based on market conditions?

**Answer: No fixed adjustment. Use a modifier flag instead.**

Rationale for NOT adjusting windows:
1. Changing the window changes the denominator, making period-over-period comparisons impossible.
2. "Bear market" is a judgment call; there's no clean binary cutoff.
3. The Council needs consistent definitions to track trends across cycles.

Rationale for context flag:
1. A user inactive 90 days during a 70% drawdown IS different from 90 days during a bull run.
2. Without context, you'd over-invest in reactivation campaigns during bear markets (users aren't gone; they're waiting).

**Solution: Fixed windows + Market Context Flag**

```sql
-- Market condition at the time of churn evaluation
market_condition = CASE
    WHEN btc_30d_return > 0.15 AND btc_90d_volatility > 0.6 THEN 'BULL'
    WHEN btc_30d_return < -0.15 THEN 'BEAR'
    ELSE 'NEUTRAL'
END

-- Churn with context
SELECT
    user_id,
    churn_horizon,  -- 'soft_30d', 'hard_90d', 'dead_180d'
    market_condition_at_churn,
    CASE
        WHEN churn_horizon = 'hard_90d' AND market_condition_at_churn = 'BEAR'
        THEN 'MARKET_DORMANT'  -- Likely to return when market recovers
        WHEN churn_horizon = 'hard_90d' AND market_condition_at_churn = 'BULL'
        THEN 'TRUE_CHURN'  -- Left during good times = genuine churn
        ELSE churn_horizon
    END AS churn_type
FROM churned_users
```

**Behavioral evidence supporting this approach:**
- Crypto D30 retention: ~18% in bull markets, ~2-3% in bear markets (6x swing).
- Users who "churn" during bear markets reactivate at 3-5x the rate of bull-market churners when the next cycle begins.
- Balance is the strongest predictor: users who leave balance on-platform during bear markets reactivate at 40-60% rate vs. 5-10% for zero-balance.

### Churn by Product (Different Windows)

| Product | Soft Churn Window | Hard Churn Window | Rationale |
|---------|------------------|-------------------|-----------|
| **Brokerage** | 21 days | 60 days | Trading is frequent-cadence. 21 days without a trade is unusual for an active trader. |
| **Pro** | 14 days | 45 days | Pro traders are higher frequency. Inactivity is a faster signal. |
| **Earn** | 60 days (no new deposit, AND yield withdrawn) | 120 days | Earn is passive by design. Only flag if user stops adding AND starts withdrawing. |
| **Card** | 30 days (no transaction) | 90 days | Card usage is episodic. Monthly check is appropriate. 29% monthly churn is the current baseline. |
| **Loan** | N/A (loan is active until repaid) | Loan fully repaid + 90 days no new loan | Loan lifecycle is tied to loan term, not calendar time. |
| **Staking** | 60 days (no new stake, AND unstaking initiated) | 120 days | Similar to Earn. Unstaking + unbonding period = strong churn signal. |
| **DCA** | DCA cancelled or paused | DCA cancelled + 30 days no manual trade | DCA cancellation is one of the strongest churn signals for mass retail users. |

### Churn Prediction Signals (Ranked by Expected Predictive Power)

| Rank | Signal | Type | Data Source | Expected Predictive Power |
|------|--------|------|------------|--------------------------|
| 1 | Days since last transaction | Behavioral | Transaction table | Very High. Direct measure of disengagement. |
| 2 | DCA cancellation/pause | Behavioral | Recurring orders table | Very High. Deliberate decision to stop. |
| 3 | Trading frequency decline WoW (% change) | Behavioral | Transaction table | High. Gradient matters more than absolute level. |
| 4 | Portfolio balance trajectory (7d rolling) | Financial | Balance snapshots | High. Withdrawals signal exit intent. |
| 5 | Deposit/withdrawal ratio (30d) | Financial | Deposit/withdrawal tables | High. Ratio < 1.0 = net outflow. |
| 6 | Products used count (current vs peak) | Behavioral | Cross-product table | High. Product density drop = disengagement. |
| 7 | Market condition (BTC 30d return) | External | Market data API | Medium-High. Explains macro-driven dormancy. |
| 8 | Staking/Earn balance change (30d) | Financial | Position tables | Medium. Reductions signal waning commitment. |
| 9 | Support ticket frequency | Behavioral | CRM/support | Medium. Spike may signal frustration (or engagement). Requires context. |
| 10 | Login frequency decline | Behavioral | CleverTap sessions | Medium. Lagging indicator (people stop logging in AFTER deciding to leave). |
| 11 | Push notification engagement decline | Behavioral | CleverTap | Low-Medium. Open rate drop is a weak signal. |
| 12 | Space Center tier (higher tier = lower churn) | Structural | Space Center data | Low-Medium. Sunk cost effect. Directional, not predictive alone. |

---

## 1.5 Taxonomía de Tipos de Ingreso (Revenue Type Taxonomy)

### Five Revenue Types

| Tipo | Nombre Español | Definition | Products | Market Sensitivity | Forecasting Reliability |
|------|---------------|-----------|----------|-------------------|------------------------|
| **FM Revenue** | Ingreso de Primera Monetización | Revenue from users whose FM event occurs within the reporting period. | All products | High (new user volume is market-driven) | Medium (can forecast from registration pipeline) |
| **LC Revenue** | Ingreso de Ciclo de Vida | Revenue from users whose FM occurred BEFORE the reporting period. | All products | Medium-High (existing users also react to market) | Higher (known population, measurable trends) |
| **Transactional Revenue** | Ingreso Transaccional | Revenue generated per discrete user action. Exists only when user acts. | Brokerage (spread), Pro (maker/taker fees), OTC (spread), Commerce (gateway fees) | Very High. Volume and frequency correlate directly with market sentiment. | Low in bear markets. Revenue can drop 60-80% in drawdowns. |
| **Recurring Revenue** | Ingreso Recurrente | Revenue generated continuously from user positions, without requiring user action. | Earn (yield spread), Staking (commission on rewards), Loans (interest), Card (interchange from repeat usage) | Low-Medium. Position sizes may shrink in bear markets but revenue doesn't go to zero. Counter-cyclical for stablecoins in Earn. | High. Predictable from AUC (Assets Under Custody) and rate spreads. |
| **Event Revenue** | Ingreso por Evento | Revenue from discrete, non-recurring events. | Launchpad (participation fees), Loan liquidations, Tax (seasonal) | High. Launchpad depends on market FOMO. Liquidations spike during crashes. | Very Low. Cannot reliably forecast. Budget as €0, treat as upside. |

### Why FM vs LC Matters

```
Total Revenue = FM Revenue + LC Revenue

FM Revenue tells you: "Is our acquisition machine working? Are new users monetizing?"
LC Revenue tells you: "Is our retention machine working? Are existing users generating value?"
```

If FM Revenue is growing but LC Revenue is flat: you're acquiring users but they're not sticking. Growth is unsustainable.
If LC Revenue is growing but FM Revenue is flat: existing users are healthy but the top of funnel is broken. Growth will stall.

**Critical insight for Bit2Me:** The current attribution data shows FM = €486K vs LC = €11.6M (all-time). LC is 24x FM. This means Bit2Me's revenue is overwhelmingly driven by existing users. The risk: if the existing user base starts to churn and acquisition doesn't compensate, revenue collapses. This ratio needs weekly monitoring.

```sql
-- FM vs LC revenue split for any period
SELECT
    reporting_period,
    SUM(CASE WHEN u.fm_date BETWEEN period_start AND period_end
             THEN r.revenue ELSE 0 END) AS fm_revenue,
    SUM(CASE WHEN u.fm_date < period_start
             THEN r.revenue ELSE 0 END) AS lc_revenue,
    SUM(r.revenue) AS total_revenue,
    ROUND(100.0 * SUM(CASE WHEN u.fm_date BETWEEN period_start AND period_end
             THEN r.revenue ELSE 0 END) / NULLIF(SUM(r.revenue), 0), 2) AS fm_pct
FROM revenue r
JOIN user_fm u ON r.user_id = u.user_id
GROUP BY reporting_period
```

### Why Transactional vs Recurring Matters

| Dimension | Transactional | Recurring |
|-----------|--------------|-----------|
| Revenue in a bear market crash | Drops 60-80% | Drops 10-30% (positions shrink but don't disappear) |
| Revenue when user stops logging in | Goes to €0 | Continues (Earn, Staking, Loans) |
| Forecasting | Requires volume prediction | Requires AUC/position tracking |
| Valuation impact | Discounted at higher rate (volatile) | Valued at premium (predictable) |
| Strategic implication | Grow via more users, more trades | Grow via AUC, deeper positions |

**Bit2Me strategic read:** The shift from Brokerage-heavy (transactional) to Earn/Staking/Loan (recurring) is a positive valuation signal. Track the Recurring Revenue Ratio:

```
Recurring_Revenue_Ratio = Recurring_Revenue / Total_Revenue
```

Target: 30%+ recurring by end of 2026. Current: REQUIRES DATA.

### Bull vs Bear Revenue Behavior by Type

| Revenue Type | Bull Market | Neutral | Bear Market |
|-------------|------------|---------|-------------|
| FM Revenue | High (new users flood in, FOMO) | Moderate | Low (few new users) |
| LC Transactional | Very High (volume spikes) | Moderate | Very Low |
| LC Recurring | Growing (users deposit more into Earn/Staking) | Stable | Most resilient. Stablecoin Earn may actually GROW as users de-risk into USDT/USDC. |
| Event Revenue | Launchpad booms; few liquidations | Moderate | Liquidations spike; Launchpad dies |

---

## 1.6 Definiciones de Activación y Dormancia por Producto (Activation & Dormancy per Product)

Per S. Rut's framework: each product needs TWO definitions. The activation moment (when the user is "activated") and the dormancy moment (when the user becomes "dormant"). This enables precise campaign timing: impact users BETWEEN activation and dormancy.

### Master Table

| Product | Momento de Activación | "Aha Moment" (behavior after which retention improves) | Activation Window | Momento de Dormancia | Dormancy Window | Industry Activation Rate Benchmark |
|---------|----------------------|-------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|---------------------|-----------------|-----------------------------------|
| **Brokerage** | First trade ≥ threshold + second trade within 14 days | Seeing portfolio value increase after first buy. The emotional reward of "I own crypto now." | 14 days from first trade | No trade for 21+ days (AND no DCA active) | 21 days | 40-50% of registered users reach first trade (Coinbase) |
| **Pro** | First limit order executed OR 3+ market orders within 7 days | Executing a profitable limit order. The sense of "I traded smart." | 7 days from first Pro trade | No Pro trade for 14+ days | 14 days | REQUIRES DATA. Pro is self-selecting; activation rate among Pro visitors is the metric. |
| **Earn** | First deposit into yield product ≥ €50 | Seeing first yield accrual in portfolio (even €0.01). The moment passive income becomes tangible. | 30 days from Earn page first visit | No new deposits in 60 days AND partial or full withdrawal initiated | 60 days + withdrawal | ~15-25% of active users use staking/earn products (Kraken benchmark) |
| **Staking** | First stake ≥ €50 + seeing first reward | First protocol reward received and visible in wallet. | 30 days (includes unbonding awareness) | Unstaking initiated + no new stake in 60 days | 60 days + unstaking | Similar to Earn. ~10-20% of active users. |
| **Card** | Card activated + 3rd purchase within 30 days | Seeing B2M cashback appear after a real purchase. The "free money" moment. | 30 days from card activation | No card transaction for 30+ days | 30 days | Current penetration: 0.26% (vs 42-48% industry). Massive gap. |
| **Loan** | Loan originated | Receiving EUR in bank account without selling crypto. The "I kept my BTC AND got cash" moment. | 7 days from loan simulation start to origination | Loan fully repaid + no new loan in 90 days | 90 days post-repayment | REQUIRES DATA. Loan is high-bar; activation rate among loan simulators is the metric. |
| **Launchpad** | First participation completed | Receiving token allocation. The exclusive access feeling. | Per event (7 days from event open to close) | No participation in 2+ consecutive events | Event-driven, ~90 days | REQUIRES DATA. Depends on event frequency. |
| **Referral** | First referred user reaches FM | Seeing referral bonus credited. The "I earned by sharing" moment. | 30 days from first share/invite | No new referral activity in 60 days | 60 days | Coinbase: >10% of users refer. Bit2Me: REQUIRES DATA. |
| **DCA** | First recurring buy set up + first execution completed | Second automatic execution. The user sees the system works without intervention. | 14 days from DCA setup | DCA paused or cancelled | Immediate (cancellation is a discrete event) | REQUIRES DATA. DCA setup rate should be a P0 tracked metric. |

### Time-to-Activation Quality

Not all "activated" users are equal. A user who activates in 2 days signals different quality than one who activates in 28 days.

```sql
-- Time-to-activation distribution per product
SELECT
    product,
    PERCENTILE_CONT(0.25) WITHIN GROUP (ORDER BY days_to_activation) AS p25,
    PERCENTILE_CONT(0.50) WITHIN GROUP (ORDER BY days_to_activation) AS median,
    PERCENTILE_CONT(0.75) WITHIN GROUP (ORDER BY days_to_activation) AS p75,
    AVG(days_to_activation) AS mean
FROM product_activations
GROUP BY product
```

**Activation speed tiers:**

| Tier | Time to Activation | Expected D90 Retention | Action |
|------|-------------------|----------------------|--------|
| Fast | ≤ 3 days | Highest | These users have high intent. Cross-sell early. |
| Normal | 4-14 days | Moderate | Standard lifecycle flow. |
| Slow | 15-30 days | Lower | May need additional nudges. Investigate friction. |
| Stalled | > 30 days, still not activated | Very Low | Probably won't activate without intervention. High-priority nudge or write-off. |

### Dormancy Detection SQL

```sql
-- Per-product dormancy flag (run daily)
SELECT
    user_id,
    'brokerage' AS product,
    CASE
        WHEN days_since_last_brokerage_trade > 21
             AND has_active_dca = FALSE
        THEN TRUE ELSE FALSE
    END AS is_dormant_brokerage,
    days_since_last_brokerage_trade AS days_dormant

FROM user_product_activity

UNION ALL

SELECT
    user_id,
    'earn' AS product,
    CASE
        WHEN days_since_last_earn_deposit > 60
             AND has_earn_withdrawal_30d = TRUE
        THEN TRUE ELSE FALSE
    END AS is_dormant_earn,
    days_since_last_earn_deposit AS days_dormant

FROM user_product_activity

-- ... repeat for each product
```

---

## 1.7 Lista de Dimensiones Canónicas (Canonical Dimensions)

Every metric in the system must be sliceable by these dimensions. If a metric cannot be cut by a dimension, it must be explicitly noted as "N/A" for that dimension, not silently omitted.

| # | Dimensión | Nombre Inglés | Values | Granularity | Source |
|---|-----------|--------------|--------|-------------|--------|
| 1 | **Tiempo** | Time | Week, Month, Quarter, YTD | WoW delta, MoM delta always calculated | All sources (timestamp on every event) |
| 2 | **Geografía** | Geography | ES, PT, IT, FR, DE, NL, AR, PE, RoW | Country level. Region groupings: Iberia (ES+PT), Core EU (IT+FR+DE+NL), LATAM (AR+PE), RoW | Qlik Geo Report, user registration country |
| 3 | **Segmento** | Segment | B2C, B2B | Binary. Mutually exclusive. | Qlik User Segment report |
| 4 | **Canal** | Channel | Paid, Organic, Referral, Partners, CRM, Direct, AI, Academy | Per Transaction Attribution definitions | Qlik Transaction Attribution |
| 5 | **Sub-canal** | Sub-channel | Google Search Brand, Google Search Non-Brand, Meta, Display, Affiliates, Referral Program, Academy Web, Academy App, Push, Email, In-App, SMS | One level below Channel | Qlik Transaction Attribution + CleverTap |
| 6 | **Producto** | Product | Brokerage, Pro, Earn, Staking, Card, Loan, OTC, API, Launchpad, Commerce, Tax, Travel | All 13 products. Some metrics only apply to subset. | Qlik Revenue per Product |
| 7 | **Tipo de Ingreso** | Revenue Type | FM, LC | Binary per user per period. | Derived from FM date vs. period |
| 8 | **Naturaleza del Ingreso** | Revenue Nature | Transactional, Recurring, Event | Per product (see Section 1.5). | Derived from product mapping |
| 9 | **Cohorte** | Cohort | Registration cohort (YYYY-MM), FM cohort (YYYY-MM), Revenue cohort (YYYY-Qn), Channel cohort | Multiple cohort types. Always specify which. | Derived from user dates |
| 10 | **Etapa de Ciclo de Vida** | Lifecycle Stage | REGISTERED_ONLY, KYC_COMPLETE, DEPOSITED_ONLY, FIRST_MONETIZATION, ACTIVE, AT_RISK, DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE, DORMANT_ZERO, CHURNED | Per Section 1.2. Mutually exclusive. | BigQuery user_lifecycle_stage view (P0) |
| 11 | **Arquetipo** | Archetype | See Phase 2 (12+ archetypes) | One per user (primary). Some users may have secondary. | BigQuery archetype classifier (rules-based) |
| 12 | **Condición de Mercado** | Market Condition | BULL, NEUTRAL, BEAR | Derived from BTC 30d return + volatility. Updated weekly. | Market data API |
| 13 | **Tier Space Center** | Space Center Tier | Tier 0, Tier 1, Tier 2, Tier 3, Tier 4, Tier 5 | At time of action. Can change over time. | Space Center data |
| 14 | **Densidad de Producto** | Product Density | 1, 2, 3, 4+ products used | Count of distinct products where user has FM. | Derived from cross-product table |
| 15 | **DCA Status** | DCA Status | No DCA, DCA Active, DCA Paused, DCA Cancelled | Current state of recurring buy. | Recurring orders table |

### Dimension Validation Rule

Before any metric is published, verify:
```
For each metric M:
  For each dimension D in canonical list:
    Either M can be sliced by D
    OR document why M × D is N/A
```

---

# PHASE 2: USER MODEL (Who Are We Serving?)

---

## 2.1 Catálogo de Arquetipos de Usuario (User Archetypes)

12 archetypes defined below. Each with all 10 required fields.

---

### Archetype 1: Novato Curioso (Curious Novice)

**1. Description:** First-time crypto buyer. Entered through news, social media, or peer conversation. Has little understanding of blockchain, wallets, or market dynamics. Deposits a small amount to "try it." High emotional sensitivity to first experience.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 25-40
- Income: €20K-€40K/year
- Geography: Spain (primary), new EU markets
- Tech literacy: Medium. Uses banking apps. Not comfortable with advanced trading interfaces.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Curiosity, FOMO avoidance, peer validation
- Risk tolerance: Low. Panics at -10% portfolio drop.
- Information: Social media (Twitter/X, YouTube), mainstream news. Does not read whitepapers.

**4. Primary motivation:** "Everyone is talking about crypto. I don't want to miss out." Or: "I want to understand what this is before committing real money."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Brokerage (simple buy BTC/ETH)
- Secondary: Academy (learning), DCA (if guided)
- Aspirational: Earn (once comfortable), Card (once committed)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-3: Registration, KYC, first small buy (€50-€200)
- Day 4-14: Checks portfolio 2-5x. May make one more small buy.
- Day 15-30: Activity drops sharply. Either makes second buy or goes silent.
- Day 31-90: 60-70% churn. Survivors either establish DCA or drift to Dormant.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €15-€80 (high churn drags down average)
- Monetization path: Single Brokerage trade → possible second trade → if DCA, jumps to €100-€300 LTV
- ARPU: €3-€8/month during active months

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: First loss (portfolio drops below purchase price), confusion about fees/spread, lack of hand-holding, competitor with simpler onboarding.
- Warning signals: No second trade within 14 days, no login after day 7, no DCA setup.
- Timeline: 70% decision point at day 14. If no second action by day 14, probability of 90-day churn > 80%.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
     AND days_since_registration <= 90
     AND total_trades <= 3
     AND total_trade_volume_eur < 500
     AND products_used = 1
     AND primary_product = 'brokerage'
THEN 'CURIOUS_NOVICE'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Enters with FOMO. Higher initial deposit (€100-€300). Still high churn but faster to second trade.
- Bear: Enters cautiously or via Academy. Lower deposit (€20-€50). Even higher churn (80%+). Survivors are higher quality (deliberate, not FOMO).

---

### Archetype 2: Inversor Millennial (Millennial Investor)

**1. Description:** 28-42 year old with existing investment portfolio (stocks, ETFs, real estate). Sees crypto as portfolio diversification. Methodical. Compares platforms before committing. Values regulation and security.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 28-42
- Income: €40K-€80K/year
- Geography: Spain, new EU (DE, FR, NL)
- Tech literacy: High. Uses multiple financial apps (Degiro, Trade Republic, etc.).

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Long-term wealth building, diversification, institutional credibility
- Risk tolerance: Medium. Accepts -20% drawdowns. Allocates 5-15% of portfolio to crypto.
- Information: Financial newsletters, podcasts (Bankless, Unchained), comparison sites, Reddit r/investing.

**4. Primary motivation:** "I want 5-15% of my portfolio in crypto for diversification. I need a regulated, reliable platform."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Brokerage (BTC, ETH, top-20 assets)
- Secondary: Earn (yield on holdings), DCA (systematic buying)
- Aspirational: Pro (as confidence grows), Staking, Tax (annual reporting)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-7: Research phase. Compares 2-3 platforms. Registers, completes KYC. First deposit €300-€1,500.
- Day 7-30: First buy (BTC, ETH). Sets up DCA. Explores Earn.
- Day 30-60: Second product adoption (Earn or DCA if not already). Portfolio settles into allocation.
- Day 60-90: Steady state. Monthly DCA. Occasional manual buy on dips.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €300-€1,500 (12-month)
- Monetization path: Brokerage → DCA → Earn → (Tax seasonal)
- ARPU: €20-€60/month. Mix of transactional (DCA, manual buys) and recurring (Earn yield).

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Better fees/rates at competitor, platform reliability issues (downtime during volatility), regulatory concerns, poor UX compared to fintech standards.
- Warning signals: DCA cancellation, Earn withdrawal, comparing platforms in support chat.
- Timeline: More resilient than Novice. Churn concentrated at Month 3-6 (fee comparison phase) and Month 12+ (portfolio rebalance).

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN total_trade_volume_eur BETWEEN 500 AND 20000
     AND products_used >= 2
     AND (has_active_dca = TRUE OR earn_balance_eur > 0)
     AND primary_assets IN ('BTC', 'ETH', 'top_20')
     AND days_since_registration > 30
THEN 'MILLENNIAL_INVESTOR'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Increases DCA amount. May add new assets (SOL, ADA). Explores Pro. LTV increases 1.5-2x.
- Bear: Reduces DCA but rarely cancels. Shifts allocation to stablecoins in Earn. More defensive but stays. This is the archetype most likely to "buy the dip."

---

### Archetype 3: Refugiado DeFi (DeFi Refugee)

**1. Description:** Technically sophisticated user migrating from DEXs (Uniswap, Aave, Curve) to CEXs for convenience, security, or regulatory comfort. Understands yield farming, liquidity pools, and gas fees. Compares everything.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 22-35
- Income: Variable (often crypto-native income)
- Geography: Spain, EU (especially DE, NL)
- Tech literacy: Very High. Has used MetaMask, Ledger, multiple DeFi protocols.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Yield optimization, self-sovereignty (but pragmatic), fee efficiency
- Risk tolerance: High. Comfortable with smart contract risk. Evaluates APY across 5+ platforms.
- Information: DeFi Llama, Dune Analytics, Crypto Twitter, Discord communities.

**4. Primary motivation:** "DeFi is getting complicated/expensive/risky. I want similar yields with less effort and more security."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Earn (comparing yields), Pro (limit orders, advanced execution)
- Secondary: Staking (native protocol staking), Loan (leverage without selling)
- Aspirational: API (building own tools), Launchpad (early access)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-3: Crypto deposit (not fiat; already holds crypto). Immediately checks Earn rates and Pro fee schedule.
- Day 7-14: First Earn deposit (tests with moderate amount). First Pro trade (limit order).
- Day 14-30: If rates are competitive, deposits more. If not, withdraws and leaves.
- Day 30-90: Power user if retained. Multiple products. High volume.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €500-€5,000 (highly variable; depends on rate competitiveness)
- Monetization path: Earn/Pro → Staking → Loan → Launchpad
- ARPU: €50-€200/month. High volume, but also price-sensitive on fees.

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Better rates elsewhere (even 0.5% APY difference matters), platform limitations (missing tokens, slow withdrawals), DeFi protocol launches with high initial yields.
- Warning signals: Earn balance decreasing week over week, Pro volume declining, checking withdrawal fees.
- Timeline: Fast decision. If staying, commits by Day 30. If leaving, gone by Day 14.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN first_deposit_type = 'crypto'
     AND (earn_balance_eur > 1000 OR pro_volume_30d > 5000)
     AND total_unique_assets_traded >= 5
     AND days_to_first_action <= 3
THEN 'DEFI_REFUGEE'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Shifts to DeFi for higher yields. Bit2Me is a "safe harbor" for profits. Usage may decrease.
- Bear: Returns to CEX for stability. Earn becomes primary product. Most active during bear (counter-cyclical).

---

### Archetype 4: Refugiado de Inflación (Inflation Hedger)

**1. Description:** LATAM-specific. Uses crypto (primarily stablecoins) to protect purchasing power from local currency devaluation. Not speculating; surviving. Stablecoin-first, not BTC-first.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 25-50
- Income: Variable (middle class by local standards; €300-€1,500/month equivalent)
- Geography: Argentina, Peru, other LATAM
- Tech literacy: Medium. Uses mobile banking. Understands exchange rates.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Capital preservation, access to USD-denominated assets, remittance efficiency
- Risk tolerance: Low on crypto (doesn't want volatility), high on stablecoins (understands devaluation risk of NOT holding USD)
- Information: Local crypto influencers, WhatsApp groups, word of mouth.

**4. Primary motivation:** "My currency is losing value every month. I need to convert to USDT/USDC and earn yield on it."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Brokerage (buy USDT/USDC), Earn (yield on stablecoins)
- Secondary: Card (if available in region, for spending)
- Aspirational: Loan (borrow against stablecoin position)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-3: Registration, KYC, first fiat deposit. Immediate conversion to USDT or USDC.
- Day 3-7: Deposits into Earn (stablecoin yield). Fast activation. Urgency-driven.
- Day 7-30: Regular deposits (monthly income cycle). Pattern establishes quickly.
- Day 30-90: Steady depositor. May introduce friends/family (referral potential).

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €100-€600 (lower AUM per user, but high retention and regular deposits)
- Monetization path: Brokerage (stablecoin buy) → Earn (stablecoin yield) → Referral
- ARPU: €5-€20/month. Lower per user but highly predictable and recurring.

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Platform stability concerns (withdrawal delays), local regulatory restrictions, better stablecoin yields elsewhere, fiat on-ramp issues.
- Warning signals: Earn withdrawal, no new deposit in 45 days, fiat deposit failure.
- Timeline: Very loyal if platform works. Churn is event-driven (regulatory, platform issue), not gradual.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN registration_country IN ('AR', 'PE', 'CO', 'MX', 'VE')
     AND primary_asset_held IN ('USDT', 'USDC', 'DAI')
     AND earn_balance_stablecoin_pct > 0.7
THEN 'INFLATION_HEDGER'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Minimal change. Not speculating. May convert small % to BTC/ETH if confident.
- Bear: Increases deposits. Local currency under more pressure during global risk-off. Counter-cyclical for Bit2Me.

---

### Archetype 5: Buscador de Rendimiento (Yield Seeker)

**1. Description:** Has significant capital (€10K-€200K+). Primary interest is earning yield on assets, not trading. Compares APYs across Celsius (gone), BlockFi (gone), Nexo, Crypto.com, and now Bit2Me. Post-CeFi-crisis, values regulated platforms.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 35-55
- Income: €60K-€150K+/year
- Geography: Spain, EU
- Tech literacy: Medium-High. Financial literacy is high. Crypto literacy varies.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Yield, capital preservation, platform safety post-Celsius/BlockFi
- Risk tolerance: Medium. Comfortable with crypto yield products. Terrified of platform risk.
- Information: Yield comparison sites, CoinMarketCap Earn, Reddit r/CryptoEarn.

**4. Primary motivation:** "I want 3-8% yield on my assets without the risk of losing principal on an unregulated platform."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Earn (BTC yield, stablecoin yield)
- Secondary: Staking (ETH, SOL), Loan (leverage existing position)
- Aspirational: Pro (active management of yield positions)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-7: Registration, KYC, test deposit (€500-€2,000). Checks Earn rates.
- Day 7-30: If rates competitive, deposits more (€5K-€50K+). Monitors yield accrual daily initially.
- Day 30-60: Settles into monitoring pattern. Checks weekly, not daily. Adds to position.
- Day 60-90: Stable. Large Earn balance. Low transaction count. High revenue.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €1,000-€10,000+ (driven by AUC, not transaction count)
- Monetization path: Earn → Staking → Loan
- ARPU: €50-€500+/month (depends entirely on deposit size and rates)

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Rate reduction (even 0.5% drop triggers comparison shopping), competitor launch with promotional rates, platform security incident, regulatory change.
- Warning signals: Partial withdrawal from Earn, checking competitor rates (if trackable), support inquiry about rates.
- Timeline: Churn is a deliberate, planned event. Weeks of comparison before moving. Withdrawal happens in 1-3 large transactions, not gradually.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN earn_balance_eur > 5000
     AND earn_balance_eur / NULLIF(total_balance_eur, 0) > 0.6
     AND total_trades_30d <= 5
THEN 'YIELD_SEEKER'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: May rotate some Earn balance to active trading (FOMO). AUC in Earn may dip temporarily.
- Bear: Increases Earn deposits. Flight to yield. Most Earn AUC growth happens during bear markets.

---

### Archetype 6: Trader Profesional (Pro Trader)

**1. Description:** 5+ trades per week. Uses limit orders, stop-losses, and advanced order types. Evaluates platforms on execution speed, fee structure, and liquidity. Often uses multiple exchanges simultaneously.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 22-40
- Income: Variable (often full-time or part-time trading income)
- Geography: Spain, EU
- Tech literacy: Very High. Uses TradingView, multiple exchanges, possibly API.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Execution quality, low fees, deep order books, advanced tools
- Risk tolerance: High. Active risk management. Understands leverage.
- Information: TradingView, Crypto Twitter, order flow analysis, exchange fee comparison sites.

**4. Primary motivation:** "I need the best execution, lowest fees, and deepest liquidity for my trading strategy."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Pro (maker/taker)
- Secondary: API (for automated strategies), Loan (leverage)
- Aspirational: OTC (as volume grows)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-3: Registration, KYC, crypto deposit. First Pro trade within hours.
- Day 3-14: Testing execution quality. Running strategy on small size. Comparing to primary exchange.
- Day 14-30: Decision point. Either increases volume or leaves.
- Day 30-90: If retained, becomes high-volume. Daily trading. High fee revenue despite low fee rate.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €500-€20,000+ (volume-driven)
- Monetization path: Pro → API → Loan → OTC
- ARPU: €100-€1,000+/month (high volume × low fee rate)

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Better fees elsewhere (the Jan 2025 95% fee cut shows this is real), poor liquidity, execution latency, missing order types, API limitations.
- Warning signals: Volume decline WoW (>30% drop), API call frequency decrease, withdrawal of trading capital.
- Timeline: Fast decision maker. Leaves within 2 weeks if unsatisfied. No warning. Just stops trading.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN pro_trades_30d >= 20
     AND pro_volume_30d > 10000
     AND uses_limit_orders = TRUE
THEN 'PRO_TRADER'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Highest activity. Volume spikes 3-5x. Highest revenue per user.
- Bear: Volume drops significantly but doesn't go to zero. Shifts to short strategies if available. May move to platforms with derivatives.

---

### Archetype 7: Conservador Regulatorio (Regulation-First Conservative)

**1. Description:** Chose Bit2Me specifically because of MiCA license, Banco de España registration, and ISO certifications. Trust and safety are primary decision factors. Not interested in DeFi, meme coins, or high-risk strategies.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 40-60
- Income: €50K-€120K/year
- Geography: Spain (primary)
- Tech literacy: Medium-Low. Uses banking apps with difficulty.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Security, regulation, institutional backing (Telefónica Ventures signal), insurance coverage
- Risk tolerance: Very Low. BTC and ETH only. No altcoins. No leverage.
- Information: Mainstream financial media (Expansión, Cinco Días), bank advisor mentions, Bit2Me marketing about regulation.

**4. Primary motivation:** "I want to own Bitcoin, but only through a platform I can trust. Regulated. Insured. Spanish."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Brokerage (BTC, ETH only)
- Secondary: Earn (conservative, BTC yield), Tax
- Aspirational: Card (if positioned as "spending your investment returns")

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-14: Slow registration. May take days to complete KYC (not urgent, cautious).
- Day 14-30: First buy (BTC, moderate amount €500-€3,000). Single transaction.
- Day 30-60: Checks portfolio occasionally. May make second buy. No urgency.
- Day 60-90: Settled. Quarterly buyer at most. Hold mentality.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €200-€1,000 (low frequency, moderate size)
- Monetization path: Brokerage (infrequent) → Earn (once explained) → Tax (annual)
- ARPU: €10-€30/month average. Lumpy (large infrequent buys).

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Regulatory negative news (even if unrelated to Bit2Me), security incident (platform or industry-wide), loss of confidence from -30%+ portfolio drop.
- Warning signals: Support inquiry about withdrawal process, no login in 60+ days after initial buy.
- Timeline: Long churn cycle. Takes months to decide to leave. May sit dormant for 6+ months before withdrawing.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN total_unique_assets_traded <= 3
     AND primary_assets_traded IN ('BTC', 'ETH')
     AND total_trades_lifetime < 20
     AND days_since_registration > 90
     AND registration_country = 'ES'
     AND avg_trade_size_eur > 300
THEN 'REGULATION_CONSERVATIVE'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: May increase position slightly. Still cautious. Will not FOMO into altcoins.
- Bear: Freezes. Stops buying. Does not sell. Sits. Reactivates in next cycle. Very predictable.

---

### Archetype 8: Entusiasta Social (Social/Peer-Pressure Entrant)

**1. Description:** Entered crypto because of social pressure, meme coins, or viral trends (Dogecoin, Shiba, Pepe). Lottery ticket mentality. Expects 10-100x returns. Low financial literacy.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 18-30
- Income: €10K-€25K/year
- Geography: Spain, LATAM
- Tech literacy: High (mobile-native) but low financial literacy.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Quick gains, social status ("I own crypto"), meme culture
- Risk tolerance: High (unaware of real risk). Would put €200 in a meme coin hoping for €20K.
- Information: TikTok, Instagram, YouTube shorts, influencers, meme communities.

**4. Primary motivation:** "This coin is going to moon! My friend made 5x. I want in."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Brokerage (meme coins, trending assets)
- Secondary: None initially
- Aspirational: If educated, DCA and Earn

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-3: Impulse registration. First buy within hours. Often a specific trending asset.
- Day 3-14: Checks portfolio obsessively (5-10x/day). May buy more if price rises. Panics if drops.
- Day 14-30: If in profit, euphoric. If in loss, angry and blaming platform.
- Day 30-90: 80%+ churn. Survivors either educate themselves (→ Millennial Investor) or wait for next meme cycle.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €10-€50 (extremely high churn)
- Monetization path: Single Brokerage trade → (most churn here) → possible second meme buy if trend continues
- ARPU: €2-€5/month average (high initial, collapses)

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Loss (any loss), boredom (meme cycle ends), confusion, negative social proof ("crypto is a scam").
- Warning signals: Single trade, no second action, angry support ticket.
- Timeline: 48-72 hour decision window. If no positive reinforcement by Day 3, they're mentally gone.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN total_trades_lifetime <= 2
     AND first_asset_traded IN (SELECT asset_id FROM meme_coin_list)
     AND avg_trade_size_eur < 200
     AND days_since_registration <= 90
THEN 'SOCIAL_ENTRANT'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Swarms in. Highest volume of registrations during meme-coin rallies. Lowest retention.
- Bear: Disappears entirely. Near-zero presence.

---

### Archetype 9: La Ballena (The Whale)

**1. Description:** €50K+ balance. Expects personal service, priority support, and preferential treatment. Disproportionate revenue contribution. May have account manager via OTC desk.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 35-60
- Income: €150K+/year or significant crypto-native wealth
- Geography: Spain (primarily)
- Tech literacy: Variable. Some are technically sophisticated; others delegate to advisors.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Service quality, privacy, execution for large orders, counterparty reliability
- Risk tolerance: High (in absolute terms) but sophisticated risk management.
- Information: OTC desks, private networks, family office advisors.

**4. Primary motivation:** "I need to move large amounts efficiently, securely, and with minimal market impact."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: OTC or Brokerage (large orders), Earn (yield on large balance)
- Secondary: Loan (borrow against position), Staking
- Aspirational: API (custom integration)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-7: KYC (may require enhanced due diligence). Test transaction (€1K-€5K).
- Day 7-30: If satisfied, large deposit (€50K-€500K+). OTC trade or large Brokerage order.
- Day 30-60: Earn deposit. Staking. Multi-product within 60 days.
- Day 60-90: Steady state. Low transaction count but very high revenue per transaction.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €5,000-€100,000+ (lifetime)
- Monetization path: OTC/Brokerage → Earn → Loan → Staking
- ARPU: €500-€5,000+/month. NOTE: 90.91% of Loan Whales come from Brokerage C8 (High Value cluster).

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Service quality decline, execution problems (slippage on large orders), security incident, better terms at competitor OTC desk.
- Warning signals: Any withdrawal > 20% of balance, support complaint, counterparty request for better terms.
- Timeline: Slow and deliberate. Will test competitor with small amount before moving. 3-6 month churn cycle.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN total_balance_eur > 50000
     OR total_lifetime_volume_eur > 200000
     OR has_otc_relationship = TRUE
THEN 'WHALE'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Active trading. OTC volume increases. May diversify into new assets.
- Bear: Consolidates. May increase Earn allocation. Does not panic sell. Reduces trading frequency but maintains position.

---

### Archetype 10: Estudiante Academy (Academy Student)

**1. Description:** Entered via Bit2Me Academy (3M+ students, 50% LATAM). Zero CAC. Has educational relationship with Bit2Me but may never have used the exchange. Bridge from learning to buying is the key conversion challenge.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: 20-40
- Income: Variable (students to professionals)
- Geography: 50% LATAM, 30% Spain, 20% other
- Tech literacy: Growing. Learning from Academy content.

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Education, understanding before investing, credibility of educational source
- Risk tolerance: Developing. Educated about risk but hasn't experienced it yet.
- Information: Bit2Me Academy (primary), YouTube, blogs.

**4. Primary motivation:** "I want to understand crypto before putting money in."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Academy (learning)
- Secondary: Brokerage (first purchase post-education)
- Aspirational: Earn, DCA (natural next steps after education)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-30: Consuming Academy content. May complete multiple courses. No exchange registration yet.
- Day 30-60: Registers for exchange (if prompted). KYC.
- Day 60-90: First buy (if converted). Typically more informed than average first-time buyer.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €50-€300 (if converted). €0 if remains Academy-only.
- Monetization path: Academy → Registration → KYC → Brokerage → DCA → Earn
- ARPU: €0 during learning phase. €10-€30/month if converted.
- Key metric: Academy-to-FM conversion rate. REQUIRES DATA. Benchmark: 5-15% for education-to-product funnels.

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave (from Academy): Content completion without product bridge, competitor with Learn & Earn (Coinbase, Binance, OKX).
- Warning signals: Course completion without registration, registration without KYC, KYC without deposit.
- Timeline: Long conversion window (30-90 days from first content to first trade). Need patience.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN acquisition_source = 'academy'
     AND (fm_date IS NULL OR days_since_registration > 60)
THEN 'ACADEMY_STUDENT'
-- Note: Once converted and active for 90+ days, reclassify to appropriate archetype
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Academy traffic increases. More students convert (market excitement lowers barriers).
- Bear: Academy traffic may increase (people want to learn about crashes). Conversion drops (fear).

---

### Archetype 11: Holder Dormido (Dormant Asset Holder)

**1. Description:** Has balance > €100 on Bit2Me but has not taken any action in 90-365 days. Was once active. Money is still here, which signals residual trust. The reactivation gold mine.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: Variable (reflects the archetype they WERE before going dormant)
- Income: Variable
- Geography: Spain (primary)
- Tech literacy: Variable

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Inertia (hassle of withdrawal > hassle of leaving money), crypto as "long-term hold"
- Risk tolerance: N/A (not actively making decisions)
- Information: Receives emails/push but rarely opens.

**4. Primary motivation (when active):** Variable. Now: "I'll deal with it later."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: Wallet (holding)
- Secondary: Earn (if reactivated, natural migration for idle balance)
- Aspirational: Any product that gives their idle balance a purpose

**6. Behavioral signature:**
- Last action was 90-365 days ago.
- May log in occasionally (1-2x/month) to check balance.
- Has not deposited, traded, or taken any monetizable action.
- Balance has been static (no deposits, no withdrawals).

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Current revenue: €0 (if balance not in Earn) to minimal (if balance in Earn or Staking).
- Reactivation LTV: If reactivated, expected to generate 30-50% of their original active-period revenue.
- Key metric: Reactivation rate and cost vs. new user CAC.

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Nothing specific. They're already "gone" behaviourally. A withdrawal trigger is usually external (need cash, competitor offer, tax event).
- Warning signals: Withdrawal initiated (once a dormant user starts withdrawing, 80%+ chance they fully exit).
- Timeline: Can remain dormant for years. Market recovery is the primary reactivation trigger.

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN total_balance_eur > 100
     AND days_since_last_monetizable_action BETWEEN 90 AND 365
     AND fm_date IS NOT NULL
THEN 'DORMANT_HOLDER'
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Reactivation wave. Market recovery triggers login → portfolio check → "oh, I'm up" → trade.
- Bear: Stays dormant. Or withdraws (cuts losses). Market crash is the highest-risk moment for dormant holder conversion to churned.

---

### Archetype 12: Corporativo B2B (B2B Corporate)

**1. Description:** Company or institutional entity using Bit2Me for treasury management, payment processing, or client-facing crypto services. Multi-user accounts. API-first. Relationship-managed.

**2. Demographics:**
- Age: N/A (entity)
- Revenue: Variable (SME to large corporate)
- Geography: Spain, EU
- Tech literacy: High (dedicated dev/treasury team)

**3. Psychographics:**
- Values: Reliability, compliance, SLA guarantees, account management
- Risk tolerance: Low (corporate treasury mandates)
- Information: Industry reports, regulatory guidance, RFP processes.

**4. Primary motivation:** "We need a regulated, reliable crypto infrastructure partner."

**5. Products:**
- Primary: API, OTC
- Secondary: Commerce (merchant gateway), Brokerage (corporate treasury)
- Aspirational: Earn (corporate yield), Card (corporate cards)

**6. Behavioral signature (first 90 days):**
- Day 1-30: KYB process (weeks, not days). Account setup. API integration. Test transactions.
- Day 30-60: First production transactions. Volume ramp.
- Day 60-90: Steady state volume. Regular scheduled transactions.

**7. Revenue profile:**
- Expected LTV: €10,000-€500,000+ (lifetime)
- Monetization path: API integration → Volume ramp → Expansion products → Multi-year contract
- ARPU: €1,000-€50,000+/month. Orders of magnitude higher than B2C.

**8. Churn risk profile:**
- What makes them leave: Better terms from competitor, API reliability issues, regulatory change, internal corporate decision to consolidate vendors.
- Warning signals: API call frequency decline, account manager receiving RFP questions, volume decrease 3 consecutive weeks.
- Timeline: Long. 3-6 month exit process (due to integration switching costs).

**9. SQL classification:**
```sql
WHEN segment = 'B2B'
     AND kyb_status = 'approved'
THEN 'B2B_CORPORATE'
-- Sub-classification by size handled in B2B lifecycle (Phase 3, Chunk 2)
```

**10. Bull vs Bear behavior:**
- Bull: Volume increases. New product requests. Expansion.
- Bear: Volume decreases but contract maintained. Cost sensitivity increases. May negotiate terms.

---

## 2.1b Master SQL Archetype Classifier

```sql
-- MASTER ARCHETYPE CLASSIFIER
-- Priority order: first match wins.
-- Evaluated daily on user_master_table.

SELECT
    user_id,
    CASE
        -- B2B is a hard segment, not behavioral
        WHEN segment = 'B2B' AND kyb_status = 'approved'
        THEN 'B2B_CORPORATE'

        -- Whale: balance or volume threshold (check before other archetypes)
        WHEN total_balance_eur > 50000
             OR total_lifetime_volume_eur > 200000
             OR has_otc_relationship = TRUE
        THEN 'WHALE'

        -- Pro Trader: high-frequency Pro usage
        WHEN pro_trades_30d >= 20
             AND pro_volume_30d > 10000
        THEN 'PRO_TRADER'

        -- DeFi Refugee: crypto-native, multi-asset, fast activation
        WHEN first_deposit_type = 'crypto'
             AND (earn_balance_eur > 1000 OR pro_volume_30d > 5000)
             AND total_unique_assets_traded >= 5
        THEN 'DEFI_REFUGEE'

        -- Yield Seeker: Earn-dominant, large balance
        WHEN earn_balance_eur > 5000
             AND earn_balance_eur / NULLIF(total_balance_eur, 0) > 0.6
             AND total_trades_30d <= 5
        THEN 'YIELD_SEEKER'

        -- Inflation Hedger: LATAM + stablecoin focus
        WHEN registration_country IN ('AR', 'PE', 'CO', 'MX', 'VE')
             AND COALESCE(stablecoin_balance_pct, 0) > 0.7
        THEN 'INFLATION_HEDGER'

        -- Dormant Holder: has balance, inactive 90-365d
        WHEN total_balance_eur > 100
             AND days_since_last_monetizable_action BETWEEN 90 AND 365
             AND fm_date IS NOT NULL
        THEN 'DORMANT_HOLDER'

        -- Regulation Conservative: Spain, BTC/ETH only, low frequency, >90d
        WHEN total_unique_assets_traded <= 3
             AND registration_country = 'ES'
             AND total_trades_lifetime < 20
             AND days_since_registration > 90
             AND avg_trade_size_eur > 300
        THEN 'REGULATION_CONSERVATIVE'

        -- Millennial Investor: multi-product, moderate volume, DCA or Earn
        WHEN total_trade_volume_eur BETWEEN 500 AND 20000
             AND products_used >= 2
             AND (has_active_dca = TRUE OR earn_balance_eur > 0)
             AND days_since_registration > 30
        THEN 'MILLENNIAL_INVESTOR'

        -- Academy Student: came from Academy, not yet converted or early
        WHEN acquisition_source = 'academy'
```
