
### Council Revenue SQL

```sql
-- Section 2: Revenue by Product × Geo (PT as separate column)
SELECT
    product,
    geography,
    SUM(CASE WHEN month = @this_month THEN revenue END) AS revenue_current,
    SUM(CASE WHEN month = @last_month THEN revenue END) AS revenue_prior,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        SUM(CASE WHEN month = @this_month THEN revenue END) -
        SUM(CASE WHEN month = @last_month THEN revenue END),
        SUM(CASE WHEN month = @last_month THEN revenue END)
    ) * 100 AS mom_pct
FROM revenue_by_stage_product
WHERE month IN (@this_month, @last_month)
GROUP BY product, geography
ORDER BY revenue_current DESC
```

```sql
-- Section 5: Revenue Opportunity Pipeline
-- DEPOSITED_ONLY (highest ROI per Chunk 1 v1.1)
SELECT
    'Convert DEPOSITED_ONLY' AS opportunity,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS population,
    SUM(eur_balance) AS total_idle_eur,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) * 0.30 AS target_conversions,  -- 30% conversion target
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) * 0.30 * 50 AS est_monthly_fm_revenue  -- €50 avg FM revenue
FROM user_lifecycle_stage
WHERE lifecycle_stage = 'DEPOSITED_ONLY'

UNION ALL

-- DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE reactivation
SELECT
    'Reactivate 10% DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE',
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id),
    SUM(total_balance_eur),
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) * 0.10,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) * 0.10 * 200  -- €200 avg reactivation D30 revenue
FROM user_lifecycle_stage
WHERE lifecycle_stage = 'DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE'

UNION ALL

-- DCA setup for single-product ACTIVE
SELECT
    'DCA setup for 1-product ACTIVE',
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id),
    NULL,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) * 0.15,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) * 0.15 * 100 * 0.015  -- €100/mo DCA × 1.5% spread
FROM user_lifecycle_stage
WHERE lifecycle_stage = 'ACTIVE'
  AND products_with_fm = 1
  AND has_active_dca = FALSE
```

### Council Timing

| Action | When | Who |
|--------|------|-----|
| Data freeze | Last day of month, 23:59 UTC | Automated |
| Report draft | Business day 1 of new month | Daniel |
| Salvia review (segment populations) | Business day 2 | Daniel + Salvia |
| Council presentation | Business day 3-5 (per calendar) | Daniel to Pablo |

## 5.3 Operational Dashboard (Always-On, Looker Studio)

### Tab 1: Lifecycle Populations

| Widget | Type | Data |
|--------|------|------|
| Stage distribution | Stacked bar (weekly) | user_lifecycle_stage grouped by stage, per week |
| Weekly deltas | Table with conditional formatting | COUNT per stage this week vs last week |
| Stage velocity | Line chart | Net flow into ACTIVE per week (entries minus exits) |
| POWER_USER count | Scorecard | Per Chunk 2 v1.1: monthly threshold, separate from ACTIVE |

```sql
-- Stage distribution with weekly deltas
SELECT
    snapshot_week,
    lifecycle_stage,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS population,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) - LAG(COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)) OVER (
        PARTITION BY lifecycle_stage ORDER BY snapshot_week
    ) AS delta_wow,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) - LAG(COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)) OVER (
            PARTITION BY lifecycle_stage ORDER BY snapshot_week
        ),
        LAG(COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)) OVER (
            PARTITION BY lifecycle_stage ORDER BY snapshot_week
        )
    ) * 100 AS delta_pct
FROM user_daily_snapshot
WHERE snapshot_date = DATE_TRUNC(snapshot_date, WEEK)
GROUP BY snapshot_week, lifecycle_stage
ORDER BY snapshot_week DESC, population DESC
```

### Tab 2: Movement Flows (Sankey)

**P0 DEPENDENCY:** Requires state_transition_history table (Chunk 2 v1.1, Stage 8 spec). Without this table, transitions cannot be tracked.

| Widget | Type | Data |
|--------|------|------|
| Stage transitions | Sankey diagram | state_transition_history |
| Top 5 flows | Table | Largest transitions ranked by volume |
| Regression alert | Scorecard | Users moving backward (ACTIVE→AT_RISK count + revenue at risk) |

```sql
-- Stage transitions for Sankey (uses state_transition_history from Chunk 2 v1.1)
SELECT
    from_stage,
    to_stage,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS users_transitioning,
    SUM(revenue_at_transition) AS revenue_at_risk,
    AVG(days_in_previous_stage) AS avg_days_in_origin
FROM state_transition_history
WHERE transition_date BETWEEN DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL 7 DAY) AND CURRENT_DATE()
  AND from_stage != to_stage
GROUP BY from_stage, to_stage
ORDER BY users_transitioning DESC
```

### Tab 3: Activation Funnels

| Widget | Type | Data |
|--------|------|------|
| Global funnel | Horizontal bar | Reg → KYC → Deposit → FM, by geo (PT separate) |
| DEPOSITED_ONLY spotlight | Scorecard | Population, median idle EUR, median days stuck (Chunk 1 v1.1 deep dive) |
| Per-product activation | Table | Activation rates per product (Chunk 1, Section 1.6) |
| Drop-off heatmap | Heatmap | Step × Geo × Device, colored by drop-off % |
| Phone verification tracker | Line chart | Drop-off at phone step: ES 32%, PT 28%, Global-sin-ES 53% |

```sql
-- Activation funnel by geo (PT as separate row) and channel
SELECT
    geography,
    acquisition_channel,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS registered,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN kyc_status = 'approved' THEN user_id END) AS kyc_complete,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN total_deposits > 0 THEN user_id END) AS deposited,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN total_deposits > 0 AND fm_date IS NULL THEN user_id END) AS deposited_only,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN user_id END) AS monetized,
    -- Conversion rates
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN kyc_status = 'approved' THEN user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)
    ) AS reg_to_kyc_rate,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN kyc_status = 'approved' THEN user_id END)
    ) AS kyc_to_fm_rate,
    -- DEPOSITED_ONLY conversion (Chunk 1 v1.1 highest-ROI target)
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN total_deposits > 0 AND fm_date IS NULL THEN user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN total_deposits > 0 THEN user_id END)
    ) AS deposit_stuck_rate
FROM user_master_table
WHERE registration_date BETWEEN @start_date AND @end_date
GROUP BY geography, acquisition_channel
ORDER BY registered DESC
```

### Tab 4: A/B Test Tracker

| Widget | Type | Data |
|--------|------|------|
| Active tests table | Table | test_id, name, status, primary_metric, bayesian_prob, days_running |
| Test pipeline | Kanban (Backlog → Building → Running → Reading → Shipped/Killed) | test_tracker |
| Cumulative test revenue | Line chart | Revenue from shipped tests, cumulative YTD |
| Test #→ Council Metric 5 link | Scorecard | Sum of incremental_revenue for all SHIPPED tests this period |

```sql
-- Test tracker view
SELECT
    test_id,
    test_name,
    status,
    segment_name,
    sample_size_treatment,
    sample_size_control,
    primary_metric,
    treatment_value,
    control_value,
    bayesian_probability,
    CASE
        WHEN bayesian_probability >= 0.90 AND guardrail_broken = FALSE THEN 'SHIP'
        WHEN bayesian_probability <= 0.20 OR guardrail_broken = TRUE THEN 'KILL'
        WHEN days_running > 56 THEN 'ITERATE'
        ELSE 'WAIT'
    END AS recommendation,
    start_date,
    DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), start_date, DAY) AS days_running,
    est_monthly_revenue_if_shipped
FROM ab_test_results
WHERE status IN ('RUNNING', 'READING')
ORDER BY bayesian_probability DESC
```

### Tab 5: Card + AUC Dashboard (NEW in v1.1)

Card is the biggest product gap (0.26% penetration vs 42-48% industry, 29% monthly churn). AUC drives the recurring revenue floor. Both need dedicated monitoring.

| Widget | Type | Data | Metric ID |
|--------|------|------|-----------|
| Card Penetration | Scorecard + trend | card_activated / MMU | CD1 |
| Card MAU | Scorecard + trend | card users with tx in 30d | CD3 |
| Card Monthly Churn | Scorecard (🔴 if >25%) | users_no_tx_30d / card_mau_start | CD4 |
| Card Interchange per User | Bar chart (by geo) | interchange / card_mau | CD5 |
| AUC Total | Scorecard + trend | SUM(all balances EUR) | AUC1 |
| Net AUC Flow | Line chart (weekly) | deposits minus withdrawals | AUC3 |
| Stablecoin Ratio | Scorecard | stablecoin_auc / total_auc | AUC5 |
| AUC per MMU | Scorecard | auc_total / mmu | AUC4 |

```sql
-- Card health dashboard
SELECT
    reporting_week,
    geography,
    -- CD1: Penetration
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN card_activated = TRUE THEN user_id END) /
        NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_economically_active = TRUE THEN user_id END), 0) AS card_penetration,
    -- CD3: Card MAU
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN card_tx_30d > 0 THEN user_id END) AS card_mau,
    -- CD4: Card churn
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN card_tx_prior_30d > 0 AND card_tx_30d = 0 THEN user_id END) /
        NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN card_tx_prior_30d > 0 THEN user_id END), 0) AS card_monthly_churn,
    -- CD5: Interchange per user
    SUM(card_interchange_30d) /
        NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN card_tx_30d > 0 THEN user_id END), 0) AS interchange_per_card_user
FROM user_daily_snapshot
WHERE snapshot_date = DATE_TRUNC(snapshot_date, WEEK)
GROUP BY reporting_week, geography
```

### Tab 6: Churn Early Warning

| Widget | Type | Data |
|--------|------|------|
| AT_RISK population | Scorecard with trend | AT_RISK count + WoW delta |
| AT_RISK by trigger | Table | By health_score component (Chunk 1 v1.1) |
| AT_RISK by Space Center tier | Table | Tier 3+ AT_RISK = high-touch intervention |
| DCA cancellation spike | Alert | DCA cancellations this week vs avg (strongest churn signal) |

```sql
-- AT_RISK breakdown by health_score component (Chunk 1 v1.1)
SELECT
    CASE
        WHEN activity_decline_4w_pct >= 50 THEN 'Activity decline >50%'
        WHEN health_score < 30 AND health_score_recency <= 10 THEN 'Recency score critical'
        WHEN health_score < 30 AND health_score_frequency <= 5 THEN 'Frequency score critical'
        WHEN health_score < 30 AND health_score_balance < 5 THEN 'Balance declining'
        WHEN dca_cancelled_recently = TRUE THEN 'DCA cancelled'
        WHEN earn_withdrawal_30d_pct > 0.5 THEN 'Earn withdrawal >50%'
    END AS at_risk_trigger,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS users,
    SUM(revenue_30d) AS revenue_at_risk,
    AVG(total_balance_eur) AS avg_balance,
    AVG(health_score) AS avg_health_score,
    -- Space Center tier distribution
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN space_center_tier >= 3 THEN user_id END) AS high_tier_at_risk
FROM user_lifecycle_stage
WHERE lifecycle_stage = 'AT_RISK'
GROUP BY at_risk_trigger
ORDER BY revenue_at_risk DESC
```

### Tab 7: Cross-Product Adoption

| Widget | Type | Data |
|--------|------|------|
| Product density histogram | Bar chart | % users with 1, 2, 3, 4+ products (L7) |
| Cross-sell waterfall | Waterfall chart | From Brokerage → next product adopted |
| DCA penetration | Scorecard | DCA users / MMU (X5), trend |
| B2M penetration | Scorecard | B2M holders / MMU (X3) |
| Golden Path progress | Funnel | Path 1 completion rate: Brokerage → DCA → Earn → Card |

## 5.4 Cohort Reports (Monthly)

### Cohort Dimensions

Every cohort tracked by:

1. **Registration month** (primary key)
2. **Acquisition channel** (Paid, Organic, Academy, Referral, B2B)
3. **Archetype** (Chunk 1 v1.1, 12 archetypes)
4. **Geography** (ES, PT, DE, IT, FR, LATAM, Other EU)
5. **Market condition at acquisition** (BULL, BEAR, NEUTRAL per Chunk 1 v1.1 thresholds)
6. **Volatility at acquisition** (HIGH_VOL, NORMAL_VOL, LOW_VOL per Chunk 1 v1.1)

### Cohort Report 1: Revenue Curves

```
Revenue per surviving user by cohort month:

Cohort      | W1    | W2    | W4    | W8    | W12   | W26   | W52
─────────────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────
Jan-26 ES Pd │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ —     │ —     │ —
Jan-26 ES Or │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ —     │ —     │ —
Jan-26 PT Pd │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ —     │ —     │ —
Dec-25 ES Pd │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ €{X}  │ —     │ —
```

```sql
-- Revenue curves by cohort (with market condition context)
SELECT
    fm_cohort_month,
    acquisition_channel,
    geography,
    market_condition_at_fm,
    months_since_fm,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS surviving_users,
    SUM(revenue) AS cohort_revenue,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(revenue), COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)) AS revenue_per_surviving_user,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT user_id),
        FIRST_VALUE(COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)) OVER (
            PARTITION BY fm_cohort_month, acquisition_channel, geography
            ORDER BY months_since_fm
        )
    ) AS survival_rate
FROM cohort_revenue_curves
GROUP BY fm_cohort_month, acquisition_channel, geography, market_condition_at_fm, months_since_fm
ORDER BY fm_cohort_month DESC, months_since_fm ASC
```

### Cohort Report 2: Retention Curves

```
% of cohort still economically active at day N:

Cohort      | D7    | D14   | D30   | D60   | D90   | D180  | D365
─────────────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────
Jan-26 ES    │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ —     │ —
Jan-26 PT    │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ —     │ —
Jan-26 DE    │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ —     │ —
```

### Cohort Report 3: Product Adoption Curves

```
% of cohort with 2+ products at day N:

Cohort      | D30   | D60   | D90   | DCA at D30
─────────────┼───────┼───────┼───────┼───────────
Jan-26 ES    │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%
Jan-26 PT    │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%  │ {X}%
```

### Cohort Comparison Template

For Council: "Jan Paid ES vs Feb Paid ES" or "Academy Q4 vs Academy Q1"

```sql
-- Side-by-side cohort comparison
SELECT
    months_since_fm,
    -- Cohort A
    SUM(CASE WHEN cohort_key = @cohort_a THEN revenue_per_surviving END) AS a_rev,
    SUM(CASE WHEN cohort_key = @cohort_a THEN survival_rate END) AS a_survival,
    -- Cohort B
    SUM(CASE WHEN cohort_key = @cohort_b THEN revenue_per_surviving END) AS b_rev,
    SUM(CASE WHEN cohort_key = @cohort_b THEN survival_rate END) AS b_survival,
    -- Delta
    b_rev - a_rev AS revenue_delta,
    b_survival - a_survival AS survival_delta
FROM cohort_revenue_curves
WHERE cohort_key IN (@cohort_a, @cohort_b)
GROUP BY months_since_fm
```

# PHASE 6: ATTRIBUTION MODEL (How We Count)

## 6.1 The Attribution Architecture

### Current State

- 7-day push attribution window (CleverTap default)
- Other channels: undocumented
- Known problem: CRM likely OVERCOUNTED, Paid likely UNDERCOUNTED
- Revenue attribution data (known): AI €598K, Brand €262K, CRM €240K, Direct €77K, Paid €17K
- Academy-to-Exchange attribution flagged as P0 data dependency (Chunk 1 v1.1): `acquisition_source = 'academy'` may not exist reliably

### Recommended Model: W-Shaped Attribution

Crypto exchanges have a gated funnel with 4 high-value touchpoints. Linear or last-touch miss the acquisition journey. U-shaped underweights deposit. W-shaped gives credit to the moments that matter.

```
Journey:
   First Touch ──→ KYC Completion ──→ First Deposit ──→ First Monetization
       │                 │                  │                  │
       ▼                 ▼                  ▼                  ▼
   Awareness          Trust built        Money committed     Revenue generated
       │                 │                  │                  │
   30% credit        20% credit          20% credit         30% credit
```

### W-Shaped Model Specification

| Touchpoint | Weight | Rationale |
|-----------|--------|-----------|
| First Touch | 30% | Determines awareness. Paid vs Organic vs Academy is a fundamental distinction. |
| KYC Completion Assist | 20% | Closest touch to KYC. In crypto, KYC is a trust barrier (phone step = 32% drop ES, 53% global). |
| First Deposit Assist | 20% | Closest touch to deposit. Committing fiat signals intent. DEPOSITED_ONLY (Chunk 1 v1.1) is highest-ROI. |
| First Monetization (last touch) | 30% | Trigger that converted deposit to revenue. |

### Attribution Windows by Channel

| Channel | Window | Rationale | Competitive Reference |
|---------|--------|-----------|----------------------|
| Paid Search (Google/Bing) | 30 days post-click | High intent, crypto consideration 1-4 weeks | Coinbase: 28-day click window |
| Paid Social (Meta, TikTok) | 7 days post-click, 1 day post-view | Lower intent | Industry standard |
| CRM Push (CleverTap) | **48 hours** post-delivery | Push is trigger, not awareness. Current 7-day inflates CRM. | Revolut: 24-48h push window |
| CRM Email | 72 hours post-open | Slightly longer consideration | Standard |
| CRM SMS | 24 hours post-delivery | Immediate channel | Standard |
| Partners/Affiliates | 60 days post-click | Longer consideration for referred traffic | Binance affiliate: 90d, Coinbase: 30d |
| Academy | 90 days post-last-content | Academy users: 30-90d from learning to trading (Chunk 2 v1.1, §3.5) | Coinbase Learn & Earn: tracks indefinitely |
| Brand (PR, events) | 14 days post-impression (if trackable) | Hard to attribute; use lift studies | N/A |
| Referral | 30 days post-click | Standard window | Crypto.com: 30d, Coinbase: 30d |
| AI (chatbot, recs) | Session-based | In-session conversion | N/A |
| Direct/Organic | N/A (baseline) | Control in incrementality tests | N/A |

### The 7-Day Push Window Problem

```
Current state:
  User sees paid ad (Day 1) → Nothing
  User receives push notification (Day 5) → User converts (Day 6)

  Result with current model: 100% credit to CRM Push
  Reality: Paid ad created awareness. Push was the trigger.

With W-shaped (proposed):
  First Touch: Paid ad (30% credit)
  KYC Assist: Paid retarget (20% credit)
  Deposit Assist: Push notification (20% credit)
  FM Assist: Push notification (30% credit)

  Result: Paid gets 50%, CRM gets 50%
```

### W-Shaped Attribution SQL

```sql
-- W-shaped attribution calculator
WITH journey AS (
    SELECT
        user_id,
        channel,
        event_timestamp,
        event_type  -- 'impression', 'click', 'push_delivered', 'email_opened', etc.
    FROM user_touchpoints
    WHERE user_id IN (SELECT user_id FROM users WHERE fm_date IS NOT NULL)
),

classified AS (
    SELECT
        j.user_id,
        j.channel,
        j.event_timestamp,
        CASE
            -- First Touch: earliest touchpoint
            WHEN j.event_timestamp = MIN(j.event_timestamp) OVER (PARTITION BY j.user_id)
                THEN 'first_touch'
            -- KYC Assist: closest touchpoint before KYC within channel-specific window
            WHEN ABS(TIMESTAMP_DIFF(j.event_timestamp, u.kyc_date, HOUR)) =
                 MIN(ABS(TIMESTAMP_DIFF(j.event_timestamp, u.kyc_date, HOUR)))
                     OVER (PARTITION BY j.user_id)
                 AND j.event_timestamp <= u.kyc_date
                THEN 'kyc_assist'
            -- Deposit Assist: closest touchpoint before first deposit
            WHEN ABS(TIMESTAMP_DIFF(j.event_timestamp, u.first_deposit_date, HOUR)) =
                 MIN(ABS(TIMESTAMP_DIFF(j.event_timestamp, u.first_deposit_date, HOUR)))
                     OVER (PARTITION BY j.user_id)
                 AND j.event_timestamp <= u.first_deposit_date
                THEN 'deposit_assist'
            -- FM Assist: closest touchpoint before FM
            WHEN ABS(TIMESTAMP_DIFF(j.event_timestamp, u.fm_date, HOUR)) =
                 MIN(ABS(TIMESTAMP_DIFF(j.event_timestamp, u.fm_date, HOUR)))
                     OVER (PARTITION BY j.user_id)
                 AND j.event_timestamp <= u.fm_date
                THEN 'fm_assist'
            ELSE 'mid_touch'
        END AS touchpoint_role,
        CASE
            WHEN touchpoint_role = 'first_touch' THEN 0.30
            WHEN touchpoint_role = 'kyc_assist' THEN 0.20
            WHEN touchpoint_role = 'deposit_assist' THEN 0.20
            WHEN touchpoint_role = 'fm_assist' THEN 0.30
            ELSE 0
        END AS attribution_weight
    FROM journey j
    JOIN users u ON j.user_id = u.user_id
)

SELECT
    channel,
    SUM(r.fm_revenue * c.attribution_weight) AS attributed_revenue,
    COUNT(DISTINCT c.user_id) AS users_touched,
    SUM(r.fm_revenue * c.attribution_weight) / NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT c.user_id), 0) AS rev_per_user
FROM classified c
JOIN revenue_events r ON c.user_id = r.user_id AND r.is_fm = TRUE
WHERE c.attribution_weight > 0
GROUP BY channel
ORDER BY attributed_revenue DESC
```

### Identifying Touchpoints from Available Data

| Touchpoint Role | How to Identify | Source Today |
|----------------|-----------------|-------------|
| First Touch | First tracked interaction (UTM at registration) | Qlik Acquisition (utm_source, utm_medium) |
| KYC Assist | Last marketing touch within 48h before kyc_approved_date | CleverTap campaign events + Qlik timestamps |
| Deposit Assist | Last marketing touch within 48h before first_deposit_date | CleverTap events |
| FM Assist | Last marketing touch within 48h before fm_date | CleverTap events |

**BLOCKED:** Server-side first-touch tracking requires engineering work (§6.2). Current first-touch relies on UTM at registration. If UTM missing: first_touch = 'Direct/Unknown'.

**Academy attribution gap (Chunk 1 v1.1):** The field `acquisition_source = 'academy'` may not exist reliably. Until resolved, Academy users who register organically (no UTM) are misclassified as Direct. This inflates Direct and deflates Academy attribution. P0 data request: validate academy→exchange user linkage.

---

## 6.2 Server-Side Tracking Requirements

### Why Server-Side

Client-side cookies are unreliable in crypto:
1. ITP (Safari): 7-day cookie expiration for third-party, 24h for some first-party
2. Ad blockers: 25-40% of crypto users block tracking scripts
3. Cross-device: registration on mobile, KYC on desktop, deposit on mobile
4. EU cookie consent: MiCA-regulated platform, GDPR applies; consent rates ~60-70%

### Server-Side Architecture

```
User Action → Bit2Me Backend → Server-Side Event Router
                                       │
                    ┌──────────────────┬┴──────────────┐
                    ▼                  ▼               ▼
              Google Ads API    Meta CAPI        CleverTap
              (offline conv)   (server events)   (profile update)
                    │                  │               │
                    ▼                  ▼               ▼
              Attribution DB (BigQuery)
```

### Implementation Priority

| Component | Priority | Effort | Impact |
|-----------|----------|--------|--------|
| Server-side conversion tracking (Google) | P1 | Medium (2-3 weeks eng) | Fixes Paid undercounting |
| Meta Conversions API | P1 | Medium (2-3 weeks eng) | Fixes Meta attribution |
| First-touch persistence (server-side) | P1 | Low (1 week eng) | Fixes unknown first-touch |
| Academy-to-Exchange user linking | P0 | Low (data team) | Fixes Academy attribution gap |
| Cross-device identity graph | P2 | High (4-6 weeks eng) | Fixes multi-device journeys |
| CleverTap event enrichment | P2 | Low (config) | Enables full-funnel CRM attribution |

### Minimum Viable Attribution (Before Server-Side)

```sql
-- Interim: First-touch from UTM + Last-touch from CleverTap, 50/50 split
SELECT
    user_id,
    COALESCE(utm_source, 'direct') AS first_touch_channel,
    last_campaign_before_fm AS last_touch_channel,
    fm_revenue * 0.5 AS first_touch_revenue,
    fm_revenue * 0.5 AS last_touch_revenue
FROM user_attribution_base
WHERE fm_date IS NOT NULL
```

---

## 6.3 Multi-Touch Journey Attribution

### Common Journeys at Bit2Me

| Journey Pattern | Frequency (est.) | Attribution Challenge |
|----------------|-------------------|----------------------|
| Academy → Organic reg → CRM push → FM | Common | Academy gets zero credit in last-touch. Academy attribution gap (Chunk 1 v1.1) compounds this. |
| Paid click → Bounce → Brand search → Reg → CRM email → FM | Very common | Paid and Brand both contributed |
| Referral click → Reg → No action 30d → Market pump push → FM | Common in bull | Was it referral or market? Volatility flag (Chunk 1 v1.1) helps disambiguate. |
| B2B sales call → KYB → Integration → First trade | B2B only | Relationship-managed, no digital attribution |
| Organic → Reg → DCA setup → FM via DCA execution | Growing | DCA setup was key. Who prompted it? |

### Journey Reconstruction SQL

```sql
-- Full journey per user
SELECT
    user_id,
    ARRAY_AGG(
        STRUCT(
            channel, campaign_name, event_timestamp,
            touchpoint_role, attribution_weight_w_shaped
        )
        ORDER BY event_timestamp
    ) AS journey,
    COUNT(*) AS journey_length,
    DATE_DIFF(fm_date, first_touch_date, DAY) AS journey_duration_days,
    SUM(CASE WHEN channel = 'paid' THEN attribution_weight_w_shaped END) AS paid_credit,
    SUM(CASE WHEN channel = 'crm' THEN attribution_weight_w_shaped END) AS crm_credit,
    SUM(CASE WHEN channel = 'organic' THEN attribution_weight_w_shaped END) AS organic_credit,
    SUM(CASE WHEN channel = 'academy' THEN attribution_weight_w_shaped END) AS academy_credit
FROM user_touchpoints_classified
WHERE fm_date IS NOT NULL
GROUP BY user_id
```

---

## 6.4 Incrementality-Adjusted Attribution

### Combining Attribution + Holdout

Attribution tells WHO gets credit. Incrementality (Chunk 2 v1.1 §4.5, permanent 10% holdout) tells IF the credit was REAL.

```
Step 1: W-shaped attribution says CRM generated €240K
Step 2: Holdout shows CRM holdout group converted at 60% of treatment group
Step 3: Incremental CRM revenue = €240K × (1 - 0.60) = €96K
Step 4: Non-incremental €144K would have happened anyway
```

### Incrementality Adjustment Formula

```
Incremental_Revenue_channel = Attributed_Revenue_channel × (1 - Holdout_Rate / Treatment_Rate)
```

### Statistical Significance Requirements (from Chunk 2 v1.1)

- Minimum holdout duration: **8 weeks** before drawing conclusions
- For segment with 10,000 users (10% holdout = 1,000): MDE at 80% power = ~2.5pp
- Segments < 4,000 users: combine with similar segments or accept directional signal
- Always report with confidence interval: "CRM generated €120K ± €35K incremental"

```sql
-- Incrementality adjustment per channel
WITH holdout_rates AS (
    SELECT
        channel,
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_holdout = FALSE AND fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN user_id END) /
            NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_holdout = FALSE THEN user_id END), 0) AS treatment_rate,
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_holdout = TRUE AND fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN user_id END) /
            NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_holdout = TRUE THEN user_id END), 0) AS holdout_rate,
        -- Confidence interval (approximate)
        SQRT(
            treatment_rate * (1 - treatment_rate) /
                NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_holdout = FALSE THEN user_id END), 0)
            + holdout_rate * (1 - holdout_rate) /
                NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN is_holdout = TRUE THEN user_id END), 0)
        ) * 1.96 AS ci_95
    FROM user_channel_exposure
    WHERE experiment_start_date <= DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL 56 DAY)  -- 8-week minimum
    GROUP BY channel
)

SELECT
    a.channel,
    SUM(a.attributed_revenue) AS raw_attributed,
    h.treatment_rate,
    h.holdout_rate,
    1 - SAFE_DIVIDE(h.holdout_rate, h.treatment_rate) AS incrementality_factor,
    SUM(a.attributed_revenue) * (1 - SAFE_DIVIDE(h.holdout_rate, h.treatment_rate)) AS incremental_revenue,
    h.ci_95 AS confidence_interval
FROM w_shaped_attribution a
JOIN holdout_rates h ON a.channel = h.channel
GROUP BY a.channel, h.treatment_rate, h.holdout_rate, h.ci_95
ORDER BY incremental_revenue DESC
```

### Expected Impact on Revenue Attribution

| Channel | Current Attribution | Expected After W-Shaped + Incrementality | Direction |
|---------|--------------------|-----------------------------------------|-----------|
| AI | €598K | Likely similar (in-session, high incrementality) | Stable |
| Brand | €262K | Likely higher (currently uncredited first touches) | ▲ |
| CRM | €240K | Likely €96K-€150K (7-day window overcounts; incrementality ~40-60%) | ▼▼ |
| Direct | €77K | Likely lower (absorbed into Academy, Brand once tracked) | ▼ |
| Paid | €17K | Likely higher (loses credit to CRM push in current model) | ▲▲ |
| Academy | Not tracked | Will emerge as channel once attribution gap fixed | NEW |

# PHASE 7: TESTING FRAMEWORK (The Engine)

## 7.1 Methodology

### Three Methods for Three Contexts

| Method | When to Use | Population | Example | Tool |
|--------|-------------|-----------|---------|------|
| **Group Sequential** | Small populations, can't wait. Early stopping. | <1,000 users | Whale reactivation (C8: 5,393 users) | R/Python, custom stopping rules |
| **Multi-Armed Bandits** | Evergreen campaigns. Continuous optimization. | Any size, recurring | Welcome series, recurring DCA nudge | CleverTap Intelligent Selection |
| **Bayesian A/B** | Executive communication. "92% probability B is better." ~75% less sample with informative priors. | >1,000 users | Most lifecycle tests | CleverTap A/B + manual Bayesian calc |

### Variance Reduction: CUPED

Apply CUPED to every test. Covariable = user's pre-experiment revenue or transaction volume.

```
Y_adjusted = Y_observed - θ × (X_pre - X̄_pre)

Where:
  θ = Cov(Y, X_pre) / Var(X_pre)
  X_pre = same metric in 4 weeks prior to experiment
```

```sql
-- CUPED adjustment
WITH pre AS (
    SELECT user_id, SUM(revenue) AS pre_revenue
    FROM revenue_events
    WHERE event_date BETWEEN DATE_SUB(@test_start, INTERVAL 28 DAY) AND @test_start
    GROUP BY user_id
),
test AS (
    SELECT user_id, test_group, SUM(revenue) AS test_revenue
    FROM revenue_events r
    JOIN test_assignments t ON r.user_id = t.user_id
    WHERE r.event_date BETWEEN @test_start AND @test_end
    GROUP BY user_id, test_group
)

SELECT
    test_group,
    AVG(test_revenue) AS raw_mean,
    AVG(test_revenue - @theta * (pre_revenue - @pre_mean)) AS cuped_mean,
    STDDEV(test_revenue - @theta * (pre_revenue - @pre_mean)) AS cuped_stddev
FROM test tp JOIN pre pp ON tp.user_id = pp.user_id
GROUP BY test_group
```

CUPED reduces variance 30-50%, meaning tests reach significance faster.

### Permanent 10% Holdout

Per Chunk 2 v1.1 §4.5:
- 10% receives NO lifecycle campaigns. Persistent assignment.
- 8-week minimum before measurement.
- Statistical significance requirements per segment size.

```sql
-- Holdout assignment (run once, persist)
SELECT
    user_id,
    CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING))), 100) < 10
         THEN TRUE ELSE FALSE
    END AS is_holdout
FROM user_master_table
WHERE account_status = 'enabled'
```

---

## 7.2 Test Card Structure (9 Points, Mandatory)

Every test filed in the backlog must complete this card. No exceptions.

```
╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║  TEST CARD #[ID]                                                    ║
╠══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
║                                                                      ║
║  1. HYPOTHESIS (IF/THEN/BECAUSE)                                     ║
║     IF we [action],                                                  ║
║     THEN [expected measurable outcome],                              ║
║     BECAUSE [behavioral economics principle + evidence].             ║
║                                                                      ║
║  2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE / BENCHMARK                                  ║
║     [Who has done this? What was the result?]                        ║
║     [Reference Phase 9 Competitive Intelligence Report]              ║
║                                                                      ║
║  3. METRICS                                                          ║
║     Primary: [one metric, from catalog ID]                           ║
║     Secondary: [2-3 metrics]                                         ║
║     Guardrail: [one metric that must NOT degrade]                    ║
║                                                                      ║
║  4. SEGMENTS                                                         ║
║     Include: [lifecycle stage + conditions]                          ║
║     Exclude: [is_holdout, other running tests, B2B unless targeted]  ║
║                                                                      ║
║  5. CONTROL vs VARIANT                                               ║
║     Control: [current experience / no message]                       ║
║     Variant A: [description]                                         ║
║     Variant B: [optional]                                            ║
║                                                                      ║
║  6. EXPECTED IMPACT (revenue)                                        ║
║     Conservative / Base / Optimistic: €[X]/month                     ║
║                                                                      ║
║  7. ICE SCORE                                                        ║
║     Impact: [1-10]  Confidence: [1-10]  Ease: [1-10]               ║
║     Total: [I × C × E]                                              ║
║                                                                      ║
║  8. DEPENDENCIES                                                     ║
║     Engineering: [Y/N]  Data: [Y/N]  Legal: [Y/N]  Design: [Y/N]   ║
║                                                                      ║
║  9. RUNTIME                                                          ║
║     Method: [Group Sequential / MAB / Bayesian A/B]                  ║
║     Sample: [N per variant, per §7.6 protocol]                       ║
║     MDE: [minimum detectable effect]                                 ║
║     Duration: [X weeks]                                              ║
║                                                                      ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝
```

---

## 7.3 Decision Criteria

| Decision | Condition | Action |
|----------|-----------|--------|
| **SHIP** | Bayesian probability >= 90% AND guardrail not degraded > 2% | Roll to full segment. Calculate monthly revenue. |
| **KILL** | Bayesian probability >= 80% treatment worse OR guardrail degradation > 5% | Stop. Document learning. |
| **ITERATE** | Mixed results after 8 weeks. Neither SHIP nor KILL. | Stop. Redesign variant. Refile test card. |

### Escalation Rules

| Scenario | Who Decides |
|----------|------------|
| SHIP, impact < €5K/month | Patri ships, reports Monday |
| SHIP, impact >= €5K/month | Daniel reviews before ship |
| KILL | Patri kills, documents learning |
| Compliance implications | Daniel + Legal review |
| Affects B2B users | Daniel reviews (relationship-managed) |
| Affects Space Center Tier 3+ users | Daniel reviews (high-value, per Chunk 1 v1.1 churn modifier) |
| Mixed results | Daniel + Patri Thursday sync |

---

## 7.4 Scaling Roadmap

| Timeline | Tests/Week | Concurrent | Team |
|----------|-----------|------------|------|
| Month 1 | 2-3 launches | 4-6 running | Patri builds, Katy/Miguel assist |
| Month 2 | 5-8 launches | 10-15 running | Full CRM team |
| Month 3 | 10-20 launches | 20-30 running | Automated infra, MAB for evergreen |

### Weekly Monday Test Table

```
Week 8 — 2026-02-23

ID   | Name                    | Status   | Days | Primary Metric      | Treat  | Ctrl   | P(win) | Decision
─────┼─────────────────────────┼──────────┼──────┼─────────────────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼─────────
#001 | DCA nudge D7 post-FM    | READING  | 21   | DCA setup rate      | 8.2%   | 3.1%   | 97%    | SHIP
#002 | Earn cross-sell balance  | RUNNING  | 14   | Earn deposit rate   | 4.5%   | 3.8%   | 68%    | WAIT
#003 | Whale reactivation €10  | RUNNING  | 10   | Reactivation rate   | 2.1%   | 1.4%   | 61%    | WAIT
#004 | KYC urgency scarcity    | BUILDING | —    | KYC completion rate  | —      | —      | —      | —
#005 | Card cashback reminder  | BACKLOG  | —    | Card tx/month       | —      | —      | —      | —
```

---

## 7.5 Behavioral Economics Toolkit

Every test hypothesis must cite one or more. Pablo's mandate: "cada acción tendrá un estudio teórico detrás."

| # | Principle | Definition | Crypto Application | Test Example |
|---|-----------|-----------|-------------------|--------------|
| BE1 | **Loss Aversion** | Losses felt ~2x more than gains (Kahneman & Tversky, 1979) | "You're missing €X in yield" > "You could earn €X" | Earn cross-sell framed as lost yield |
| BE2 | **Endowment Effect** | People overvalue what they own (Thaler, 1980) | Portfolio milestone notifications | "Your BTC is worth €X more than when you bought" |
| BE3 | **Commitment/Consistency** | Small commitments → larger ones (Cialdini, 1984) | DCA setup (small recurring) → larger deposits | DCA nudge D7, small amount → increase D30 |
| BE4 | **Social Proof** | Others' behavior signals correct (Cialdini, 1984) | "12,847 users started DCA this month" | Registration page counter |
| BE5 | **Scarcity/Urgency** | Limited availability → perceived value (Cialdini, 1984) | "Launchpad allocation closes in 48h" | KYC urgency for Launchpad access |
| BE6 | **Default Effect** | People stick with defaults (Johnson & Goldstein, 2003) | Pre-selected DCA amount, default yield reinvestment | Default €25/week DCA during onboarding |
| BE7 | **Anchoring** | First number frames judgment (Tversky & Kahneman, 1974) | "Users like you invest €200/month" | Deposit screen anchor |
| BE8 | **FOMO** | 84% of crypto holders report FOMO decisions (Gemini survey) | "BTC up 12% this week. Your DCA would have captured this." | AT_RISK market momentum push |
| BE9 | **Disposition Effect** | Sell winners early, hold losers (Shefrin & Statman, 1985) | Users sell profitable positions, stop trading | "Portfolio up. Consider DCA to keep building." |
| BE10 | **Sunk Cost** | Past investment increases commitment (Arkes & Blumer, 1985) | B2M token staking = switching cost | "You've earned €X in rewards. Unstaking loses yield." |
| BE11 | **Reciprocity** | Give value first, then ask (Cialdini, 1984) | Free Academy content → registration CTA | Learn & Earn: give crypto → ask for deposit |
| BE12 | **Peak-End Rule** | Experience judged by peak + end (Kahneman, 1999) | First trade success + exit UX | Celebrate first profitable trade. Smooth withdrawal. |

---

## 7.6 Standard Sample Sizing Protocol

Pablo's mandate: "dijimos un % del total del segmento para test."

### Standard Table

| Segment Size | Method | Sample per Variant | Min Runtime | Scale Threshold |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| <1,000 | Group Sequential (full segment, early stopping) | 50/50 split | 2 weeks | Bayesian > 90% |
| 1,000-10,000 | Bayesian A/B | 15-20% per variant | 3-4 weeks | Bayesian > 90% + MDE met |
| 10,000-50,000 | Bayesian A/B | 10-15% per variant | 2-3 weeks | Bayesian > 90% + MDE met |
| 50,000+ | Bayesian A/B | 5-10% per variant | 2 weeks | Bayesian > 90% + MDE met |
| Evergreen | Multi-Armed Bandit | Full eligible | Continuous | Automatic convergence |

### Sample Size Formula

```
n = (Z_α/2 + Z_β)² × [p1(1-p1) + p2(1-p2)] / (p2 - p1)²

For Bayesian: multiply by 0.75 (informative priors)
```

### Assignment SQL (Respecting Pablo's Rule)

```sql
-- Never test full segment unless known-good rollout
SELECT
    user_id,
    CASE
        WHEN segment_size < 1000 THEN
            CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 2) = 0
                 THEN 'treatment' ELSE 'control' END
        WHEN segment_size BETWEEN 1000 AND 10000 THEN
            CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 100) < 20
                 THEN CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 2) = 0
                      THEN 'treatment' ELSE 'control' END
                 ELSE 'not_in_test' END
        WHEN segment_size BETWEEN 10001 AND 50000 THEN
            CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 100) < 10
                 THEN CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 2) = 0
                      THEN 'treatment' ELSE 'control' END
                 ELSE 'not_in_test' END
        ELSE
            CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 100) < 5
                 THEN CASE WHEN MOD(ABS(FARM_FINGERPRINT(CAST(user_id AS STRING) || @test_id)), 2) = 0
                      THEN 'treatment' ELSE 'control' END
                 ELSE 'not_in_test' END
    END AS test_assignment
FROM user_lifecycle_stage
WHERE lifecycle_stage IN (@target_stages)
  AND is_holdout = FALSE
  AND user_id NOT IN (
      SELECT user_id FROM active_test_assignments
      WHERE test_id != @test_id AND status = 'RUNNING'
  )
```

### Team: Patri (lead), Katy, Miguel

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│                                                                         │

│   □ No overlap with running tests?                                      │

│     unless verified, no financial advice language)                       │

│   □ Frequency cap: max 2 pushes/week per user?                          │
│   □ Space Center tier 3+ users flagged for review if targeted?          │
│                                                                         │
│ Launch: Wednesday by 14:00 CET                                          │
│                                                                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ THURSDAY: MID-WEEK CHECK (30 min)                                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│ Delivery check:                                                         │
│   → Push: >95% delivery, >5% open                                      │
│   → Email: >90% delivery, >20% open                                    │
│   → If below: investigate immediately                                   │
│                                                                         │
│ Early signal (directional only, NO decisions):                          │
│   → Treatment directionally positive?                                   │
│   → Guardrail already breaking? If yes: STOP immediately               │
│                                                                         │
│ Salvia sync if needed on segment data                                   │
│                                                                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ FRIDAY: REPORT + QUEUE (1 hour)                                         │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│ Update test tracker: status, metrics, Bayesian prob, days running       │
│ Document learnings and surprises                                        │
│ Queue top 3 for next week (pre-check: segments, conflicts, deps)        │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### Patri's Targeting Decision Tree

```
Start
  │
  ▼
AT_RISK spike this week? (>10% WoW growth)
  ├─ YES → Priority: AT_RISK retention test
  ├─ NO ──▶ Test at SHIP criteria with >€5K impact?
  │           ├─ YES → Roll out shipped test
  │           ├─ NO ──▶ DEPOSITED_ONLY alert active? (population growing)
  │                       ├─ YES → Priority: DEPOSITED_ONLY conversion test
  │                       ├─ NO ──▶ Pick highest ICE from backlog
  │                                   ├─ Conflicts with running test? → Next ICE
  │                                   ├─ No conflict → Run this test
  ▼
Capacity check: can team build + launch this week?
  ├─ YES → Proceed
  ├─ NO → Defer, document in backlog
```

### Campaign Conflict Resolution

```sql
-- Detect conflicts before launch
SELECT
    t1.test_id AS proposed_test,
    t2.test_id AS running_test,
    COUNT(DISTINCT ta1.user_id) AS overlap_users,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT ta1.user_id),
        LEAST(t1.sample_size, t2.sample_size)
    ) AS overlap_pct
FROM test_assignments ta1
JOIN test_assignments ta2 ON ta1.user_id = ta2.user_id
    AND ta2.test_id != ta1.test_id AND ta2.status = 'RUNNING'
JOIN tests t1 ON ta1.test_id = t1.test_id
JOIN tests t2 ON ta2.test_id = t2.test_id
WHERE ta1.test_id = @proposed_test_id
GROUP BY t1.test_id, t2.test_id
HAVING overlap_pct > 0.10
```

| Overlap % | Resolution |
|-----------|-----------|
| <10% | Acceptable. Run both. |
| 10-30% | Exclude overlapping users from NEWER test. |
| >30% | Queue lower-ICE test for after higher-ICE completes. |

## 7.8 Test Proposals (12 Fully Specified Test Cards)

### Test #001: DCA Setup Nudge at D7 Post-FM

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we send a push at D7 post-FM suggesting €25/week DCA in FM asset,
   THEN DCA setup rate increases 50% (4% → 6%),
   BECAUSE commitment/consistency (BE3): small recurring buy extends initial commitment.

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   Coinbase recurring buy prompt D3-D7: 15-20% of DCA activations.
   Robinhood recurring investment nudge: 2-3x adoption vs no nudge.
   (Phase 9: Coinbase One subscription bundles DCA with zero-fee trading.)

3. METRICS
   Primary: Tasa de Activación DCA (DCA setup rate within 14d) [catalog: DCA metrics]
   Secondary: D30 retention (R1), Revenue D30, Second product adoption (X1)
   Guardrail: Unsubscribe rate (must not increase >1pp)

4. SEGMENTS
   Include: FIRST_MONETIZATION stage, D7 post-FM, fm_product = 'brokerage'
   Exclude: Active DCA, B2B, is_holdout, in other running test

5. CONTROL vs VARIANT
   Control: No message at D7 (next message at D14)
   Variant A: Push — "Tu primera compra fue solo el inicio. Activa compra recurrente
              de €25/semana y construye tu cartera en automático."
   Variant B: Push + in-app card — Same copy + persistent card 48h

6. EXPECTED IMPACT
   Conservative: 200 DCA/month × €100/mo × 1.5% = €300/month
   Base: 400 DCA = €600/month + retention premium (DCA users: 2-3x D90)
   Optimistic: 600 DCA = €900/month

7. ICE: Impact 8, Confidence 7, Ease 9 = 504

8. DEPENDENCIES
   Eng: No. Data: DCA setup event in CleverTap (⚠️ P0 verify per Chunk 2 v1.1).
   Legal: No. Design: In-app card (Variant B).

9. RUNTIME
   Method: Bayesian A/B (3 arms). Population: ~5,000-8,000/month (ES).
   Sample: 15%/variant (~750-1,200/arm). MDE: 2pp. Duration: 3 weeks.
```

### Test #002: Earn Cross-Sell for Idle Balance (Loss Aversion Frame)

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we send a push to ACTIVE users with idle balance >€500 (no Earn deposit)
   framing as lost yield,
   THEN Earn deposit rate increases 30% (8% → 10.4%),
   BECAUSE loss aversion (BE1): "missing" yield is 2x more motivating than "earning."

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   Revolut savings vault suggestion: 15-25% conversion.
   Crypto.com Earn prompt: 12-18% adoption.
   (Phase 9: Crypto.com Earn up to 14.5% APY, aggressive staking promotion.)

3. METRICS
   Primary: Earn deposit rate within 14d. Secondary: AUC increase (AUC2), L7 density.
   Guardrail: Brokerage activity (no cannibalization).

4. SEGMENTS
   Include: ACTIVE, balance > €500, earn_balance = 0, not Earn TRIED.
   Exclude: B2B, is_holdout, running test.

5. CONTROL vs VARIANT
   Control: No message.
   Variant A (Gain): "Tu balance está listo. Deposita en Earn, genera hasta {rate}% anual."
   Variant B (Loss): "Estás perdiendo ~€{X}/año. Tu €{balance} podría generar yield ahora."

6. EXPECTED IMPACT
   Conservative: 150 deposits × €2K × 4% yield × margin = €360/month
   Base: 300 = €720/month. Optimistic: 500 = €1,200/month.

7. ICE: Impact 7, Confidence 8, Ease 8 = 448

8. DEPENDENCIES
   Eng: No. Data: idle_balance calc (balance minus Earn/Staking). Legal: "hasta" language. Design: No.

9. RUNTIME
   Bayesian A/B (3 arms). 15%/variant. MDE: 2.4pp. Duration: 3-4 weeks.
```

### Test #003: Whale Reactivation Bonus (DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE)

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we send personalized email to DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE (>€5K, 90-365d dormant)
   with €10 trading credit,
   THEN reactivation rate doubles (2% → 4%),
   BECAUSE reciprocity (BE11) + sunk cost (BE10).

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   Coinbase $10 reactivation credit: 3-5x reactivation vs no incentive.
   Binance fee rebate for returning traders: significant volume recovery.
   (Phase 9: Coinbase reactivation leverages One subscription free trial.)

3. METRICS
   Primary: Reactivation rate 30d (R3). Secondary: Revenue D30, R5 quality.
   Guardrail: Cost per reactivation < €25.

4. SEGMENTS
   Include: DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE, balance > €5K, days_dormant 90-365.
   Exclude: balance < €5K, dormant > 365d, B2B, is_holdout.
   Track: reactivation_events table (Chunk 1 v1.1) for "Second FM" if new product.

5. CONTROL vs VARIANT
   Control: No message.
   Variant A: Email — "Hola {name}, tu cartera de €{balance} sigue aquí.
              Te regalamos €10 para tu próxima operación. Válido 14 días."

6. EXPECTED IMPACT
   Population: ~14K global (Salvia), ~2,000 with >€5K.
   Conservative: 40 reactivations × €200 = €8K/month. Cost: €400.
   Base: 80 × €200 = €16K/month. Cost: €800. ROI: 20x.
   Optimistic: 120 × €300 = €36K/month.

7. ICE: Impact 9, Confidence 7, Ease 7 = 441

8. DEPENDENCIES
   Eng: Trading credit mechanism. Data: DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE + balance.
   Legal: Credit T&C. Design: Email template.

9. RUNTIME
   Group Sequential (small population). Full 50/50. MDE: 2pp. Duration: 2-3 weeks.
```

### Test #004: KYC Urgency via Launchpad Scarcity

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we send D3 push to REGISTERED_ONLY with scarcity ("Solo quedan plazas
   para Launchpad este mes"),
   THEN KYC completion rate increases 15% relative,
   BECAUSE scarcity (BE5): limited Launchpad access creates urgency.

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   OKX Jumpstart: KYC spike before launches.
   Binance Launchpad: drives KYC specifically.
   (Phase 9: Binance Launchpool and Megadrop drive similar behavior.)

3. METRICS
   Primary: KYC completion rate 7d. Secondary: Time-to-KYC, FM rate of nudged users.
   Guardrail: KYC abandonment mid-flow.

4. SEGMENTS: REGISTERED_ONLY, D3 post-registration, email verified.
   Exclude: KYC in progress, B2B, is_holdout.

5. CONTROL: Standard onboarding emails.
   Variant A: Push — "Completa tu verificación y accede a los próximos lanzamientos."

6. EXPECTED IMPACT
   Pop: ~5,000 D3 reg-not-KYC/month (ES).
   Conservative: 250 KYC × 40% FM = 100 × €50 = €5K/month.
   Base: 375 KYC × 40% = 150 FM = €7.5K. Optimistic: €10K.

7. ICE: 7 × 6 × 9 = 378

8. DEPENDENCIES
   Legal: Scarcity claim must be truthful. If no Launchpad cap, cannot use "plazas limitadas." VERIFY.

9. Bayesian A/B. 15%/variant. MDE: 5pp (ES baseline 68% Reg→KYC). 3 weeks.
```

### Test #005: Card Cashback Reminder (Card PRODUCT_CHURNED)

```
1. HYPOTHESIS

6. Impact
   Conservative: 50 reactivations × €200/mo spend × 0.5% = €50/month.
   Base: 100 = €100. Optimistic: 200 = €200.
   NOTE: Real value = account retention (Card is stickiest daily touchpoint).

7. ICE: 5 × 7 × 9 = 315

8. Data: Accumulated cashback per user in CleverTap. VERIFY.

9. Bayesian A/B. 20%/variant. MDE: 3pp. 3-4 weeks.
```

### Test #007: Default DCA Amount During Onboarding

```
   Organ donation opt-in studies: 85-90% acceptance (Johnson & Goldstein, 2003).
   (Phase 9: Coinbase One bundles recurring buy into subscription.)

   Guardrail: Onboarding completion rate (no confusion).
```

### Test #008: AT_RISK FOMO Push (Market Momentum Trigger)

```
1. HYPOTHESIS

   BECAUSE FOMO (BE8): 84% of crypto holders report FOMO decisions.

   Coinbase price alerts: 3-5x login rate during movements.
   Robinhood volatile market push: significant DAU spikes.
   (Phase 9: OKX real-time alerts drive engagement.)

   Guardrail: Unsubscribe rate, complaint rate (FOMO can feel manipulative).

4. Include: AT_RISK, trigger = activity_decline (health_score recency < 10).
   Exclude: B2B, holdout, pushed in last 48h. Only triggered when btc_7d > +5%.

5. Control: No message. Variant A: "BTC ha subido un {X}% esta semana.
   Tu cartera también se mueve."

6. AT_RISK pop: 8,000-15,000. Trigger: ~2-3x/month neutral market.
   Conservative: 200 recoveries × €150 = €30K.
   Base: 400 = €60K. Optimistic: 600 = €90K.

7. ICE: 9 × 6 × 6 = 324

8. Eng: Market trigger in CleverTap (BTC API → webhook). Legal: No "buy" language. VERIFY.

9. Bayesian A/B. 20%/variant. MDE: 3pp. 4-6 weeks (trigger-dependent).
```

```
   Conservative: €735/month. Base: €1,100. Optimistic: €1,840.

9. Bayesian A/B (3 arms). 33%/variant. MDE: €15 increase. 3 weeks.
```

### Test #010: B2M Tier-Up Nudge for Single-Product ACTIVE

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we push single-product ACTIVE users about Space Center tier benefits
   they're 1 tier away from,
   THEN B2M purchase rate increases 25% and cross-product adoption 10%,
   BECAUSE commitment/consistency (BE3) + goal-gradient effect.

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   Crypto.com CRO tier prompts: 20-30% of upgrades from nudges.
   Binance VIP proximity: volume increase near next tier.
   (Phase 9: Binance VIP has 9 tiers. Crypto.com 6 tiers with clear reward escalation.)

3. Primary: B2M purchase rate 14d. Secondary: Tier upgrade, X1 cross-sell, Revenue D30.
   Guardrail: Brokerage volume (B2M must not replace other trading).

4. Include: ACTIVE, products_with_fm = 1, Space Center tier 0-2, no B2M.
   Exclude: B2B, holdout, POWER_USER.

5. Control: No message. Variant A: "Estás a {X} B2M de Tier {next}. Compra B2M
   y desbloquea tu descuento."

6. Pop: REQUIRES DATA (est. 10K-20K). Conservative: €500. Base: €1K. Optimistic: €2K.
   Real value = switching cost increase.

7. ICE: 7 × 6 × 7 = 294

8. Data: Space Center tier + B2M balance + distance to next tier. VERIFY in CleverTap.

9. Bayesian A/B. 10%/variant. MDE: 2pp. 3-4 weeks.
```

### Test #011: DEPOSITED_ONLY Conversion Push (48h trigger)

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we push DEPOSITED_ONLY users within 48h of first deposit with guided
   first-buy CTA,
   THEN Deposit→FM rate increases by 20% relative,
   BECAUSE commitment/consistency (BE3): they already committed money; a guided
   next step reduces the friction to complete the action.

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   Revolut first investment prompt post-deposit: high conversion.
   (Phase 9: Bitpanda Savings Plan prompt after deposit drives DCA setup.)

3. METRICS
   Primary: Deposit→FM rate 7d. Secondary: Time deposit-to-FM (A11), FM revenue (M2).
   Guardrail: Withdrawal rate (push must not trigger "second thoughts").

4. SEGMENTS
   Include: DEPOSITED_ONLY, deposit within last 48h, Spain B2C.
   Exclude: B2B, holdout, running test.

5. Control: Standard lifecycle (no specific DEPOSITED_ONLY trigger).
   Variant A: Push — "Tu €{deposit} está listo. Compra tu primer crypto en 30 segundos."
   with deep link to simplified buy screen.

6. EXPECTED IMPACT
   Pop: REQUIRES DATA (est. 500-1,500/month from Chunk 1 v1.1 analysis).
   Conservative: 75 additional FM × €50 = €3,750/month.
   Base: 150 FM = €7,500. Optimistic: 225 FM = €11,250.

7. ICE: 8 × 7 × 8 = 448

8. Eng: No (push + deep link). Data: DEPOSITED_ONLY real-time segment in CleverTap (P0 event "Deposit_No_Purchase"). Legal: No.

9. Bayesian A/B. 20%/variant (small pop, need adequate sample). MDE: 5pp. 3-4 weeks.
```

### Test #012: Portugal Localization + Social Proof (GTM Convergence)

```
1. HYPOTHESIS
   IF we send PT-specific onboarding emails in native Portuguese (not translated
   Spanish) with PT-specific social proof ("2,056 portugueses verificados em 2025"),
   THEN PT Reg→KYC rate increases from 39% toward ES benchmark of 60%,
   BECAUSE social proof (BE4) + friction reduction (localization).

2. COMPETITOR EVIDENCE
   (Phase 9: Bitpanda localized in 15+ languages with local payment methods.
   Revolut's localized onboarding achieves consistent conversion across markets.)

3. METRICS
   Primary: PT Reg→KYC rate (A9 by geo). Secondary: PT KYC→FM rate, email drop rate.
   Guardrail: PT registration rate (localized email must not deter).

4. Include: REGISTERED_ONLY, geography = 'PT'. Exclude: holdout.

5. Control: Current PT emails (translated Spanish template).
   Variant A: Native Portuguese copy + PT social proof counter.

6. Pop: ~437/month PT registrations (5,248/year ÷ 12).
   Conservative: 20 additional KYC × 20% FM = 4 × €50 = €200/month.
   Base: 40 KYC = 8 FM = €400. Optimistic: 60 KYC = 12 FM = €600.
   NOTE: Small absolute impact but critical for PT convergence target (Chunk 2 v1.1).

7. ICE: 5 × 6 × 8 = 240

8. Eng: No. Data: PT-specific stats. Legal: No. Design: Email template.

9. Bayesian A/B. 50%/variant (small pop). MDE: 8pp. 4-6 weeks.
```

# CHUNK 4: Data Infrastructure + Execution Roadmap
## Growth Operating System — Bit2Me

**Version:** 1.1 — Chunk 4 of 4 (built on Chunks 1-3 v1.1)

**Author:** Head of Growth (Daniel)

### v1.1 Notes (alignment with Chunks 1-3 v1.1)
- All BigQuery views reference the reconciled lifecycle classifier from Chunk 2 v1.1 (11 stages + EXCLUDED).
- state_transition_history table (Chunk 2 v1.1 Stage 8) is a P0 view dependency, not P1.
- health_score (Chunk 1 v1.1) requires daily computation; included in user_daily_snapshot.
- POWER_USER monthly threshold stored in monthly_thresholds config table (Chunk 2 v1.1).
- DCA data availability flagged as P0 blocker for views 1, 2, and test infrastructure.
- Card metrics CD1-CD7 and AUC metrics AUC1-AUC5 (Chunk 2 v1.1) require dedicated data joins.
- Portugal as separate geo dimension in all views and dashboards.
- Academy attribution gap (Chunk 1 v1.1) included as P0 data request.
- Reactivation event table (Chunk 1 v1.1) is a new table to create, not just a view.
- Competitive intelligence (Phase 9 separate document) informs benchmark targets in roadmap.
- 12 test cards from Chunk 3 v1.1 drive the testing sprint sequence.

# PHASE 8: DATA INFRASTRUCTURE (The Plumbing)

## 8.1 Current State Audit

### What Exists Today (Qlik, Available Now)

| Report | What It Contains | Growth Use | Gaps |
|--------|-----------------|-----------|------|
| **Qlik Acquisition Dashboard** | Registrations, verifications, funnels by channel/geo | FM tracking (Brokerage only), CAC calculation, funnel drop-off | No cross-product FM. No EMA logic. Brokerage-centric. |
| **Qlik Transaction Attribution** | Revenue by channel, product, region, B2C/B2B | Revenue split, channel ROAS, product revenue | 7-day push attribution window (overcounts CRM). No W-shaped model. |
| **Qlik Revenue per Product** | Product-level revenue | Product contribution tracking | No per-user granularity. No lifecycle stage mapping. |
| **Qlik Clusters per Product** | Cluster analysis per product (new, 2026) | Salvia's per-product segmentation (C0-C9 Brokerage, etc.) | One table per product. Not unified. No cross-product view. |
| **Qlik Geo Report** | Country/region breakdown | Geo performance comparison | No per-user lifecycle mapping. Aggregate only. |

### What Does NOT Exist

| Gap | Impact | Priority |
|-----|--------|----------|
| Cross-product FM (EMA) view | Cannot calculate MMU, activation rate across products. Council Metric 1 and 2 blocked. | P0 |
| User lifecycle stage classifier | Cannot segment by lifecycle stage. All lifecycle reporting blocked. | P0 |
| User daily snapshot | No historical tracking of user state. No Sankey flows, no cohort retention. | P0 |
| state_transition_history | REACTIVATED classifier blocked. Sankey dashboard blocked. Transition rate metrics blocked. | P0 |
| Unified cluster table | Cross-product analysis blocked. Archetype classifier incomplete. | P0 |
| DCA / recurring_orders table | DCA penetration metric (X5), DCA as health_score component, DCA test cards blocked. | P0 |
| Academy user linking | Academy attribution gap (Chunk 1 v1.1). acquisition_source = 'academy' field unreliable. | P0 |
| Balance snapshots by product | AUC metrics AUC1-AUC5 blocked. Idle balance calculation blocked. | P1 |
| Card transaction history per user | Card metrics CD1-CD7 blocked. Card dashboard blocked. | P1 |
| Churn prediction model | Proactive retention blocked. Month 3 target. | P3 |
