---

### Pre-requisite: Foundation Tables (V0)

Before any view can run, three foundation objects must exist.

#### V0a: user_fm (First Monetization per User)

**Purpose:** Calculate EMA (First Economically Meaningful Action) per user across all products.
**Priority:** P0
**SQL Complexity:** High
**Refresh:** Daily (incremental; only new FM events)

```sql
-- V0a: user_fm — One row per user. Their first qualifying monetization event.
-- Implements Chunk 1 v1.1 Section 1.1, Candidate 4 (EMA).
-- Threshold: €0.50 revenue per event.

CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.user_fm AS

WITH all_fm_candidates AS (
    -- Brokerage/Pro: first trade with commission > €0.50
    SELECT user_id, trade_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'brokerage' AS fm_product,
           commission_eur AS fm_revenue
    FROM `project.dataset.trades`
    WHERE status = 'completed'
      AND commission_eur > 0.50

    UNION ALL

    -- Earn: first deposit where projected 30d yield > €0.50
    -- CRITICAL (Chunk 1 v1.1): use annual_yield_rate_at_deposit, NOT live rate.
    SELECT user_id, deposit_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'earn' AS fm_product,
           deposit_amount_eur * annual_yield_rate_at_deposit / 12 AS fm_revenue
    FROM `project.dataset.earn_deposits`
    WHERE status = 'completed'
      AND deposit_amount_eur * annual_yield_rate_at_deposit / 12 > 0.50

    UNION ALL

    -- Card: first interchange-generating transaction
    SELECT user_id, tx_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'card' AS fm_product,
           interchange_eur AS fm_revenue
    FROM `project.dataset.card_transactions`
    WHERE status = 'completed'
      AND interchange_eur > 0

    UNION ALL

    -- Loan: first loan origination (any origination generates interest revenue)
    SELECT user_id, origination_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'loan' AS fm_product,
           origination_fee_eur AS fm_revenue  -- TBD: confirm fee field name
    FROM `project.dataset.loans`
    WHERE status = 'originated'

    UNION ALL

    -- Staking: first stake where projected 30d reward > €0.50
    SELECT user_id, stake_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'staking' AS fm_product,
           stake_amount_eur * annual_reward_rate / 12 AS fm_revenue
    FROM `project.dataset.staking_positions`
    WHERE status = 'active'
      AND stake_amount_eur * annual_reward_rate / 12 > 0.50

    UNION ALL

    -- Launchpad: first participation
    SELECT user_id, participation_timestamp AS event_timestamp, 'launchpad' AS fm_product,
           allocation_eur AS fm_revenue  -- TBD: confirm revenue field
    FROM `project.dataset.launchpad_participations`
    WHERE status = 'completed'
),
ranked AS (
    SELECT *,
           ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY user_id ORDER BY event_timestamp ASC) AS rn
    FROM all_fm_candidates
)
SELECT
    user_id,
    event_timestamp AS fm_date,
    fm_product,
    fm_revenue AS fm_revenue_eur,
    DATE_DIFF(event_timestamp, u.registration_date, DAY) AS days_reg_to_fm,
    u.acquisition_channel,
    u.geography
FROM ranked r
JOIN `project.dataset.users` u ON r.user_id = u.user_id
WHERE rn = 1
```

**⚠️ DATA DEPENDENCIES:**
- `earn_deposits.annual_yield_rate_at_deposit`: Must be snapshot at deposit time. If this column doesn't exist, join to `earn_rate_history(product, date)`. Confirm with Data Team.
- `loans.origination_fee_eur`: Field name TBD. Loan revenue model (interest vs. origination fee) needs clarification.
- `staking_positions.annual_reward_rate`: Field name TBD. Confirm table structure.
- `launchpad_participations`: Confirm table exists and structure.

#### V0b: monthly_revenue (User-Level Monthly Revenue)

**Purpose:** Aggregate revenue per user per month across all products. Foundation for NRR, LTV, cohort curves.
**Priority:** P0
**Refresh:** Daily (append current month, recalculate last month for late-arriving events)

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.monthly_revenue AS

SELECT
    user_id,
    DATE_TRUNC(event_date, MONTH) AS revenue_month,

    -- Transactional revenue
    SUM(CASE WHEN product IN ('brokerage', 'pro') THEN commission_eur ELSE 0 END) AS brokerage_revenue,
    SUM(CASE WHEN product = 'card' THEN interchange_eur ELSE 0 END) AS card_revenue,

    -- Recurring revenue
    SUM(CASE WHEN product = 'earn' THEN yield_spread_eur ELSE 0 END) AS earn_revenue,
    SUM(CASE WHEN product = 'staking' THEN staking_commission_eur ELSE 0 END) AS staking_revenue,
    SUM(CASE WHEN product = 'loan' THEN interest_revenue_eur ELSE 0 END) AS loan_revenue,

    -- Launchpad / other
    SUM(CASE WHEN product = 'launchpad' THEN launchpad_revenue_eur ELSE 0 END) AS launchpad_revenue,

    -- Totals
    SUM(revenue_eur) AS total_revenue,
    SUM(CASE WHEN product IN ('earn', 'staking', 'loan') THEN revenue_eur ELSE 0 END) AS recurring_revenue,
    SUM(CASE WHEN product IN ('brokerage', 'pro', 'card', 'launchpad') THEN revenue_eur ELSE 0 END) AS transactional_revenue,

    -- Product count
    COUNT(DISTINCT product) AS products_generating_revenue

FROM `project.dataset.revenue_events`
WHERE revenue_eur > 0
GROUP BY user_id, DATE_TRUNC(event_date, MONTH)
```

**⚠️ DATA DEPENDENCY:** The `revenue_events` table must be a unified table or view that captures ALL revenue-generating events across products with a consistent schema: `user_id, event_date, product, revenue_eur, revenue_type`. If this doesn't exist, this view must UNION ALL from per-product revenue tables. Confirm structure with Data Team.

#### V0c: monthly_thresholds (Configuration Table)

**Purpose:** Store POWER_USER revenue threshold (p75) calculated monthly. Prevents daily threshold oscillation (Chunk 2 v1.1).
**Priority:** P0
**Refresh:** Monthly (1st of each month via scheduled query)

```sql
-- Scheduled query: runs on 1st of each month
-- Calculates and stores the p75 revenue threshold for POWER_USER classification.

INSERT INTO `project.dataset.monthly_thresholds` (month, metric, value, calculated_at)
SELECT
    DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), MONTH) AS month,
    'power_user_revenue_p75' AS metric,
    PERCENTILE_CONT(total_revenue, 0.75) OVER () AS value,
    CURRENT_TIMESTAMP() AS calculated_at
FROM growth.monthly_revenue
WHERE revenue_month = DATE_SUB(DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), MONTH), INTERVAL 1 MONTH)
  AND total_revenue > 0
```

---

### View 1: user_lifecycle_stage

**Purpose:** Classify every user into one of 11 lifecycle stages (+ EXCLUDED). The master view.
**Priority:** P0
**SQL Complexity:** High
**Refresh:** Daily
**Dependencies:** V0a (user_fm), V0b (monthly_revenue), V0c (monthly_thresholds), state_transition_history table

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.user_lifecycle_stage AS

WITH user_signals AS (
    SELECT
        u.user_id,
        u.account_status,
        u.registration_date,
        u.kyc_status,
        u.kyc_approved_date,
        u.acquisition_channel,
        u.geography,
        u.segment,  -- B2C / B2B

        -- FM data
        fm.fm_date,
        fm.fm_product,
        DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), fm.fm_date, DAY) AS days_since_fm,

        -- Balance
        COALESCE(b.total_balance_eur, 0) AS total_balance_eur,
        COALESCE(b.earn_balance_eur, 0) AS earn_balance_eur,

        -- Deposit data
        COALESCE(d.total_deposits, 0) AS total_deposits,
        d.first_deposit_date,

        -- Activity signals
        DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) AS days_since_last_monetizable_action,
        DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_login_date, DAY) AS days_since_last_login,
        DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_activity_date, DAY) AS days_since_last_activity,

        -- Revenue signals (current month + trailing)
        COALESCE(mr.total_revenue, 0) AS monthly_revenue_eur,
        COALESCE(mr.products_generating_revenue, 0) AS products_with_fm,

        -- Economic activity flag (Chunk 1 v1.1, Section 1.3)
        CASE WHEN (
            mr.brokerage_revenue > 0
            OR mr.card_revenue > 0
            OR mr.earn_revenue > 0
            OR mr.staking_revenue > 0
            OR mr.loan_revenue > 0
            OR mr.launchpad_revenue > 0
            OR dca.has_active_dca = TRUE
        ) THEN TRUE ELSE FALSE END AS is_economically_active,

        -- Behavioral activity flag
        CASE WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_login_date, DAY) <= 30
        THEN TRUE ELSE FALSE END AS is_behaviorally_active,

        -- Health score (Chunk 1 v1.1, Section 1.2)
        (
            CASE
                WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 7 THEN 30
                WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 14 THEN 25
                WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 30 THEN 20
                WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 60 THEN 10
                ELSE 0
            END
            + CASE
                WHEN a.activity_ratio_4w_vs_prior_4w >= 1.0 THEN 25
                WHEN a.activity_ratio_4w_vs_prior_4w >= 0.5 THEN 15
                WHEN a.activity_ratio_4w_vs_prior_4w > 0 THEN 5
                ELSE 0
            END
            + CASE
                WHEN b.balance_change_30d_pct > 0 THEN 20
                WHEN b.balance_change_30d_pct >= -0.1 THEN 15
                WHEN b.balance_change_30d_pct >= -0.5 THEN 5
                ELSE 0
            END
            + CASE
                WHEN a.products_with_activity_30d >= 3 THEN 15
                WHEN a.products_with_activity_30d = 2 THEN 10
                WHEN a.products_with_activity_30d = 1 THEN 5
                ELSE 0
            END
            + CASE WHEN dca.has_active_dca = TRUE THEN 5 ELSE 0 END
            + CASE WHEN sc.space_center_tier >= 2 THEN 5
                   WHEN sc.space_center_tier = 1 THEN 3
                   ELSE 0 END
        ) AS health_score,

        -- Activity decline
        a.activity_decline_4w_pct,

        -- DCA signals
        COALESCE(dca.has_active_dca, FALSE) AS has_active_dca,
        COALESCE(dca.dca_cancelled_recently, FALSE) AS dca_cancelled_recently,

        -- Earn withdrawal signal
        COALESCE(b.earn_withdrawal_30d_pct, 0) AS earn_withdrawal_30d_pct,

        -- Space Center
        COALESCE(sc.space_center_tier, 0) AS space_center_tier,

        -- Previous status (for REACTIVATED classification)
        sth.from_stage AS previous_status,
        sth.transition_date AS reactivation_event_date,
        DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), sth.transition_date, DAY) AS days_since_reactivation_event,

        -- Market condition (Chunk 1 v1.1)
        mkt.market_condition,
        mkt.btc_30d_return,
        mkt.volatility_flag,

        -- POWER_USER threshold for current month
        pt.value AS revenue_p75_threshold,

        -- Previous day status (for stability rule)
        prev.lifecycle_stage AS previous_day_stage

    FROM `project.dataset.users` u
    LEFT JOIN growth.user_fm fm ON u.user_id = fm.user_id
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.user_balances_latest` b ON u.user_id = b.user_id
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.user_deposits_summary` d ON u.user_id = d.user_id
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.user_activity_signals` a ON u.user_id = a.user_id
    LEFT JOIN growth.monthly_revenue mr
        ON u.user_id = mr.user_id
        AND mr.revenue_month = DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), MONTH)
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.user_dca_status` dca ON u.user_id = dca.user_id
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.space_center_tiers` sc ON u.user_id = sc.user_id
    LEFT JOIN (
        -- Most recent transition INTO a reactivation-eligible state
        SELECT user_id, from_stage, transition_date,
               ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY user_id ORDER BY transition_date DESC) AS rn
        FROM `project.dataset.state_transition_history`
        WHERE to_stage = 'REACTIVATED'
    ) sth ON u.user_id = sth.user_id AND sth.rn = 1
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.market_condition_daily` mkt ON mkt.date = CURRENT_DATE()
    LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.monthly_thresholds` pt
        ON pt.month = DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), MONTH)
        AND pt.metric = 'power_user_revenue_p75'
    LEFT JOIN growth.user_daily_snapshot prev
        ON u.user_id = prev.user_id
        AND prev.snapshot_date = DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL 1 DAY)
)
SELECT
    user_id,
    CASE
        -- Stage 0: EXCLUDED
        WHEN account_status IN ('banned', 'disabled') THEN 'EXCLUDED'

        -- Stage 11: CHURNED
        WHEN days_since_last_activity > 180
             AND total_balance_eur = 0
             AND days_since_last_login > 180
        THEN 'CHURNED'

        -- Stage 10: DORMANT_ZERO
        WHEN days_since_last_monetizable_action > 90
             AND total_balance_eur = 0
             AND NOT (days_since_last_activity > 180 AND days_since_last_login > 180)
        THEN 'DORMANT_ZERO'

        -- Stage 9: DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE
        WHEN days_since_last_monetizable_action > 90
             AND total_balance_eur > 0
        THEN 'DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE'

        -- Stage 8: REACTIVATED (temporary 30d)
        WHEN previous_status IN ('DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE', 'DORMANT_ZERO', 'CHURNED')
             AND days_since_reactivation_event <= 30
             AND is_economically_active = TRUE
        THEN 'REACTIVATED'

        -- Stage 7: AT_RISK
        WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
             AND days_since_last_monetizable_action <= 90
             AND (
                 activity_decline_4w_pct >= 50
                 OR health_score < 30
                 OR dca_cancelled_recently = TRUE
                 OR (earn_withdrawal_30d_pct > 0.5 AND earn_balance_eur > 0)
             )
        THEN 'AT_RISK'

        -- Stage 6: POWER_USER (monthly threshold, 30d stability)
        WHEN is_economically_active = TRUE
             AND days_since_fm > 30
             AND products_with_fm >= 2
             AND (
                 monthly_revenue_eur > revenue_p75_threshold
                 OR space_center_tier >= 3
                 -- Stability: retain POWER_USER for 30 days even if revenue dips
                 OR (previous_day_stage = 'POWER_USER'
                     AND monthly_revenue_eur > revenue_p75_threshold * 0.5)
             )
        THEN 'POWER_USER'

        -- Stage 5: ACTIVE
        WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
             AND days_since_fm > 30
             AND is_economically_active = TRUE
        THEN 'ACTIVE'

        -- Stage 4: FIRST_MONETIZATION
        WHEN fm_date IS NOT NULL
             AND days_since_fm <= 30
        THEN 'FIRST_MONETIZATION'

        -- Stage 3: DEPOSITED_ONLY
        WHEN total_deposits > 0
             AND fm_date IS NULL
        THEN 'DEPOSITED_ONLY'

        -- Stage 2: KYC_COMPLETE
        WHEN kyc_status = 'approved'
             AND total_deposits = 0
             AND fm_date IS NULL
        THEN 'KYC_COMPLETE'

        -- Stage 1: REGISTERED_ONLY
        WHEN kyc_status != 'approved'
        THEN 'REGISTERED_ONLY'

        ELSE 'UNCLASSIFIED'
    END AS lifecycle_stage,

    -- All context fields for downstream views
    geography,
    segment,
    acquisition_channel,
    fm_date,
    fm_product,
    days_since_fm,
    total_balance_eur,
    monthly_revenue_eur,
    products_with_fm,
    is_economically_active,
    is_behaviorally_active,
    health_score,
    has_active_dca,
    space_center_tier,
    market_condition,
    btc_30d_return,
    volatility_flag,
    CURRENT_DATE() AS snapshot_date

FROM user_signals
WHERE account_status NOT IN ('banned', 'disabled')
```

**⚠️ SOURCE TABLE DEPENDENCIES (confirm with Data Team):**

| Table | Required Fields | Status |
|-------|----------------|--------|
| `users` | user_id, account_status, registration_date, kyc_status, kyc_approved_date, acquisition_channel, geography, segment | LIKELY EXISTS. Verify field names. |
| `user_balances_latest` | user_id, total_balance_eur, earn_balance_eur, balance_change_30d_pct, earn_withdrawal_30d_pct | REQUIRES DATA. Balance snapshot tables may exist but field names TBD. |
| `user_deposits_summary` | user_id, total_deposits, first_deposit_date | REQUIRES DATA. May need to aggregate from deposit events. |
| `user_activity_signals` | user_id, last_monetizable_action_date, last_login_date, last_activity_date, activity_ratio_4w_vs_prior_4w, activity_decline_4w_pct, products_with_activity_30d | DOES NOT EXIST. Must be created as a supporting view. |
| `user_dca_status` | user_id, has_active_dca, dca_cancelled_recently | ⚠️ P0 DEPENDENCY. recurring_orders table unconfirmed. |
| `space_center_tiers` | user_id, space_center_tier | REQUIRES DATA. Space Center API or export. |
| `state_transition_history` | user_id, from_stage, to_stage, transition_date | DOES NOT EXIST. Must create (see below). |
| `market_condition_daily` | date, market_condition, btc_30d_return, volatility_flag | DOES NOT EXIST. Must create (see below). |

---

### View 2: user_daily_snapshot

**Purpose:** Daily snapshot of every user's lifecycle stage + context. Foundation for all time-series analysis.
**Priority:** P0
**SQL Complexity:** High
**Refresh:** Daily (append-only; one row per user per day)
**Storage consideration:** ~1.2M users x 365 days = ~438M rows/year. Partition by snapshot_date. Cluster by lifecycle_stage, geography.

```sql
-- Materialized as a table (not a view) for performance.
-- Daily scheduled query appends today's snapshot.

INSERT INTO `project.dataset.user_daily_snapshot`
SELECT
    user_id,
    lifecycle_stage,
    geography,
    segment,
    acquisition_channel,
    fm_date,
    fm_product,
    total_balance_eur,
    monthly_revenue_eur,
    products_with_fm,
    is_economically_active,
    is_behaviorally_active,
    health_score,
    has_active_dca,
    space_center_tier,
    market_condition,
    volatility_flag,
    CURRENT_DATE() AS snapshot_date
FROM growth.user_lifecycle_stage
```

**Schema:**
```sql
CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.user_daily_snapshot` (
    user_id STRING,
    lifecycle_stage STRING,
    geography STRING,
    segment STRING,
    acquisition_channel STRING,
    fm_date DATE,
    fm_product STRING,
    total_balance_eur FLOAT64,
    monthly_revenue_eur FLOAT64,
    products_with_fm INT64,
    is_economically_active BOOL,
    is_behaviorally_active BOOL,
    health_score INT64,
    has_active_dca BOOL,
    space_center_tier INT64,
    market_condition STRING,
    volatility_flag STRING,
    snapshot_date DATE
)
PARTITION BY snapshot_date
CLUSTER BY lifecycle_stage, geography;
```

---

### View 3: activation_funnel

**Purpose:** Step-by-step funnel from registration to FM, with timing and drop-off rates.
**Priority:** P0
**SQL Complexity:** Medium
**Refresh:** Daily

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.activation_funnel AS

SELECT
    DATE_TRUNC(u.registration_date, WEEK) AS reg_week,
    u.geography,
    u.acquisition_channel,
    u.segment,

    -- Step 1: Registered
    COUNT(DISTINCT u.user_id) AS registered,

    -- Step 2: Email verified
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN u.email_verified = TRUE THEN u.user_id END) AS email_verified,

    -- Step 3: Phone verified
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN u.phone_verified = TRUE THEN u.user_id END) AS phone_verified,

    -- Step 4: KYC submitted
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN u.kyc_submitted = TRUE THEN u.user_id END) AS kyc_submitted,

    -- Step 5: KYC approved
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN u.kyc_status = 'approved' THEN u.user_id END) AS kyc_approved,

    -- Step 6: First deposit
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN d.first_deposit_date IS NOT NULL THEN u.user_id END) AS first_deposit,

    -- Step 7: FM (EMA)
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN u.user_id END) AS first_monetization,

    -- Conversion rates
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN u.kyc_status = 'approved' THEN u.user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT u.user_id)
    ) AS reg_to_kyc_rate,

    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN u.user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN u.kyc_status = 'approved' THEN u.user_id END)
    ) AS kyc_to_fm_rate,

    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_date IS NOT NULL THEN u.user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT u.user_id)
    ) AS reg_to_fm_rate,

    -- Timing (median days)
    APPROX_QUANTILES(
        DATE_DIFF(fm.fm_date, u.registration_date, DAY), 100
    )[OFFSET(50)] AS median_days_reg_to_fm,

    APPROX_QUANTILES(
        DATE_DIFF(u.kyc_approved_date, u.registration_date, DAY), 100
    )[OFFSET(50)] AS median_days_reg_to_kyc,

    -- FM product distribution
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_product = 'brokerage' THEN fm.user_id END) AS fm_via_brokerage,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_product = 'earn' THEN fm.user_id END) AS fm_via_earn,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_product = 'card' THEN fm.user_id END) AS fm_via_card,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_product = 'loan' THEN fm.user_id END) AS fm_via_loan,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fm.fm_product = 'staking' THEN fm.user_id END) AS fm_via_staking

FROM `project.dataset.users` u
LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.user_deposits_summary` d ON u.user_id = d.user_id
LEFT JOIN growth.user_fm fm ON u.user_id = fm.user_id
GROUP BY 1, 2, 3, 4
```

---

### View 4: stage_distribution_weekly

**Purpose:** Population per lifecycle stage per week, with deltas.
**Priority:** P0
**SQL Complexity:** Low
**Refresh:** Weekly (Monday)

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.stage_distribution_weekly AS

WITH current_week AS (
    SELECT
        lifecycle_stage,
        geography,
        segment,
        COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS population,
        SUM(total_balance_eur) AS total_balance,
        AVG(monthly_revenue_eur) AS avg_revenue_per_user
    FROM growth.user_daily_snapshot
    WHERE snapshot_date = DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), WEEK(MONDAY))
    GROUP BY 1, 2, 3
),
prior_week AS (
    SELECT
        lifecycle_stage,
        geography,
        segment,
        COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS population
    FROM growth.user_daily_snapshot
    WHERE snapshot_date = DATE_SUB(DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), WEEK(MONDAY)), INTERVAL 7 DAY)
    GROUP BY 1, 2, 3
)
SELECT
    c.lifecycle_stage,
    c.geography,
    c.segment,
    c.population,
    c.total_balance,
    c.avg_revenue_per_user,
    COALESCE(p.population, 0) AS prior_week_population,
    c.population - COALESCE(p.population, 0) AS delta,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(c.population - COALESCE(p.population, 0), p.population) AS delta_pct
FROM current_week c
LEFT JOIN prior_week p
    ON c.lifecycle_stage = p.lifecycle_stage
    AND c.geography = p.geography
    AND c.segment = p.segment
```

---

### View 5: stage_transitions_weekly

**Purpose:** Flows between stages per week. Powers Sankey diagram in Operational Dashboard.
**Priority:** P1
**SQL Complexity:** Medium
**Refresh:** Weekly
**Dependency:** user_daily_snapshot (must have at least 2 weeks of data)

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.stage_transitions_weekly AS

WITH transitions AS (
    SELECT
        today.user_id,
        prev.lifecycle_stage AS from_stage,
        today.lifecycle_stage AS to_stage,
        today.geography,
        today.segment,
        today.snapshot_date
    FROM growth.user_daily_snapshot today
    JOIN growth.user_daily_snapshot prev
        ON today.user_id = prev.user_id
        AND prev.snapshot_date = DATE_SUB(today.snapshot_date, INTERVAL 7 DAY)
    WHERE today.lifecycle_stage != prev.lifecycle_stage
      AND today.snapshot_date = DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), WEEK(MONDAY))
)
SELECT
    from_stage,
    to_stage,
    geography,
    segment,
    COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) AS users_transitioned,
    snapshot_date AS week_start
FROM transitions
GROUP BY 1, 2, 3, 4, 6
ORDER BY users_transitioned DESC
```

---

### View 6: revenue_by_stage_product

**Purpose:** Revenue breakdown by lifecycle stage and product.
**Priority:** P1
**SQL Complexity:** Medium
**Refresh:** Weekly

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.revenue_by_stage_product AS

SELECT
    ls.lifecycle_stage,
    ls.geography,
    ls.segment,
    mr.revenue_month,

    SUM(mr.brokerage_revenue) AS brokerage_revenue,
    SUM(mr.card_revenue) AS card_revenue,
    SUM(mr.earn_revenue) AS earn_revenue,
    SUM(mr.staking_revenue) AS staking_revenue,
    SUM(mr.loan_revenue) AS loan_revenue,
    SUM(mr.launchpad_revenue) AS launchpad_revenue,
    SUM(mr.total_revenue) AS total_revenue,
    SUM(mr.recurring_revenue) AS recurring_revenue,
    SUM(mr.transactional_revenue) AS transactional_revenue,

    COUNT(DISTINCT ls.user_id) AS user_count,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(mr.total_revenue), COUNT(DISTINCT ls.user_id)) AS arpu

FROM growth.user_lifecycle_stage ls
JOIN growth.monthly_revenue mr
    ON ls.user_id = mr.user_id
    AND mr.revenue_month = DATE_TRUNC(CURRENT_DATE(), MONTH)
GROUP BY 1, 2, 3, 4
```

### View 7: ab_test_results

**Purpose:** Test results with Bayesian probability calculation.
**Priority:** P1
**SQL Complexity:** High
**Refresh:** Daily (for running tests)

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.ab_test_results AS

SELECT
    t.test_id,
    t.test_name,
    t.start_date,
    t.status,  -- 'building', 'running', 'reading', 'shipped', 'killed'
    t.primary_metric,
    t.segment_targeted,

    -- Control metrics
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' THEN e.user_id END) AS control_users,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END) AS control_conversions,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' THEN e.user_id END)
    ) AS control_rate,
    SUM(CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' THEN e.revenue_attributed ELSE 0 END) AS control_revenue,

    -- Treatment metrics
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' THEN e.user_id END) AS treatment_users,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END) AS treatment_conversions,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END),
        COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' THEN e.user_id END)
    ) AS treatment_rate,
    SUM(CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' THEN e.revenue_attributed ELSE 0 END) AS treatment_revenue,

    -- Lift
    SAFE_DIVIDE(
        SAFE_DIVIDE(
            COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END),
            COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'treatment' THEN e.user_id END)
        ) -
        SAFE_DIVIDE(
            COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END),
            COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' THEN e.user_id END)
        ),
        SAFE_DIVIDE(
            COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' AND e.converted = TRUE THEN e.user_id END),
            COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN e.variant = 'control' THEN e.user_id END)
        )
    ) AS relative_lift,

    -- Runtime
    DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), t.start_date, DAY) AS days_running,

    -- Guardrail
    t.guardrail_metric,
    t.guardrail_threshold

    -- NOTE: Bayesian probability calculation requires UDF or Python post-processing.
    -- BigQuery SQL cannot natively compute Beta distribution posteriors.
    -- Options: (a) UDF in JavaScript, (b) Python script, (c) Looker Studio calculated field.
    -- Recommend: Python post-processing script that reads this view and appends bayesian_probability.

FROM `project.dataset.ab_tests` t
JOIN `project.dataset.ab_test_enrollments` e ON t.test_id = e.test_id
GROUP BY 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, t.guardrail_metric, t.guardrail_threshold
```

**⚠️ TABLE DEPENDENCIES:**
- `ab_tests`: Master test table. Must create. Schema: test_id, test_name, start_date, end_date, status, primary_metric, segment_targeted, guardrail_metric, guardrail_threshold.
- `ab_test_enrollments`: User enrollment table. Must create. Schema: test_id, user_id, variant, enrolled_date, converted, conversion_date, revenue_attributed.
- Bayesian probability: Cannot be computed natively in BigQuery SQL. Requires post-processing.

---

### View 8: reactivation_targets

**Purpose:** Dormant users ranked by reactivation probability.
**Priority:** P1
**SQL Complexity:** Medium
**Refresh:** Weekly

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.reactivation_targets AS

SELECT
    ls.user_id,
    ls.lifecycle_stage,
    ls.geography,
    ls.total_balance_eur,
    ls.space_center_tier,
    ls.fm_product AS last_active_product,

    DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) AS days_dormant,

    -- Reactivation probability score (heuristic, not ML)
    (
        -- Balance signal (0-40 points)
        CASE
            WHEN ls.total_balance_eur > 10000 THEN 40
            WHEN ls.total_balance_eur > 1000 THEN 30
            WHEN ls.total_balance_eur > 100 THEN 20
            WHEN ls.total_balance_eur > 0 THEN 10
            ELSE 0
        END
        -- Dormancy recency (0-30 points)
        + CASE
            WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 120 THEN 30
            WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 180 THEN 20
            WHEN DATE_DIFF(CURRENT_DATE(), a.last_monetizable_action_date, DAY) <= 365 THEN 10
            ELSE 0
        END
        -- Product density at peak (0-15 points)
        + CASE
            WHEN peak.max_products >= 3 THEN 15
            WHEN peak.max_products = 2 THEN 10
            WHEN peak.max_products = 1 THEN 5
            ELSE 0
        END
        -- Space Center tier loyalty signal (0-15 points)
        + CASE
            WHEN ls.space_center_tier >= 3 THEN 15
            WHEN ls.space_center_tier = 2 THEN 10
            WHEN ls.space_center_tier = 1 THEN 5
            ELSE 0
        END
    ) AS reactivation_score,

    -- Market context
    mkt.market_condition,

    -- Previous LTV signal
    hist.total_historical_revenue

FROM growth.user_lifecycle_stage ls
JOIN `project.dataset.user_activity_signals` a ON ls.user_id = a.user_id
LEFT JOIN (
    SELECT user_id, MAX(products_with_fm) AS max_products
    FROM growth.user_daily_snapshot
    GROUP BY user_id
) peak ON ls.user_id = peak.user_id
LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.market_condition_daily` mkt ON mkt.date = CURRENT_DATE()
LEFT JOIN (
    SELECT user_id, SUM(total_revenue) AS total_historical_revenue
    FROM growth.monthly_revenue
    GROUP BY user_id
) hist ON ls.user_id = hist.user_id
WHERE ls.lifecycle_stage IN ('DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE', 'DORMANT_ZERO', 'CHURNED')
```

---

### View 9: cross_product_adoption

**Purpose:** Product density per user, cross-sell funnels, product combination analysis.
**Priority:** P2
**SQL Complexity:** Medium
**Refresh:** Weekly

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.cross_product_adoption AS

WITH product_flags AS (
    SELECT
        user_id,
        MAX(CASE WHEN brokerage_revenue > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS has_brokerage,
        MAX(CASE WHEN earn_revenue > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS has_earn,
        MAX(CASE WHEN card_revenue > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS has_card,
        MAX(CASE WHEN loan_revenue > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS has_loan,
        MAX(CASE WHEN staking_revenue > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS has_staking,
        MAX(CASE WHEN launchpad_revenue > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS has_launchpad
    FROM growth.monthly_revenue
    GROUP BY user_id
)
SELECT
    ls.lifecycle_stage,
    ls.geography,

    COUNT(DISTINCT pf.user_id) AS total_users,

    -- Density distribution
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN (has_brokerage + has_earn + has_card + has_loan + has_staking + has_launchpad) = 1
        THEN pf.user_id END) AS single_product,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN (has_brokerage + has_earn + has_card + has_loan + has_staking + has_launchpad) = 2
        THEN pf.user_id END) AS two_products,
    COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN (has_brokerage + has_earn + has_card + has_loan + has_staking + has_launchpad) >= 3
        THEN pf.user_id END) AS three_plus_products,

    -- Product penetration rates
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(has_brokerage), COUNT(DISTINCT pf.user_id)) AS brokerage_penetration,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(has_earn), COUNT(DISTINCT pf.user_id)) AS earn_penetration,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(has_card), COUNT(DISTINCT pf.user_id)) AS card_penetration,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(has_loan), COUNT(DISTINCT pf.user_id)) AS loan_penetration,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(has_staking), COUNT(DISTINCT pf.user_id)) AS staking_penetration,

    -- Top combinations
    CONCAT(
        CASE WHEN has_brokerage = 1 THEN 'B' ELSE '' END,
        CASE WHEN has_earn = 1 THEN 'E' ELSE '' END,
        CASE WHEN has_card = 1 THEN 'C' ELSE '' END,
        CASE WHEN has_loan = 1 THEN 'L' ELSE '' END,
        CASE WHEN has_staking = 1 THEN 'S' ELSE '' END
    ) AS product_combination

FROM growth.user_lifecycle_stage ls
JOIN product_flags pf ON ls.user_id = pf.user_id
GROUP BY 1, 2, product_combination
```

---

### View 10: cohort_revenue_curves

**Purpose:** Revenue by cohort x channel x month. Powers LTV calculation and cohort comparison.
**Priority:** P2
**SQL Complexity:** High
**Refresh:** Weekly

```sql
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW growth.cohort_revenue_curves AS

SELECT
    DATE_TRUNC(fm.fm_date, MONTH) AS fm_cohort_month,
    fm.acquisition_channel,
    fm.geography,
    fm.fm_product AS first_product,
    mkt.market_condition AS market_at_acquisition,

    -- Cohort size
    COUNT(DISTINCT fm.user_id) AS cohort_size,

    -- Month-by-month performance
    DATE_DIFF(mr.revenue_month, DATE_TRUNC(fm.fm_date, MONTH), MONTH) AS months_since_fm,
    COUNT(DISTINCT mr.user_id) AS surviving_users,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(COUNT(DISTINCT mr.user_id), COUNT(DISTINCT fm.user_id)) AS survival_rate,
    SUM(mr.total_revenue) AS total_revenue,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(mr.total_revenue), COUNT(DISTINCT mr.user_id)) AS arpu_surviving,
    SAFE_DIVIDE(SUM(mr.total_revenue), COUNT(DISTINCT fm.user_id)) AS ltv_contribution,

    -- Revenue mix
    SUM(mr.recurring_revenue) AS recurring_revenue,
    SUM(mr.transactional_revenue) AS transactional_revenue,

    -- Product density at month t
    AVG(mr.products_generating_revenue) AS avg_product_density

FROM growth.user_fm fm
JOIN growth.monthly_revenue mr
    ON fm.user_id = mr.user_id
    AND mr.revenue_month >= DATE_TRUNC(fm.fm_date, MONTH)
LEFT JOIN `project.dataset.market_condition_daily` mkt
    ON mkt.date = fm.fm_date
GROUP BY 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 7
```

---

## 8.3 New Tables to Create

These are not views (computed from existing data) but new tables that must be created and populated.

### Table: state_transition_history

**Purpose:** Track every lifecycle stage transition. Required for REACTIVATED classifier and Sankey flows.
**Priority:** P0
**Population method:** Daily scheduled query comparing today's snapshot to yesterday's.

```sql
CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.state_transition_history` (
    user_id STRING,
    transition_date DATE,
    from_stage STRING,
    to_stage STRING,
    trigger_event STRING,       -- Enriched in post-processing
    market_condition STRING,
    days_in_previous_stage INT64
)
PARTITION BY transition_date
CLUSTER BY from_stage, to_stage;

-- Daily population query
INSERT INTO `project.dataset.state_transition_history`
SELECT
    t.user_id,
    t.snapshot_date AS transition_date,
    y.lifecycle_stage AS from_stage,
    t.lifecycle_stage AS to_stage,
    NULL AS trigger_event,
    t.market_condition,
    DATE_DIFF(t.snapshot_date, (
        SELECT MAX(sth.transition_date)
        FROM `project.dataset.state_transition_history` sth
        WHERE sth.user_id = t.user_id AND sth.to_stage = y.lifecycle_stage
    ), DAY) AS days_in_previous_stage
FROM growth.user_daily_snapshot t
JOIN growth.user_daily_snapshot y
    ON t.user_id = y.user_id
    AND y.snapshot_date = DATE_SUB(t.snapshot_date, INTERVAL 1 DAY)
WHERE t.lifecycle_stage != y.lifecycle_stage
  AND t.snapshot_date = CURRENT_DATE()
```

### Table: reactivation_events

**Purpose:** Dedicated reactivation event log (Chunk 1 v1.1 spec). Append-only.
**Priority:** P1

```sql
CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.reactivation_events` (
    user_id STRING,
    reactivation_date DATE,
    previous_status STRING,
    days_dormant INT64,
    reactivation_trigger STRING,      -- 'campaign_email', 'campaign_push', 'organic_market', 'organic_self', 'paid_retargeting'
    reactivation_campaign_id STRING,  -- NULL if organic
    reactivation_product STRING,
    reactivation_revenue_30d FLOAT64, -- Populated 30 days after event
    balance_at_reactivation FLOAT64,
    market_condition_at_reactivation STRING
)
PARTITION BY reactivation_date;

-- Populated from state_transition_history where to_stage = 'REACTIVATED'
```

### Table: market_condition_daily

**Purpose:** Daily market condition flag based on BTC 30-day return (Chunk 1 v1.1 thresholds).
**Priority:** P0

```sql
CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.market_condition_daily` (
    date DATE,
    btc_price_usd FLOAT64,
    btc_30d_return FLOAT64,
    btc_7d_volatility FLOAT64,
    market_condition STRING,    -- BULL, NEUTRAL, BEAR
    volatility_flag STRING      -- HIGH, NORMAL, LOW
);

-- Daily population (requires BTC price feed)
INSERT INTO `project.dataset.market_condition_daily`
SELECT
    CURRENT_DATE() AS date,
    btc_price AS btc_price_usd,
    (btc_price - btc_price_30d_ago) / btc_price_30d_ago AS btc_30d_return,
    btc_7d_vol AS btc_7d_volatility,
    CASE
        WHEN (btc_price - btc_price_30d_ago) / btc_price_30d_ago > 0.15 THEN 'BULL'
        WHEN (btc_price - btc_price_30d_ago) / btc_price_30d_ago < -0.15 THEN 'BEAR'
        ELSE 'NEUTRAL'
    END AS market_condition,
    CASE
        WHEN btc_7d_vol > 0.05 THEN 'HIGH'
        WHEN btc_7d_vol < 0.02 THEN 'LOW'
        ELSE 'NORMAL'
    END AS volatility_flag
FROM `project.dataset.btc_price_daily`  -- TBD: source for BTC price feed
WHERE date = CURRENT_DATE()
```

### Table: ab_tests + ab_test_enrollments

**Purpose:** Test tracking infrastructure for View 7.
**Priority:** P1

```sql
CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.ab_tests` (
    test_id STRING,
    test_name STRING,
    hypothesis STRING,
    start_date DATE,
    end_date DATE,
    status STRING,               -- building, running, reading, shipped, killed, iterating
    primary_metric STRING,
    secondary_metrics ARRAY<STRING>,
    guardrail_metric STRING,
    guardrail_threshold FLOAT64,
    segment_targeted STRING,
    sample_pct FLOAT64,
    ice_score INT64,
    owner STRING,
    created_at TIMESTAMP
);

CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.ab_test_enrollments` (
    test_id STRING,
    user_id STRING,
    variant STRING,              -- control, treatment_a, treatment_b
    enrolled_date DATE,
    converted BOOL,
    conversion_date DATE,
    revenue_attributed FLOAT64,
    primary_metric_value FLOAT64
)
PARTITION BY enrolled_date
CLUSTER BY test_id, variant;
```

### Table: unified_clusters

**Purpose:** Unify Salvia's per-product clusters into one table for cross-product analysis.
**Priority:** P0

```sql
CREATE TABLE `project.dataset.unified_clusters` (
    user_id STRING,
    brokerage_cluster STRING,     -- C0-C9
    pro_cluster STRING,
    earn_cluster STRING,
    card_cluster STRING,
    loan_cluster STRING,
    staking_cluster STRING,
    cluster_updated_at DATE
);

-- Populated by joining per-product cluster tables (Qlik Clusters per Product)
```

## 8.5 Automation Stack

### Architecture

```
┌───────────────┐     ┌──────────────┐     ┌────────────────┐
│   BigQuery     │────▶│ Looker Studio │────▶│   Council /     │
│  (source of    │     │ (dashboards)  │     │   Flash Report  │
│   truth)       │     └──────────────┘     └────────────────┘
└───────┬────────┘              │
        │                      │
        ▼                      ▼
┌───────────────┐     ┌──────────────┐
│ Scheduled      │     │ Connected    │
│ Queries        │     │ Sheets       │
│ (daily/weekly) │     │ (ad-hoc)     │
└───────┬────────┘     └──────────────┘
        │
        ▼
┌───────────────┐     ┌──────────────┐
│ Alert Pipeline │────▶│    Slack      │
│ (anomaly       │     │ #growth-alerts│
│  detection)    │     └──────────────┘
└───────────────┘
```

### Scheduled Queries

| Query | Frequency | Time | Priority |
|-------|-----------|------|----------|
| user_lifecycle_stage (View 1) | Daily | 06:00 UTC | P0 |
| user_daily_snapshot (View 2) | Daily | 06:30 UTC (after View 1) | P0 |
| state_transition_history | Daily | 07:00 UTC (after View 2) | P0 |
| market_condition_daily | Daily | 05:00 UTC (before View 1) | P0 |
| monthly_thresholds (V0c) | Monthly | 1st of month, 08:00 UTC | P0 |
| activation_funnel (View 3) | Daily | 07:00 UTC | P0 |
| stage_distribution_weekly (View 4) | Weekly (Mon) | 08:00 UTC | P0 |
| stage_transitions_weekly (View 5) | Weekly (Mon) | 08:30 UTC | P1 |
| revenue_by_stage_product (View 6) | Weekly | 08:30 UTC | P1 |
| ab_test_results (View 7) | Daily | 07:30 UTC | P1 |
| reactivation_targets (View 8) | Weekly | 09:00 UTC | P1 |
| cross_product_adoption (View 9) | Weekly | 09:00 UTC | P2 |
| cohort_revenue_curves (View 10) | Weekly | 09:30 UTC | P2 |

### Alert Pipeline (Slack #growth-alerts)

| Alert | Trigger | Severity |
|-------|---------|----------|
| Scheduled query failure | Any scheduled query fails or timeout | Critical |
| MMU drop > 5% WoW | stage_distribution_weekly | High |
| AT_RISK population > 20% of ACTIVE | stage_distribution_weekly | High |
| CHURNED inflow > 2x baseline | stage_transitions_weekly | Medium |
| Net AUC Flow negative for 2+ weeks | AUC3 metric | Medium |
| DEPOSITED_ONLY > 5,000 users | View 1 count | Medium |
| Test running > 8 weeks without decision | View 7 | Low |
| Market condition change (NEUTRAL → BULL or BEAR) | market_condition_daily | Info |

### Looker Studio Dashboard Map

| Dashboard | Primary Source Views | Audience | Refresh |
|-----------|---------------------|----------|---------|
| **Flash Revenue Report** | Views 1, 4, 6, monthly_revenue | Daniel, Pablo | Weekly (auto-populated Mon AM) |
| **Council Report** | Views 1, 4, 6, 10, monthly_thresholds | Pablo, Leadership | Monthly |
| **Operational Dashboard** | Views 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 7, 8, 9 | Growth Team (Daniel, Patri, Katy, Miguel, Salvia) | Daily |
| **Cohort Analysis** | View 10, user_fm | Growth Team | Weekly |
| **Card Dashboard** | Card transaction data, View 1 | Growth + Card Product | Weekly |
| **AUC Tracker** | Balance snapshots, View 1 | Growth + Finance | Weekly |

### Target: Zero Manual Pulls

| Current State | Target State | Timeline |
|--------------|-------------|----------|
| Manual Qlik export → spreadsheet → email | Looker Studio auto-refresh, Slack alerts | 60 days |
| Daniel manually calculates MMU weekly | View 1 → Looker Studio widget | Week 3-4 |
| Patri manually checks test results | View 7 → Test Tracker dashboard tab | Month 2 |
| No cohort tracking | View 10 → Cohort dashboard | Month 2 |
| No lifecycle stage visibility | View 1 + View 4 → Population dashboard | Week 2 |

### Connected Sheets for Ad-Hoc Analysis

BigQuery → Connected Sheets (Google Sheets with live BigQuery connection). 25K row limit per sheet, acceptable for most analyses.

**Pre-built queries for Connected Sheets:**
1. DEPOSITED_ONLY population profile (Chunk 1 v1.1 deep dive SQL)
2. Reactivation target list with scores
3. AT_RISK user detail with health_score breakdown
4. Test enrollment audit (user overlap check)
5. Cross-product adoption detail by user

### Critical Path

```
T003 (BQ access)
  → T004 (JOIN tables) + T005 (clusters) + T006 (DCA) + T008 (BTC price)
    → T009 (market table) + T010 (user_fm) + T011 (monthly_revenue)
      → T012 (monthly_thresholds)
        → T013 (lifecycle classifier) ← THIS IS THE BOTTLENECK
          → T019 (daily snapshot) → T020 (populations) → T022 (Flash Report)
          → T016 (CleverTap segments) → T026 (holdout) → T027+ (tests)
```

**The single biggest blocker is T003 → T013.** If the BigQuery alignment sync happens in Week 1, and Data Team allocates 8-12 hours that week, the lifecycle classifier can be live by end of Week 2. Everything else flows from there.

---

## 10.7 Risk Register

| Risk | Impact | Probability | Mitigation |
|------|--------|-------------|-----------|
| Data Team bandwidth insufficient for P0 requests | All lifecycle reporting blocked | Medium | Scope P0 to minimum viable (D1-D4 only). Offer to write all SQL ourselves. |
| DCA table doesn't exist (D4 = negative) | DCA metrics, health_score component, Test #001 blocked | Medium | Use Brokerage recurring trades as proxy. Flag DCA as Month 2 data project. |
| Academy linking unreliable (D5 = negative) | Academy attribution gap persists. Learn & Earn ROI unquantifiable. | High | UTM-based fallback. Manual cohort matching by registration time + source. |
| BigQuery table names don't match our SQL | All views need rewriting | High | This is why T003 (alignment sync) is the first task. Budget 2 days for SQL adaptation. |
| Pablo changes FM definition after validation | Cascade change through all 4 chunks | Low | Modular design: FM is defined in one view (V0a). Change propagates automatically. |
| Market enters deep bear during Month 1-2 | Lower test velocity, smaller populations, harder to measure lifts | Medium | Group Sequential testing for small pops. Focus on DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE reactivation. |
| CleverTap segment limits or event gaps | Cannot target lifecycle stages for tests | Medium | D11 (CleverTap audit) is P1 Week 3. Identify gaps early. |
| Salvia's clusters change methodology | Unified cluster table invalidated | Low | Regular sync (T018). Cluster table includes updated_at field. |

## FILE: mega-prompt-v2.1-final.md

# MEGA-PROMPT v2: Building the Growth Operating System for Bit2Me from Scratch

**Version:** 2.1 — Definitive
**Purpose:** This prompt builds the entire growth machine from zero. No legacy assumptions. Every definition, model, metric, formula, framework, and system is created here.

**Organizational mandate from COO (Pablo Campos, verbatim):** "1º tener control de todo, plan de trabajo, los primeros A+B y entonces sumamos fuerzas de forma organizada." Translation: Control first → Plan → First A/B tests → Then scale team. He wants a structured backlog (Jira or folder). This prompt builds the foundation BEFORE execution.

---

## ROLE

You are the new Head of Growth at Bit2Me. Day one. Clean slate.

You think in unit economics, not vanity metrics. You build systems, not slides. Every definition must be SQL-translatable. Every metric must answer "what do we do next?" Every number must survive being challenged by a COO who thinks in revenue.

You combine the analytical rigor of a data scientist, the strategic thinking of a Reforge-trained growth leader, the behavioral economics depth of a BJ Fogg / Nir Eyal practitioner, and the operational pragmatism of someone who has built growth engines at Coinbase, Revolut, or Nubank.

---

## COMPANY CONTEXT

### Identity
**Bit2Me** is a regulated Spanish cryptocurrency exchange founded in 2014.

- **Regulation:** First Spanish-origin fintech with MiCA CASP license from CNMV. Registered with Banco de España. Triple ISO compliance (37301, 37001, UNE 19601). ISO 27001 + 22301. €150M crypto insurance via Ledger.
- **Users:** ~1.8M registered. ~85K with balance. ~50K active with value (Spain only).
- **Markets:** Spain (primary, mature), Portugal (growing), EU (new markets: IT, FR, DE, NL), LATAM/RoW (Argentina, Peru; inflation-hedging use case).
- **Segments:** B2C (retail) and B2B (institutional/corporate).
- **Investors:** Telefónica Ventures, Investcorp, Ledger Enterprise, Tether Ventures (€30M round, Aug 2025).
- **Reports to:** COO Pablo Campos.
- **Growth team:** Maxim (analyst, arriving), Patri Gargallo (operations, executing campaigns), Katy + Miguel (CRM/CleverTap specialists).
- **Coordinators:** Salvia/S. Rut (lifecycle product owner, clusters, segmentation), Consuelo Morcillo (paid acquisition), Rut (Space Center).
- **Data team:** David Sales (lead), Álvaro Durán (Earn/Loan data), Juan Fornell (Brokerage clusters).
- **Pablo's plan for team expansion:** First get control + plan + first A/B tests working. Then bring in Katy and Miguel in an organized way. Do NOT scale team before having structure.

### Products (13 B2C + B2B services)

| # | Product | Revenue Model | Revenue Type | Current State |
|---|---------|---------------|--------------|---------------|
| 1 | **Wallet/Brokerage** | Commission on spread at trade execution | One-time per tx | Primary driver (~52% revenue). Simple buy/sell. |
| 2 | **PRO Trading** | Maker/taker fees (0%-0.60% by 30d volume) | One-time per tx | Advanced platform. Fees cut 95% Jan 2025. |
| 3 | **Earn** | Yield spread (platform takes % of protocol yield) | Recurring (daily/weekly accrual) | +€5.2M volume. 82% BTC. €1.02M stablecoins. No minimum. |
| 4 | **Staking (Native)** | Protocol reward commission | Recurring | Extension of Earn. ETH, ADA, SOL, DOT. Unbonding periods. |
| 5 | **Card (Mastercard)** | Interchange (EU 0.2% cap) + FX markup | Recurring per tx | 0.26% penetration (vs 42-48% industry). 29% monthly churn. ~4,600 annual active. €53 ARPU. |
| 6 | **Loans** | Interest on crypto-collateralized loans | Recurring (interest) + event (liquidation) | +202% revenue growth. €54K from liquidations. 90.91% Loan Whales from Brokerage C8. |
| 7 | **OTC** | Spread on large-volume trades | One-time per tx | Institutional/HNWI. Account manager. KYB/enhanced KYC. |
| 8 | **API** | Revenue share / volume-based | Recurring | B2B pure. 82% institutional volume is API-driven (Coinbase benchmark). |
| 9 | **Launchpad** | Token sale participation fees | Event-driven | B2M holder priority. FOMO + engagement lever. |
| 10 | **Commerce** | Payment gateway fees | Per tx | Merchant crypto acceptance. |
| 11 | **Academy** | Free (top-of-funnel) | None (conversion funnel) | +3M students. 50% LATAM. Web3MBA advanced. NO Learn & Earn yet (major gap vs Coinbase, Binance, OKX). |
| 12 | **Tax** | Tool fees (discount by B2M held) | Seasonal | Tax reporting. Seasonal spike Q1-Q2. |
| 13 | **Travel (Bit2Me Life)** | Commission on bookings | Per booking | +1M hotels via Entravel. 4% discount with Card. |

**Revenue Quality Classification:**
- **Transactional (one-time):** Brokerage, Pro, OTC, Commerce. Revenue only when user acts.
- **Recurring (passive):** Earn, Staking, Loans (interest), Card (interchange). Revenue generated while user is "inactive."
- **Event-driven:** Launchpad, Liquidations, Tax.

This distinction is CRITICAL because a user with €50K in Earn who never logs in generates more recurring revenue than an active Brokerage user trading €200/month. Traditional "active/inactive" classifications break here.

### Space Center (Loyalty/Tier System)

The B2M token is the ecosystem glue. This is the Bit2Me equivalent of Binance's BNB or Crypto.com's CRO.

| Benefit | How B2M Connects It |
|---------|---------------------|
| Wallet bonus | Up to 100% with higher B2M tier |
| Earn APY boost | Up to +50% APY at higher tiers |
| Pro fee discount | 25-50% reduction |
| Card cashback | Up to 7% in B2M |
| Launchpad priority | Higher tier = earlier/larger allocation |
| Tax discount | By B2M held |
| Travel discount | 4% with Card |

**Tier climbing = multi-product lock-in.** Every tier upgrade makes every product more attractive. Each B2M staked increases switching cost. This creates the retention moat.

**Key question for this framework:** How do Space Center tiers map to lifecycle stages? Does tier = lifecycle proxy?

### Current Data Infrastructure

**CRM (CleverTap):**
- Has Brokerage + Wallet events.
- Has events and attributes per product (confirmed by Patri: "teniendo en cuenta los eventos y atributos que tenemos de cada producto").
- Specific coverage per product still needs validation (what events exist for Pro, Earn, Loan, Card, Staking, Space Center).

**Qlik Dashboards (confirmed available):**
- **Acquisition Dashboard:** Registration, verification funnels. Daily refresh.
- **Transaction Attribution:** Revenue by channel (AI, Brand, CRM, Direct, Paid), by product, by region, by B2C/B2B. This is the core attribution engine. Daily.
- **Revenue Report per Product:** Revenue by product. Daily.
- **Geo Report:** Revenue/registrations by country/region. Daily.
- **User Segment:** B2C vs. B2B tagging. Daily.
- **Onboarding:** Registration → verification flow.
- **Activation / First Monetization Report:** First purchase tracking (Brokerage only currently).
- **Churn Analysis:** K-Means clustering. Previously Brokerage-only, but...
- **Clusters by Product:** NOW exist per product (new development). Each product has its own cluster analysis. Need to be unified into a single user-level table.

**BigQuery:** Available. Views need to be built. Growth team needs read access.

**Clusters (Per Product, Current State):**
- **Brokerage:** 10 K-Means clusters → 4 segments (High Value C8, Smart Holders C6/C7, Mass Retail C0/C4/C9/C1, Descartes/Inactivos C2/C3/C5). 81,463 users B2C.
- **Pro, Earn, Card, Loan, Staking:** Clusters now exist per product (details TBD; need to pull structure from Salvia/Data team).
- **Critical next step:** Unify clusters into single table: `user_id, brokerage_cluster, pro_cluster, earn_cluster, card_cluster, loan_cluster`. This unlocks "Silent Whale" detection (user "Inactive" in Brokerage but "Active" in Earn).

**Key data JOINs needed (identified, pending):**
- JOIN LC table with Transaction Attribution: gives `user_id, first_mon_date, total_trades, trades_30d, revenue_30d, revenue_total, last_trade_date, products_traded`
- This unlocks: real MMU, ARPMMU, retention cohorts, multi-product detection.

**8 P0 Computed Events (defined, pending Data team implementation):**
1. Idle_EUR: Deposited EUR, hasn't bought in X days
2. Deposit_No_Purchase: Deposit made, no trade within 48h
3. First_No_Second: First trade done, no second within 14d
4. Earn_Abandoned: Started Earn flow, didn't deposit
5. Loan_Abandoned: Started Loan simulation, didn't originate
6. Pro_No_Trade: Visited Pro, no trade placed
7. Mission_Incomplete: Started Space Center mission, didn't finish
8. Churn_Risk: Health score dropped below threshold

### Revenue Attribution (Current State, YTD Feb 2026)
- AI: €598K (49%), Brand: €262K (21%), CRM: €240K (20%), Direct: €77K (6%), Paid: €17K (1.4%)
- Total YTD: ~€1.22M
- FM vs LC split: €486K FM, €11.6M LC (all-time)
- Push attribution window: 7 days. Other channels: not documented.
- Problem: 7-day window likely UNDERREPORTS Paid and OVERREPORTS CRM for longer consideration journeys.

### Known Population Data (Spain, Feb 2026)
- L0 (Unverified): 213,863 (49.1%)
- L1 (Verified, no monetization): 29,010 (6.7%)
- L2 (First monetization, no retention): 36,866 (8.5%)
- L3 (Active with value): 50,416 (11.6%)
- L4 (Dormant with value): 4,414 (1.0%)
- L5 (Churned): 101,029 (23.2%)
- Total Spain: 435,598
- Key: 72% generate zero revenue (49% unverified + 23% churned). Only 11.6% active with value.

Weekly flows (approximate): New→L0: ~1,400/wk. L0→L1: ~850/wk. L1→L2: ~610/wk. L2→L3, L3→L4, L3→L5, L4→L3, L5→reactivation: unknown.

---

## THE BUILD: 10 PHASES

Each phase feeds the next. The order is non-negotiable. You cannot build Phase 3 without Phase 1.

---

### PHASE 1: FOUNDATIONAL DEFINITIONS (The Language)

Every term gets one definition. No ambiguity. Every definition must be SQL-translatable.

**1.1 The "First Monetization" Decision**

This is the single most consequential definition in the entire system. It cascades into CAC, LTV, lifecycle stages, activation metrics, and Council reporting.

**LIVE DEBATE (Feb 2026):** This is actively being discussed by the team right now.

Pablo Campos (COO) raised these exact questions:
- "el FM (First Monetization, que es como decidió Data llamarle), lo veo incierto a día de hoy."
- "¿Cómo se calcula?"
- "¿Por qué se calcula así?"
- "¿Se calcula igual en el agregado que en cada producto?"
- "¿Se calcula igual según el canal de adquisición?"
- "hay fórmulas matemáticas para eso tb que pueden ayudar"

S. Rut (lifecycle product owner) reframed it correctly:
- "Entiendo que no es primera compra lo que hay que definir, sino el momento de activación."
- "Para cada producto habría un momento de activación, que entiendo que es la primera 'operación'."
- "En referidos sería que trae el primer referido."
- "¿Habría que tener definido el momento de 'activación' y de 'dormido' de cada producto?"
- "Esto nos permitirá iterar sobre el momento de impactar a los usuarios para cada producto."

S. Rut is correct. The answer to ALL of these questions must come from this framework.

There are (at minimum) 6 candidate definitions. Evaluate each:

| Candidate | Definition | Strength | Weakness |
|-----------|-----------|----------|----------|
| First Revenue Event (FRE) | First time exchange captures any revenue from user | Precise | Treats €0.01 spread same as €100 fee |
| First Completed Trade (FCT) | First buy/sell execution | Simple, industry standard | Brokerage-only; ignores Earn/Card/Loan |
| First Deposit (FD) | First fiat/crypto deposit | High-intent leading indicator | Generates zero direct revenue |
| First Economically Meaningful Action (EMA) | First revenue-generating action above threshold (trade >€10, fee >€0.50, Earn deposit >€100) | Cross-product, filters noise | Requires threshold calibration |
| First Value Exchange (FVE) | First bilateral value creation (user gets value AND platform earns) | Philosophically sound | Hard to operationalize |
| First Qualified Monetization (FQM) | First action with statistically significant correlation to 90-day retention | Most predictive | Requires 12+ months cohort data |

**Deliver:**
- Recommendation: which definition is the North Star? (Research suggests EMA with product-level variants)
- Product-level FM definitions: What counts as FM for Brokerage? Pro? Earn? Card? Loan? Staking?
- Threshold calibration methodology
- Edge cases: dust transactions, free crypto from promotions, card-before-trade users, users who deposit but never trade
- Anti-gaming safeguards
- How this definition cascades into CAC, LTV, activation rate

**1.2 User Status Definitions (SQL-level)**

Mutually exclusive, collectively exhaustive. Every user falls into exactly one status at any point in time.

| Status | SQL Logic (pseudocode) | Notes |
|--------|----------------------|-------|
| REGISTERED_ONLY | has_account=TRUE AND kyc NOT approved AND trades=0 | |
| KYC_COMPLETE | kyc=approved AND deposits=0 AND trades=0 | |
| DEPOSITED_ONLY | deposits>0 AND trades=0 AND earn_deposits=0 | |
| FIRST_MONETIZATION | (has FM event) AND days_since_FM<=30 | Per the FM definition chosen above |
| ACTIVE | [DEFINE across ALL products] | This is the hard one. See 1.3. |
| AT_RISK | Was ACTIVE, activity_decline_4w>=50% OR health_score<30 | |
| DORMANT_WITH_BALANCE | days_since_activity>90 AND balance>0 | 5-10x higher reactivation probability than zero-balance |
| DORMANT_ZERO | days_since_activity>90 AND balance=0 | |
| CHURNED | days_since_activity>180 AND balance=0 AND no_login_180d | |

**1.3 The "Active" Definition Problem**

This is the second most consequential definition. It determines TAU (Total Active Users), the number Pablo sees every week.

The problem: In crypto, "active" is not just "logged in" or "traded." Consider:
- User A: Trades €500/month on Brokerage. Clearly active.
- User B: Has €50K in Earn, never logs in. Generates €200/month in yield commission for Bit2Me. Is this user "active"?
- User C: Uses Card 20x/month, never trades. €4 interchange/month. Active?
- User D: Logged in 15 times this month, checked prices, traded zero. Active?

**Deliver:**
- A multi-product "active" definition that accounts for ALL revenue-generating behaviors
- The concept of "Behaviorally Active" vs. "Economically Active" and whether they should be separate metrics
- Monthly Monetized Users (MMU) as potential North Star: unique users generating >€1 revenue in a calendar month through any combination of products
- How this compares to Coinbase's MTU (Monthly Transacting Users)

**1.4 Churn Definitions (Three Horizons + Market Adjustment)**

| Horizon | Definition | Action | Market Adjustment |
|---------|-----------|--------|-------------------|
| Soft (30d) | No monetizable action in 30 days | Early warning. Trigger AT_RISK. | During bear market, extend to 45 days? |
| Hard (90d) | No monetizable action in 90 days AND no login in 60 days | Primary churn metric for reporting. | During bear market, extend to 120 days? |
| Dead (180d) | No activity 180 days, zero balance, no login | Write-off. | No adjustment. |

**Critical crypto-specific challenge:** Retention swings 6x between bull and bear markets (D30: 18% bull vs. 2-3% bear). A user inactive for 90 days during a bear market is NOT the same as 90 days during a bull run.

**Deliver:**
- Should churn windows adjust based on market conditions? If yes, how? If no, why not?
- How to separate "market-cycle dormancy" (will return when market recovers) from "true churn" (gone forever)
- The role of balance as a churn modifier: user with balance = likely dormant, not churned
- Churn by product: different windows for different products? (Pro trader inactive 30d = concerning. Earn depositor inactive 30d = normal.)
- Churn prediction signals (ranked by predictive power): days since last tx, trading frequency decline WoW, portfolio balance trajectory, deposit/withdrawal ratio, products used count, market conditions, staking engagement, support ticket frequency

**1.5 Revenue Type Definitions**

| Type | Definition | Why It Matters |
|------|-----------|----------------|
| FM Revenue | Revenue from users whose first monetization occurs in the period | Measures acquisition quality |
| LC Revenue | Revenue from users previously monetized | Measures retention/expansion |
| Transactional Revenue | Revenue generated per user action (trade, OTC deal) | Volatile, market-dependent |
| Recurring Revenue | Revenue generated without user action (Earn yield, Loan interest, Card interchange) | Stable, counter-cyclical |
| Event Revenue | Revenue from discrete events (Launchpad, liquidations) | Unpredictable |

**Deliver:**
- Why separating FM vs. LC is critical: it tells you if Paid acquires new users or re-monetizes existing ones
- Why separating Transactional vs. Recurring matters for valuation and forecasting
- How each revenue type behaves in bull vs. bear markets

**1.6 Activation AND Dormancy Definitions by Product**

S. Rut correctly identified: for each product, you need TWO definitions:
1. **Activation moment:** When is the user "activated" for this product?
2. **Dormancy moment:** When does the user become "dormant" for this product?

This allows precise timing of lifecycle campaigns per product: impact users BETWEEN activation and dormancy.

For each product, define:
- What is the "aha moment"? (The behavior after which retention materially improves)
- What counts as "activated" for this product?
- What counts as "dormant" for this product?
- Time window for activation
- Time window for dormancy (different per product; Pro trader inactive 30d is concerning, Earn depositor inactive 30d is normal)
- Activation rate benchmark (industry)
- For Referrals specifically: activation = first successful referral (not just sharing a link)

| Product | Proposed Activation | Aha Moment | Time Window |
|---------|-------------------|------------|-------------|
| Brokerage | First trade + second trade within 14d | Seeing portfolio value increase | 14 days |
| Pro | First limit order or 3+ trades | Executing a profitable limit order | 7 days |
| Earn | First deposit into yield product >€50 | Seeing first yield accrual | 30 days |
| Card | Card activation + 3rd transaction | Seeing cashback in B2M | 30 days |
| Loan | Loan originated | Receiving EUR without selling crypto | 7 days |
| Staking | First stake + seeing first reward | Seeing protocol reward | 30 days |

**Deliver:**
- Validated activation definitions per product with reasoning
- Research on crypto-specific "aha moments" (is it first profit? First portfolio view? First recurring buy setup?)
- Time-to-activation benchmarks by product
- How to measure: the user who activated on Brokerage in 2 days vs. 28 days. Same "activated" status, different quality.

**1.7 Canonical Dimensions (The Matrix)**

Every metric in the system must be cuttable by these dimensions. Even if a cell is empty, the dimension must exist.

- **Time:** Week, Month, Quarter, YTD, WoW delta, MoM delta
- **Geography:** ES, PT, EU (IT, FR, DE, NL), LATAM (AR, PE), RoW
- **Segment:** B2C, B2B
- **Channel:** Paid, Organic, Referral, Partners, CRM, Direct, AI, Academy
- **Sub-channel:** Google Search Brand, Google Search Non-Brand, Meta, Display, Affiliates, etc.
- **Product:** Brokerage, Pro, Earn, Staking, Card, Loan, OTC, API
- **Revenue Type:** FM, LC, Transactional, Recurring, Event
- **Cohort:** Registration cohort, FM cohort, Revenue cohort, Acquisition channel cohort
- **Lifecycle Stage:** Per the lifecycle model defined in Phase 2
- **Archetype:** Per the user archetypes defined in Phase 2
- **Market Condition:** Bull, Neutral, Bear (derived from BTC 30d trend + volatility)
- **Space Center Tier:** Tier level at time of action

---

### PHASE 2: USER MODEL (Who Are We Serving?)

**2.1 User Archetypes**

Define (minimum) 10 distinct archetypes. For each:

1. Name and 2-3 sentence description
2. Demographics: age, income, geography, tech literacy
3. Psychographics: values, risk tolerance, information consumption
4. Primary motivation for crypto entry
5. Products they gravitate toward (primary, secondary, aspirational)
6. Behavioral signature: first 30/60/90 day pattern
7. Revenue profile: expected LTV range, monetization path
8. Churn risk profile: what makes them leave, warning signals, timeline
9. SQL classification logic (rules-based, using available signals)
10. Bull vs. bear market behavior shift

**Known archetypes from research (validate and expand):**
- Curious Novice (first-time, €50-200, high churn 60-70%)
- Millennial Investor (portfolio diversifier, €300-1,500 LTV)
- DeFi Refugee (technically sophisticated, comparing to DEXs)
- Inflation Hedger (LATAM-specific, stablecoin-first)
- Yield Seeker (stablecoin deposit, comparing APYs cross-platform)
- Pro Trader (5+ trades/month, platform-promiscuous)
- Regulation-First Conservative (chose Bit2Me for MiCA/BdE)
- Social/Peer-Pressure Entrant (meme coins, lottery ticket mentality)
- The Whale (€50K+ balance, personal service expectations)
- Academy Student (zero CAC channel, needs product bridge)
- Dormant Asset Holder (balance >€100, 90-365d inactive)
- B2B Corporate (KYB, multi-user, API-first)

**Deliver:**
- Complete archetype catalog with all 10 fields per archetype
- Master SQL classifier (CASE WHEN hierarchy)
- Archetype distribution matrix: bull vs. bear, new vs. existing, by geo, by revenue contribution
- Archetype evolution paths: which converts to which, what triggers evolution
- How to classify users who don't fit cleanly (the UNCLASSIFIED bucket)

**2.2 Multi-Geo User Differences**

The lifecycle of a Spanish user is different from an Argentine user. Define how.

| Dimension | Spain | LATAM (AR, PE) | New EU (IT, FR, DE) |
|-----------|-------|----------------|---------------------|
| Primary motivation | Investment/speculation | Inflation hedging, remittance | Diversification |
| First asset | BTC/ETH | USDT/USDC | BTC/ETH |
| Activation pattern | Standard | Faster (urgency) | Slower (cautious) |
| Product affinity | Brokerage → Earn → Card | Brokerage → Earn (stablecoin) | Brokerage → DCA |
| Regulatory experience | Familiar (MiCA) | Less regulated environment | Variable (some MiCA, some not) |
| Churn triggers | Fee comparison, bear market | Platform stability concerns, FX | Competitor entry, better UX |
| Conversion rate benchmark | 45% reg-to-FM | Higher (urgency) | 20-25% |

**Deliver:** Geo-specific lifecycle adjustments, activation targets, and churn definitions.

---

### PHASE 3: LIFECYCLE MODEL (The Architecture)

**Decision already validated: Hybrid model.** One global user lifecycle overlaid with per-product adoption tracking. This is what Coinbase, Binance, Crypto.com, Nubank, and Revolut converge on.

**3.1 Global User Lifecycle**

Design lifecycle stages that are:
- **Non-linear** (users can regress, reactivate, skip stages)
- **Revenue-aligned** (each stage maps to a revenue behavior)
- **SQL-classifiable** (no manual tagging, computed from data)
- **Product-agnostic** at the global level
- **Market-cycle aware** (accounts for bull/bear dormancy patterns)

For each stage, define:
- Name and precise definition
- Entry criteria (what moves the user INTO this stage?)
- Exit criteria (what moves the user OUT?)
- Regression criteria (what moves the user BACKWARD?)
- Population estimate (known data)
- Revenue contribution (estimated)
- Target interventions (what does Growth DO for users in this stage?)
- Metrics that matter at this stage

**Address these hard design questions:**
- Is "Dormant with Balance" one stage or multiple? (Dormant 30d vs. 90d vs. 180d are very different.)
- How does "Active" handle the passive revenue problem? (€50K Earn user who never logs in)
- Where does "At-Risk" sit? Is it a stage or a flag overlaid on Active?
- Should there be a "Power User" or "Advocate" stage above Active?
- How do reactivated users re-enter? Same stage they left, or a special "Reactivated" stage with different churn expectations?

**3.2 Per-Product Lifecycle Overlays**

For each of the 6 core products (Brokerage, Pro, Earn, Card, Loan, Staking), define:

| Dimension | Brokerage | Pro | Earn | Card | Loan | Staking |
|-----------|-----------|-----|------|------|------|---------|
| Stages | Unaware→Aware→Tried→Active→Power→Churned | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... |
| Activation def | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... |
| Churn def | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... |
| "Aha moment" | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... |
| Time window | Daily/weekly | Daily | Monthly | Weekly | Per loan term | Monthly |
| Key metric | Tx/month, Volume | Volume, Maker% | AUC, Yield | Tx/month, Spend | Loans outstanding | Amount staked |

**3.3 Cross-Product Adoption Matrix**

Product density is the #1 predictor of retention and LTV.

| Products Used | Est. 12-Month Retention | LTV Multiplier | Implied Bit2Me LTV |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 product | 20-30% | 1.0x | ~€388 |
| 2 products | 45-55% | 1.8-2.5x | ~€700-€970 |
| 3 products | 65-75% | 3.0-4.0x | ~€1,164-€1,552 |
| 4+ products | 80-90% | 4.0-6.0x | ~€1,552-€2,328 |

**Deliver:**
- Complete cross-sell matrix: which product leads to which? With what probability?
- "Golden paths" by archetype/segment (Mass Retail, Smart Holders, High Value)
- Optimal timing between products (how many days after Brokerage activation should Earn be suggested?)
- Trigger signals for cross-sell readiness (balance thresholds, frequency, page views)
- The B2M Token flywheel: buy B2M for fee discounts → hold for Space Center → stake for yield → spend via Card → use for Launchpad
- **DCA as the retention bridge:** Brokerage (manual) → DCA (recurring) → Earn (yield on accumulated) is the highest-retention path for Mass Retail. A user with active DCA has 2-3x better D90 retention than manual-only traders (validate with Bit2Me data). DCA setup rate should be tracked as a leading retention indicator. DCA stop/cancel is one of the strongest churn signals (stronger than missing a single manual trade).

**3.4 B2B Lifecycle (Separate Model)**

B2B lifecycle is fundamentally different:
- Longer onboarding (KYB: weeks/months vs. KYC: minutes)
- Multi-user accounts (admin, trader, viewer roles)
- API-first vs. dashboard users
- Volume-based pricing, negotiated terms
- Relationship-managed (account manager)
- Different churn signals (API call frequency, not login frequency)
- Revenue profile: fewer users, much higher revenue per user

**Deliver:**
- Complete B2B lifecycle stages (Lead → KYB → Integration → First Trade → Ramp → Steady State → Expansion → At-Risk → Churned)
- B2B-specific activation and churn definitions
- B2B metrics separate from B2C
- How B2B feeds into Council reporting

**3.5 The Academy-to-Conversion Pipeline**

3M students. 50% LATAM. Zero CAC. No Learn & Earn.

This is potentially the highest-ROI acquisition channel Bit2Me has. It needs its own lifecycle path:
Academy Student → Registered (still learning) → KYC → First Purchase → Active User

**Deliver:**
- Academy lifecycle stages and conversion funnel
- Benchmarks: what conversion rate should Academy → Registration → FM achieve?
- The Learn & Earn gap: what competitors do, estimated ROI, implementation complexity
- How Academy users differ in lifecycle behavior from Paid/Organic users

**3.6 GTM Market Expansion Lifecycle (New Market Playbook)**

When Bit2Me enters a new market (PT done, IT/FR/DE/NL next), the lifecycle has a compressed, distinct pattern. Week 1 of a new market = acquisition. Week 2 = those same users are already in lifecycle. This happened live with Portugal: "la parte GTM es LC también, tenemos una BBDD de muchos usuarios de PT, y la semana que viene los usuarios de la 1ª semana ya estarán en LC."

GTM lifecycle is different because:
- Users arrive in a concentrated burst (campaign-driven, not organic trickle)
- No local brand awareness yet (higher trust barrier)
- Regulatory context may differ (MiCA coverage vs. local requirements)
- Product availability may be partial (not all products in all markets from day 1)
- Local competitors may already be entrenched (Bitpanda in AT/DE, Bitstamp in NL/UK)
- Conversion benchmarks are lower (20-25% new EU vs. 45% Spain)

**Deliver:**
- GTM lifecycle stages: Pre-launch DB build → Launch burst → Week 1-2 activation → Week 3-4 early lifecycle → Month 2+ steady state
- Metrics that matter in each GTM phase (registration velocity → KYC completion → FM rate → D30 retention → convergence with mature market benchmarks)
- When to transition a new market from "GTM mode" to "business as usual"
- How GTM cohorts should be tracked separately (they have different baseline behaviors than organic users in the same market)
- The Portugal playbook: what worked, what didn't, what to replicate for IT/FR/DE/NL
